## In progress - Forward trajectory rendering (flight-map + tracking-station)

**Goal:** render the FUTURE portion of a ghost's trajectory ahead of the icon, as one continuous chained line, stopping before the first full-loop closed orbit and at the first SOI change. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/forward-trajectory-render.md` (Option 1 - draw at the live production surfaces with a pure forward-window helper; not the Director-extension Option 2). Branch `claude/flight-map-trajectory-render-io6be0`.

**Built so far:** Step 1 pure `ForwardRenderWindow` (window/stop helpers, effective-segment-sourced, xUnit-covered), Step 2 shared `OrbitArcSampler` (extracted the arc-clip math out of `GhostOrbitArcPatch.UpdateSpline`, one copy), Step 3 forward draw folded into `Display/GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs` as a PURELY ADDITIVE pass: future legs (B') via `ShouldDrawForwardLeg`, future arcs (C) sampled into per-segment `VectorLine`s converted through `ScaledSpace.LocalToScaledSpace` (the ARC pipeline), keyed per recording by `(currentElementIndex, bodyName, reaimWindowIndex)`. The forward pass NEVER touches `drewNonOrbitalLegRecordings` (the CRITICAL ownership prerequisite, safest option (a)), so the current element + its proto-suppression contract are byte-identical to today and all three ownership consumers keep seeing "owns" iff the polyline draws the CURRENT element. CRITICAL re-aim sourcing via `GhostMapPresence.ResolveEffectiveMapOrbitSegments`; gap-hold honored via `ShadowRenderDriver.IsDirectorTracking`; below-surface descents fall to forward legs (FIX #27 cover); `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` reused so a fragmented coast does not split the chain.

**Reviewed (clean-context Opus, against the f5c56e733 diff):** verdict SHIP-READY modulo the in-game playtest; no confirmed bugs/regressions. Three low findings actioned: (1) added an in-game `OrbitArcSampler_ClipsLiveOrbitToOpenArc` test (`RuntimeTests.cs`, category `ForwardRender`) covering the live-Orbit sampler that xUnit cannot reach (elliptical open arc / hyperbolic / degenerate fall-through); (2) hoisted the per-cache-miss 180-element sampler buffer to a reusable `forwardArcSampleScratch` field (off the hot path, but no alloc on a cache miss now); (3) the `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` no-alloc by-reference fast path was confirmed caller-safe (all three callers read-only) and the read-only return contract was hardened in the doc comments on both the method and the `ChainAssembler` call site (a future mutation would corrupt recorded `OrbitSegments`). Confirmed the forward-arc `new Orbit(...)` needs no `Init()` (matches the shipped `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs:739` / `TrajectoryMath.cs:214` sites). Build 0 errors; 14810/14810 xUnit pass (InjectAllRecordings env-flake excluded).

**Playtest 1 (2026-06-09, log `logs/2026-06-09_2157_forward-render-playtest`):** the forward chain DID draw (`Forward arcs drawn count=1 legsDrawn=3` at 50x warp) and the window/stop logic was correct, but the maintainer found the past trail dropping off one element at a time distracting. **Requirement revised:** keep PAST segments on screen too - draw the whole RUN the icon is in (past + current + future), persistent as the icon advances, and reset the line only at a boundary (the icon entering a full-loop closed orbit, or an SOI change). This REVERSES the original "past stays gone" rule #1.

**Run-model rework (2026-06-09):** `ForwardRenderWindow` now computes a render run `[RunStartUT, StopUT]` - the forward walk is unchanged, plus a BACKWARD walk to the previous boundary (prior full-loop closed orbit's endUT / prior SOI boundary / -inf = data start) so earlier legs persist; `StopUT` is +inf at end-of-data so trailing legs persist. The icon-on-closed-orbit empty-run now fires only when the icon is BRACKETED by the ellipse (a gap-before ghost, e.g. on the ascent, still draws its backward run). The renderer feeds `RunStartUT` as the window start (past legs/arcs included), and `BuildForwardArcKey` now keys on the actual SELECTED segment set (+ re-aim window) instead of `currentElementIndex`, because with past arcs included the same index maps to different selections as the icon crosses element boundaries. Build 0 errors; 14814/14814 xUnit pass (InjectAllRecordings env-flake excluded; +4 run tests). Deployed for re-test.

**Reviewed (clean-context Opus, against the pre-rework f5c56e733 diff):** verdict SHIP-READY; no confirmed bugs/regressions. Three low findings actioned: (1) in-game `OrbitArcSampler_ClipsLiveOrbitToOpenArc` test; (2) hoisted the per-cache-miss sampler buffer to a reusable field; (3) hardened the `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` read-only return contract (all callers verified read-only). Confirmed the forward-arc `new Orbit(...)` needs no `Init()` (matches `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs:739` / `TrajectoryMath.cs:214`).

**Playtest 4 (2026-06-09, log `logs/2026-06-09_2253_forward-render-4`):** the launch polyline drew ALONE (no forward continuation), then vanished once the icon passed its end while the rest of the line up to the parking ellipse appeared. Log-confirmed root cause: the run was computed PER RECORDING, but the flight is a CHAIN (`chain=aff63064`, members `5d68d429` launch + `61e9177` rest). The launch member has ZERO OrbitSegments (`rebuiltOrbitSegments=0`), so `ComputeForwardWindow` returned no run while the icon rode it (`Render run` first appears only at the handoff, 22:52:08.953); post-handoff the next member's run (`runStart=-Infinity`) only reached its OWN legs, and the launch member's leg was head-UT-gated out (its sibling is renderHidden), so the ascent disappeared.

**Chain-boundary fix (2026-06-09):** the run pass is now CHAIN-AWARE. `CollectChainRunMembers` (pure, xUnit-covered) collects every committed member of the icon's chain StartUT-ordered; `DecideForwardWindowForRecording` computes the window over the CONCATENATED per-member effective segments (re-coalesced chain-wide so a same-orbit coast split across a member boundary still classifies as one full-loop stop) and enqueues run legs/arcs from EVERY member - refreshing hidden siblings' leg caches on demand, mirroring the walk's recording-level static gates for them, keying each member's forward-arc cache on its own selected set + re-aim window. Decided ONCE per chain per frame (per-frame `chainRunProcessedThisFrame` dedupe; the first non-hidden member runs it - for a looped chain exactly the active member). Sibling legs stay `forward=true` so the ownership contract is untouched. Standalone recordings collect as a single member (byte-identical pre-chain behaviour). Build 0 errors; 14822/14822 xUnit pass (+5 chain-membership/window tests).

**Playtest 5 (2026-06-09, log `logs/2026-06-09_2341_forward-render-5`): chain fix VALIDATED.** The run now computes from playback start owned by the LAUNCH member (`Render run: rec=5d68d429 ... members=4 runLegs+=3 runArcs+=1 headUT=52569234.2` = the pad), hands off to `61e9177` with `runLegs+=4` (launch leg included), `onPreCull runLegs=4/4` drawn, works in TRACKSTATION too; zero run-leg skip/no-draw lines. The log-validation REC-001/REC-003 failure is benign (watch-only session, no live recording started/stopped). NEW artifact observed: the body-fixed launch leg (drawn at the LIVE planet rotation) swept against the inertial arcs - the gap closed exactly as the icon approached the handoff (the 'Duna One' mission cadence is exactly 912 Kerbin rotations, so body-fixed == inertial precisely when the icon arrives at each point), then re-opened as OVERLAP behind it. With a non-rotation-aligned loop cadence the seam gap at crossing would be arbitrary.

**Body-fixed run-leg hide (2026-06-09, maintainer rule):** a persistent run leg must be drawable in the INERTIAL frame. Decide-side `IsRunLegAnchorCandidate` (both-side same-body conic bracket in the leg's own recording, the `TryAnchorLegToConicSeam` precondition) gates the run enqueue; draw-side `TryDrawLeg(requireConicAnchor: true)` skips forward legs whose anchor is residual-rejected. One-sided body-fixed legs (launch ascent, descent-to-surface, no-conic segments) draw ONLY while the icon rides them (head-gated pass, where body-fixed is correct - the live ghost is glued to the pad/terrain) and disappear once the icon steps onto the next run element, so they can never rotate-sweep into the inertial line. `bodyFixedHidden=N` added to the `Render run` log line. Build 0 errors; 14827/14827 xUnit pass (+5 anchor-candidate tests).

**Playtest 6 (2026-06-10, log `logs/2026-06-10_0043_forward-render-6`): body-fixed hide VALIDATED, no excessive overlap.** Launch run shows `runLegs+=2 runArcs+=1 bodyFixedHidden=1` (anchored coast legs + suborbital arc forward, stub hidden), post-handoff `bodyFixedHidden=2` (launch leg + stub gone, no overlap sweep); zero draw-side anchor rejects; `selected=1 sampled=1` per arc refresh (no duplicate arcs); the lone `polyline-orbit-overlap` anomaly is a one-frame proto-line handoff race (`drawIcons=NONE`, benign). Remaining artifact: while the icon RIDES the body-fixed ascent, its end visibly trails the inertial run (gap closes only at the handoff).

**Seam bridge (2026-06-10, maintainer request):** fill the ascent-to-run gap with a connector that uses the NEXT ARC'S OWN CURVATURE: draw the target arc's first 60 samples with the seam rotation unwound along them (sample i rotated `seamAngle*(1-i/60)` about the seam axis, radial-blended so point 0 lands exactly on the leg's drawn end and point 60 exactly on the arc); while bridging, the arc's draw range starts at sample 60 so the bridge REPLACES its lead-in (never a double line) and degenerates continuously into the arc as the gap closes (no pop at handoff). Gates: angle <= 45 deg, seam UT gap <= 120 s, same body (`IsBridgeArcCandidate`, the tested rule used by the production tracking). Pure `TryBuildSeamBridgeLocalPoints` (Rodrigues, xUnit-covered) + `SeamBridgeAngleRad` + `SelectBridgeArcIndex`; armed in the decide pass (`bridge=True bridgeAngleDeg=` on the `Render run` line), drawn in `TryDrawSeamBridge` (onPreCull, after legs + arcs, `bridge=` in the onPreCull summary). Build 0 errors; 14867/14867 xUnit pass (+7 bridge tests).

**Playtest 7 (2026-06-10, log `logs/2026-06-10_1754_forward-render-7`): launch bridge works; Duna issues confirmed.** Only 7 `Seam bridge drawn` lines, ALL in the launch window; the Duna run shows `bridge=False` throughout (no body-fixed HEAD-leg-end -> arc pair exists there) and `bodyFixedHidden=2-3` (the landing descent legs were hidden until the icon reached them - the "landing polyline only rendered at the end" report). The launch bridge angle is dominated by a ~5 deg STATIC geometric seam offset (not the rotation gap), and the unsigned angle gate kept drawing the bridge on the OVERSHOOT side too.

**Generalized bridges + future body-fixed legs (2026-06-10, maintainer rules):** (1) only PAST body-fixed legs hide (`ShouldHideBodyFixedRunLeg`); FUTURE ones (the landing descent) draw body-fixed, enqueued with `requireConicAnchor=false` (past legs keep the anchor requirement). (2) Bridges generalize to BOTH SIDES of every drawn body-fixed/future leg: `DecideSeamBridges` finds the adjacent above-surface conic per side across chain members (`IsBridgeAdjacentConic`), sources its inertial samples from the matching cached forward arc (clipped at the merge sample via `drawStartIndex`/`drawEndIndex` - never a double line) or on-demand `GetBridgeConicSamples` (the stock-drawn current element; 61 `getPositionAtUT` samples cached per segment+side), and unwinds the seam rotation along the lead-in (end-side) or REVERSED tail (start-side) through the same pure helper. (3) The signed-gap rule (`IsSeamGapAhead`: displacement from previous end to next start projected on the conic's travel direction) skips the bridge on OVERSHOOT - a bridge only fills a real trajectory gap. All endpoints recompute per frame from the leg's fresh scratch + inertial samples, so bridges track at any warp and any icon position. Logs: `bridges+=N bridgeLegs=M` on the Render run line, per-bridge `Seam bridge drawn ... side= src=`, skip reasons (`angle too large` / `overshoot`). Build 0 errors; 14870/14870 xUnit pass (adjacency/signed-gap/visibility/reversed-tail tests replace the retired single-side selector tests).

**Playtest 8 (2026-06-10, log `logs/2026-06-10_1823_forward-render-8`): star-polygon lines around Kerbin.** Log-confirmed source: `Seam bridge drawn: rec=61e9177 leg=2 side=end src=sampled-conic` - the end-side bridge of the pre-ellipse coast leg targeted the PARKING ELLIPSE, and `GetBridgeConicSamples` sampled "duration/3" of a segment spanning 11.4M s (~660 loiter revolutions): 61 samples at ~63000 s strides land at arbitrary orbit phases, and the connected polyline drew as a star around Kerbin.

**Star fix (2026-06-10):** (1) full-loop closed orbits are RUN BOUNDARIES - `DecideSeamBridges` now skips them as bridge targets (`IsFullLoopClosedOrbit` on the adjacency candidate; bridging into one violates the stop-before-the-repeating-ellipse rule, and the anchored leg ends exactly ON the ellipse seam anyway, so no gap exists there); (2) defense-in-depth: `ComputeBridgeSampleSpanSeconds` (pure, xUnit-covered) clamps the on-demand sample span to min(duration, period)/3, so a multi-revolution segment can never stride-scatter again even if classification misses. Build 0 errors; 14871/14871 xUnit pass (+1 span-clamp test).

**Playtest 9 (2026-06-10, log `logs/2026-06-10_1837_forward-render-9`): star FIXED (zero `src=sampled-conic`, `bridges+=2`), DLL verified not clobbered (loaded 18:29:21 > deploy 18:28). NEW root cause found for "bridges only update at transitions": KSP's CO-ROTATING WORLD FRAME.** At low altitude the world frame rotates WITH the main body; the "frame-stable" inertial offsets captured once at cache build (forward arcs + bridge conic samples) freeze in that frame - effectively rotating WITH the planet while the true inertial orbit counter-rotates - so legs, arcs, and bridges stay mutually frozen until an element transition rebuilds the cache (the constant `angleDeg=5.02/4.49` across whole warp runs; the anchored leg's drifting 0.02->1.26 bridge angle was the live-evaluated leg moving against the frozen samples).

**Rotating-frame resample (2026-06-10):** `ForwardArcSet.captureInverseRotAngle` + per-entry capture on the bridge sample cache; when `Planetarium.InverseRotAngle` drifts from capture (`HasFrameRotationDrift`, pure), the offsets are RESAMPLED IN PLACE (`ResampleForwardArcOffsetsInPlace` via each arc's stored `sourceSegment`; `FillBridgeConicSamples` refills the cached array) - same VectorLines, same arrays, only values refresh, evaluated through the live frame-correct Orbit. In inertial-frame eras the angle does not move, so the cache behaves exactly as before. Rate-limited `fwd-arc-rot-resample` log shows the cadence. Build 0 errors; 14872/14872 xUnit pass (+1 drift-predicate test).

**Playtest 10 (2026-06-10, log `logs/2026-06-10_1849_forward-render-10`): rotating-frame fix VALIDATED.** `fwd-arc-rot-resample` fired per frame in the co-rotating era with `faults=0`; the launch bridge angle now BREATHES (5.01 -> 3.55 -> closing); start-side bridge live (`leg=2 side=start`); Duna descent legs visible ahead of the icon (`runLegs+=5 bodyFixedHidden=0`) with end-side bridges at 0.06/0.16 deg and overshoot skips at 12/22.6 deg (the signed rule pruning correctly); zero stars, zero Parsek exceptions; the log-validation REC-001/REC-003 failure is the benign watch-only-session case.

**Clean-context Fable review (2026-06-10, against the full origin/main...HEAD diff):** verdict SHIP-READY modulo playtest; all six critical invariants verified to hold (ownership publish untouched by the forward pass, recorded-data immutability incl. the CoalesceSameOrbitFragments by-reference contract, scratch reuse, VectorLine lifecycle, once-per-chain decide, pass ordering). Findings actioned: **MAJOR-1** (icon entering a TRAILING leg past the last conic cleared the whole run; fixed - `ComputeForwardWindow` past-end branch keeps the run alive back to the previous boundary with `StopUT=+inf`, gated by a new `dataEndUT` param (chain max `EndUT`) so static recordings never paint; +3 window tests); **MINOR-2** (decide-time arc clip could orphan a one-frame hole if the bridge draw failed; fixed - bridges now draw BEFORE arcs and the clip applies only on an actual bridge draw); **MINOR-3** (bridge sample cache key now includes sma+ecc so a re-aim window rollover cannot serve stale wrong-aimed samples); **NIT-6** (OrbitArcSampler doc said BODY-LOCAL, samples are world-frame; fixed in doc + in-game test message); **NIT-7** (bridge-key prefix match now uses the `|` separator; stale cacheKey doc comments fixed). **MINOR-4** (residual per-frame allocations on the fragmented-chain path - coalesce copies + arc key strings) accepted as bounded and consistent with existing log-key churn. **MINOR-5** documented below.

**Playtest 11 (2026-06-10, evidence from `Player-prev.log` - KSP was restarted so KSP.log only has the fresh boot; `logs/2026-06-10_1931_forward-render-11` captures the new session):** two maintainer reports at the Duna landing. (1) "the landing trail + its bridge disappeared after the icon passed" - LOG-CONFIRMED: at touchdown the chain hands off to the next member (`0b91670c`, the surface segment), the landing leg becomes a PAST body-fixed leg and the playtest-5/7 hide rule ate it (`bodyFixedHidden=1 bridges+=0` post-handoff) while the inertial arcs persisted. (2) "the bridge before the landing polyline renders straight" - NOT yet reproducible from the geometry (the construction rotates curved conic-tail samples and cannot produce a straight line from a curved source); the leg-15 start bridge behaved as designed in the log (overshoot-skipped 27->1.3 deg converging on approach, drawn 0.01->1.11 deg growing after the pass).

**Terminal-leg keep + curvature instrumentation (2026-06-10):** the past-hide rule now applies ONLY when an ABOVE-SURFACE conic follows the leg within the run (`AnyAboveSurfaceConicStartsAtOrAfter`, pure): the launch ascent (suborbital conic follows) still hides, but a TERMINAL past body-fixed leg - the landing trail, nothing after it - stays visible, glued to its landing site, drawn with `requireConicAnchor=false` (one-sided legs cannot anchor) and kept bridge-eligible so its start-side bridge persists and tracks the growing rotation gap. The bridge draw log gains `chordDevKm=` (max deviation of the drawn bridge from its straight chord, via pure `MaxChordDeviation`) + `sliceSpanDeg=` (angular span of the conic-side sample slice), so the next playtest QUANTIFIES the straightness report: chordDevKm ~0 on a drawn bridge = genuinely straight (source slice degenerate, investigate); substantial = the straight line was a different element. Build 0 errors; 14877/14877 xUnit pass (+2 tests).

**Playtest 12 (2026-06-10, TS session, log `logs/2026-06-10_1956_forward-render-12`): terminal-keep VALIDATED; bridge curvature PROVEN; two NEW bugs root-caused.** The leg-15 start bridge logged `chordDevKm=22.9-26.2 sliceSpanDeg=38.85` (healthily curved) and persisted past touchdown with growing angles - so the seam bridge is NOT the straight line. The maintainer's straight segment = LEG 15'S INTERIOR CHORD: the landing leg merges Absolute frame clusters across frameless OrbitalCheckpoint spans whose covering conics are BELOW-SURFACE (FIX #27 cover exclusion), so the 208 s [70963444->70963652] recorded-data gap rendered as one straight chord. The missing icon (both on the landing chord and on the TS escape-burn leg) = `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip`'s `OrbitSegmentActive` veto: ANY recorded conic covering the current UT killed the marker - including a below-surface conic that draws no arc (and whose proto was DESTROYED at the below-surface boundary, `GhostDestroyed ut=70963396.4`), and mid-burn fragments under a polyline-owned leg whose proto icon is force-hidden.

**Playtest-12 fixes (2026-06-10):** (1) the `OrbitSegmentActive` veto is BYPASSED when the polyline OWNS the recording's phase (`IsRenderingNonOrbitalLeg`): ownership means the proto line/icon is hidden or the proto destroyed, so the marker is the sole indicator; the veto keeps its no-duplicate-marker job for non-owned orbital phases. (2) Frameless-gap CONIC FILL: `FillFramelessGapsFromConics` (pure) inserts up to 30 interior points per >15 s same-body gap covered by a BELOW-SURFACE recorded conic, sampled from THAT conic via the injected `ConicGapSampler` seam (Driver-side `SampleConicBodyFixedAtUT`: frame-correct Orbit eval; lat/alt rotation-free; lon counter-rotated to the RECORDED basis via the new pure `RecordedLongitudeAtUT`, the exact inverse of `BodyFixedLongitudeAtUT`, time-invariant so the cached leg never drifts). The landing chord now renders with the recorded descent conic's own curvature, and the marker rides the curve. RENDER-time only - recorded data untouched. `gapFilled=` added to the Polyline build log. Build 0 errors; 14880/14880 xUnit pass (+3 tests).

**Playtest-12 follow-up (2026-06-10): icon STILL vanished on the gap-filled chord.** The veto bypass let the classifier through, but the next step killed the marker: `TryResolveRecordingWorldPosition` brackets the RECORDING's frames, and the chord span is a frameless OrbitalCheckpoint section (`bracket-miss` -> `SkippedPositionFail`); the conic gap-fill points live only in the renderer's leg cache, which that resolver never sees. The flight map survives because its marker RIDES the polyline; the TS single-marker tail drew only at the resolver position. Fixed: on resolver failure, the TS marker falls back to `TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` (the drawn line, including the gap-filled curve; the ride only succeeds when a leg containing the head actually drew this frame, so no undrawn-phase markers). `rodePolyline=` added to the marker draw log. Build 0 errors; 14880/14880 xUnit pass.

**Playtest 13 (2026-06-10, FLIGHT map, log `logs/2026-06-10_2025_forward-render-13`): gap-fill VALIDATED (`gapFilled=35`, leg 15 39->74 pts, curved chord), but the icon STILL vanished - in MAP VIEW this time.** Root cause: the flight-map labeled-marker walk iterates `flight.Engine.ghostStates` (pid-keyed); the ENGINE GHOST is destroyed at the below-surface boundary (`Ghost #30 destroyed (chain-loop unit member outside its window) ut=70963396.4`), so the recording has no walk entry at all (`Map marker summary: candidates=4 drawn=0 positionFailure=0` - never considered). Fixed: recording-keyed fallback after the pid walk (the TS atmospheric-pass equivalent) - any committed recording NOT covered by a ghost state whose polyline OWNS the current phase draws its labeled marker riding the drawn line (`TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` self-gates on the leg having drawn this frame; ownership is exactly one recording per chain). `Ghost-less polyline marker` log line marks the path. Build 0 errors; 14880/14880 xUnit pass.

**Playtest 14 (2026-06-10): CONFIRMED GOOD by the maintainer** (curved landing descent, icon across the chord in both scenes, trail + bridge persist after touchdown).

**Pre-merge clean-context Fable review #2 (2026-06-10, full origin/main...HEAD diff at d48f25a51): verdict SAFE TO MERGE.** All five critical invariants re-verified across the whole diff (ownership untouched by the forward pass, recorded-data immutability incl. the gap-fill build-time-copy contract and the Coalesce by-reference results, VectorLine lifecycle, scratch reuse, pending-list lifecycles); the conic gap-fill's time-invariance (RecordedLongitudeAtUT inverse identity) confirmed mathematically sound; both origin/main merges proven lossless (merge-base == main tip, doc-only conflicts). 14898/14898 tests. Findings actioned pre-merge: MINOR-1 (transient two-markers-per-chain at a warp handoff: the ghost-less fallback now skips chains that already drew a LABELED marker via the pid-keyed walk this frame - `drawnChainMarkerBuffer`; a chain whose live sibling shows only its stock vessel icon still gets the playing head marked); NIT-3 (drawn-this-frame comments softened to mention the HeldLastGood pan-hold). Accepted as documented: MINOR-2 (head-leg bridge candidacy inspects the chain-deciding member only - looped chains unaffected), NIT-1 (eager rate-limited log formats, bounded), NIT-2 (coarse bridge sample cache clear on release).

**Known limitations:** (pre-existing) the forward/run pass only runs for recordings with at least one non-orbital leg, so a chain whose ACTIVE member is leg-less (pure-conic segment) computes no run that frame; (review MINOR-5) ghosts in OVERLAP loop units are skipped by `ShadowRenderDriver.ClassifyScope`, so `IsDirectorTracking` is false and the gap-hold gate suppresses their run entirely (fail-closed, Director-consistent).

## TODO - Missions feature completion milestones (M-MIS roadmap; investigated 2026-06-10)

The single ordered list of what remains to call the Missions feature (`docs/parsek-missions-design.md`, shipped core) COMPLETE. Ordered by necessity / priority: each milestone was code-investigated on 2026-06-10 (implemented-already? viable? what exactly remains?) and the findings are recorded inline. Detailed history for each item lives in the per-item entries further down this file (cross-referenced); this list is the planning surface.

### Reuse mandate (applies to every solver-flavored milestone below)

Do NOT re-implement intercept / window math from scratch. The 2026-05-28 prior-art survey (recorded in `docs/dev/done/plans/reaim-interplanetary-transfers.md` + the prior-art note in the phase-lock entry below) already settled the sourcing:

- **`Reaim/UvLambert.cs`** is OUR owned, unit-tested (Curtis Algorithm 5.2) full-3D universal-variables Lambert solver. Extend it; do not replace it.
- **`Reaim/ITransferSolver.cs`** is the deliberate swap seam. The sanctioned fallback if UvLambert robustness proves insufficient (multi-rev, near-180-deg singularity) is porting **MechJebLib's Gooding solver** (permissive license: public domain / Unlicense; ~577 lines + `V3`/`Statics` deps) behind that seam - a port, not a rewrite.
- **`Reaim/TransferWindowMath.cs`** already carries the KerbalAlarmClock-derived (MIT, attributed) phase-angle + synodic math. TransferWindowPlanner2's porkchop grid was evaluated and deliberately NOT needed (the congruent-window model uses recorded tof + synodic spacing). KSTS / Principia: surveyed, not applicable.
- The launch-side zero-drift near-coincidence primitive (`MissionPeriodicity.NextJointNearCoincidenceUT` / `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule`) and the unwired `Reaim/DestinationArrivalSolver.SolveArrivalWindow` are the in-repo multi-constraint window search. New milestones REUSE these, never re-derive them.

### M-MIS-0 - Land the Structure window (PR #1107) [in flight]

- **Status:** implemented; full xUnit suite green; **in-game playtest pending**, then merge. Read-only, additive (mission + route step list).
- **Requirement:** playtest in KSC + Flight (mission header button, logistics route detail button), then merge. No design work left.

### M-MIS-1 - Re-aim resolver reliability: deterministic E2E + congruent-window hardening

- **Why first:** every later re-aim milestone (M-MIS-2/3/6/7) builds on `ReaimPlaybackResolver.TryResolveWindowSegments`; today it fails INTERMITTENTLY (see the "Re-aim E2E in-game test ... is FLAKY" entry below: three distinct live-UT-dependent failure modes across 2026-06-06/07 runs).
- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** `ReaimEndToEndInGameTest.Reaim_KerbinToDuna_EveryWindowResolvesSaneTransfer` seeds its departure off the LIVE `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` (ReaimEndToEndInGameTest.cs:48), so failures are irreproducible by construction. Window-resolution failure conditions are enumerable (no heliocentric leg in window; body lookup; Lambert synthesis non-convergent across the +/-6% tof search, ReaimPlaybackResolver.cs:189-210; heliocentric-leg replacement returns null) - so a pinned-UT harness can binary-search the failing geometry.
- **Requirements:** (1) make the E2E deterministic (pinned departure UT(s), including at least one UT from each observed failure mode); (2) measure before any knob math (per the re-aim seam guidance); (3) "the faithful render is good enough for window k" is a valid outcome - the fix may be widening the tof search or simply classifying the window unresolvable-by-design, NOT stacking solver heuristics.
- **Harness step SHIPPED (branch `reaim-resolver-reliability`, 2026-06-10; plan `docs/dev/plans/reaim-resolver-reliability.md`):** root causes pinned statically. Mode A (`lan0=lanLast=0.00`) was a TEST-MODEL defect: the plane-constrained transfer is near-equatorial, where LAN alone is degenerate (decompile-confirmed: KSP pins LAN to 0 with a +X default node and AoP carries the periapsis longitude) - the rotation assertion now uses `TransferWindowMath.LongitudeOfPeriapsisDegrees` (LAN+AoP). Modes B/C (`window k must resolve`) came from the live-UT seed picking the FIRST scan success = the feasibility-band EDGE by construction, where Duna's eccentricity (synodic recurrence is exact only for circular orbits) pushes later windows outside the +/-6% recorded-tof search. The E2E now scans from a PINNED base UT and splits into: strict test on the band-CENTER departure (every window must resolve; a mid-band decline in-game = real resolver bug, investigate, never loosen), a band-EDGE test asserting the weak designed contract (resolve or decline cleanly to faithful, deterministically; all-decline valid), and a manual-only `Reaim_KerbinToDuna_FeasibilitySweep_Diagnostic` (AllowBatchExecution=false) that logs the full departure x window resolve/decline map. Pure helpers `ReaimFeasibilityScan` (cyclic band center/edge) + `LongitudeOfPeriapsisDegrees` are xUnit-covered.
- **Measured + CLASSIFIED (2026-06-10 in-game run, logs `2026-06-10_2213_reaim-mmis1-sweep`; full results in the plan's section 9):** all four Periodicity tests passed twice + sweep. The LPe fix validated directly (KSP's LAN/AoP split flipped between runs for the same transfer while LAN+AoP stayed 36.99). Sweep: 17-18/48 departures feasible; EVERY departure in the contiguous band resolved ALL 5 windows; declines only at isolated knife-edge departures (dep=25 Lambert non-convergence; dep=43/44 retrograde-branch mismatch), all clean fail-closed. **Decision: NO tof-search widening; knife-edge window declines are classified unresolvable-by-design** (a real recorded departure lies inside the band by definition). Geometry-aware tof centering stays M-MIS-3. One claim corrected: determinism is PER-FRAME, not absolute (KSP re-bases body-orbit epochs every frame, ~1e-15 fixed-UT noise flips only knife-edge scan entries; band center stable in every invocation; tests insensitive by design).
- **Status: COMPLETE with PR #1116** (merge pending). No solver changes shipped or needed.
- **Viability:** high; pure investigation + test work first, bounded solver tuning second.

### M-MIS-2 - Re-aim Phase-4 completion for the SUPPORTED shape (single Sun-child destination, <=1 moon)

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** of the Phase-4 ladder, P1 (`Reaim/DestinationArrivalSolver.SolveArrivalWindow`) EXISTS but is UNWIRED (no production caller); P2 (`DestinationConstraintExtractor.ExtractDestinationConstraints`) is wired into `ArrivalHoldPlanner.cs:57-58`; P3a-c + the per-loop hold `W_N` SHIPPED (PR #1030, Duna One validated). Remaining per `docs/dev/plans/reaim-destination-arrival-alignment.md` sect. 7: **P4 loiter re-timer** - `ArrivalHoldPlanner.ComputeArrivalHold` REJECTS any destination with post-arrival loiter cuts (ArrivalHoldPlanner.cs:70-75), so a recorded destination parking loiter disables alignment entirely; needs the `keepRevs` API on `ReaimLoiterCompressor` (re-time the loiter instead of refusing - the same shared phasing-loiter knob M-MIS-4 specifies for the launch/rendezvous side; build it ONCE). **P5 render-path threading validation** - an in-game canary asserting the director orbit + body-fixed polyline read the SAME loop shift. **P6 tolerance UI** - tooltip widening only; its on-camera landing acceptance is GATED on the deferred S4 descent re-stitch (see the "#27 Problem 2 / S4 arrival-restitch" entry below - a playback-engine change, fix direction specified: rigid transform of the recorded arrival about the destination center).
- **Requirements:** implement P4 -> P5 -> P6 in order; wire `SolveArrivalWindow` only when a consumer needs the multi-constraint window pick (M-MIS-4 and M-MIS-6 are those consumers; do not wire speculatively). S4 re-stitch carries a product decision (rotate approach only = land at recorded site, vs approach + descent = re-aimed site) - decide before building.
- **Viability:** high for P4/P5/P6 (designs written); S4 is the one risky piece (playback-engine change on the re-aim seam).

### M-MIS-3 - High-inclination AND high-eccentricity targets (Moho-, Eeloo-class intercepts)

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (answers two open uncertainties).** Two SEPARATE limitations, neither in the solver itself (`UvLambert` is full-3D):
  - **Inclination (Moho ~7 deg):** a deliberate v1 simplification in `ReaimTransferSynthesizer.cs:130-153` PROJECTS the target endpoint r2 onto the launch body's orbital plane (to dodge the near-180-deg Lambert plane singularity); the SOI proximity check then measures against the target's ACTUAL position, so for a high-inclination small-SOI target the projected aim point is far outside the real SOI, the encounter check fails, and the window declines to faithful. For Duna (~0.06 deg) the offset stays inside the SOI, which is why it works today.
  - **Eccentricity (Eeloo ecc ~0.26, Moho ~0.2):** window spacing is pure synodic (`ReaimWindowPlanner.cs:59-86`, computed from the two orbital PERIODS only) and the per-window Lambert reuses the RECORDED time-of-flight with a fixed +/-6% search (`ReaimPlaybackResolver.cs:179-203`, 0.5% steps x 12) that was designed for the 180-deg singularity, NOT radial variation. An eccentric target sits at a DIFFERENT RADIUS each window (same phase angle, different true anomaly), so the required tof routinely leaves the +/-6% band and the window declines to faithful. Acknowledged as "not modeled this phase; fail closed" in `docs/dev/design-mission-periodicity.md` (~:969) but absent from the re-aim plan's deferred list (which covers only inclination). The congruent-window premise (same transfer SHAPE every window) is also false for an eccentric target - shape must adapt per window; the E2E asserts only LAN rotation, never sma/ecc congruence, so per-window expectations need to be made explicit when extending.
- **Requirements:** (1) inclination: make the projection CONDITIONAL - true 3D r2 except inside a guard band around the ~180-deg singularity (or skip projection whenever the out-of-plane offset `a*sin(inc)` exceeds a fraction of the target SOI, where projection guarantees a miss anyway); (2) eccentricity: make the tof search GEOMETRY-AWARE - REUSE `TransferWindowMath` (the KAC-derived closed-form transfer-time math) to center the per-window search on the tof implied by the ACTUAL window radii instead of the recorded tof, and/or scale the search band by target eccentricity; (3) relax the shape-congruence expectation for eccentric targets (varying sma/ecc per window is correct, not a defect); (4) for residual near-180-deg windows, widen the tof search first and only then port the Gooding multi-rev solver behind `ITransferSolver` (reuse mandate - never a new solver); (5) validation = deterministic synthetic Moho AND Eeloo window tests on the M-MIS-1 pinned-UT harness. `ReaimWindowPlanner` synodic spacing itself needs no change (the cadence is still synodic; only the per-window solve must adapt).
- **Viability:** high - both are scoped v1 simplifications, not new math. Depends on M-MIS-1 (deterministic harness).

### M-MIS-4 - Looped rendezvous / station-dock phase alignment (the logistics resupply profile)

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (answers the "rendezvous with an orbiting station at the destination" question):** today ANY Relative track section anchored to another vessel inside the included window flags the whole mission `Support.UnsupportedRendezvous` (`MissionPeriodicity.HasRendezvousWithinWindow`, MissionPeriodicity.cs:1474-1506) -> no phase-lock, no re-aim, arbitrary relaunch phase. The RENDERING of the docked/approach Relative sections mostly works, with one correction from review: LOOP playback resolves the anchor through the live-PID contract ONLY (`Recording.LoopAnchorVesselId`; an unloaded/unresolvable anchor SKIPS/RETIRES the member - `GhostPlaybackEngine` `loop-anchor-unloaded` / `unit-member-anchor-unloaded`), while the recorded-anchor-trajectory resolution via `TrackSection.anchorRecordingId` exists only on the NON-loop flight/map/KSC paths - so on loop the final approach follows the LIVE station when it resolves and renders nothing when it does not. What breaks is everything BEFORE the Relative section: the inertial transfer / phasing legs replay at an arbitrary station orbital phase, so the approach-to-station seam teleports each loop (the rendezvous twin of the Mun desync). Logistics v0 routes are FUNCTIONALLY unaffected (delivery fires at the `RecordedDockUT` loop-clock marker regardless of visual alignment); this milestone is the faithfulness layer that station-resupply routes will sit on.
- **Requirements - two tiers, both reusing shipped primitives (no new solver):**
  - **Tier 1 (same-parent, e.g. LKO station resupply - the canonical route):** add a `VesselOrbital` constraint kind whose period comes from the station's orbit (live orbit when the anchor PID resolves; else the anchor recording's OrbitSegments) and feed it to the EXISTING zero-drift near-coincidence scheduler (`MissionPeriodicity.TryBuildRelaunchSchedule`) as one more constraint. Station orbital periods are short (minutes-hours), so faithful windows stay frequent. Flip `HasRendezvousWithinWindow` from reject to extract for this shape.
  - **Tier 2 (cross-parent: station orbiting the destination body):** generalize the shipped per-loop arrival hold - a hold in `[0, T_station)` aligns the station's orbital phase at the rendezvous exactly as `W_N` aligns destination rotation (substitute the station period for T_rot); T_station is short, so the hold is cheap and achievable every window.
  - **The phasing-loiter knob (the "100-revolutions" resupply case, 2026-06-10):** a recorded LKO resupply that loitered ~100 parking revs before rendezvous would, replayed faithfully, (a) make every route cycle days long and (b) make faithful windows astronomically rare - the joint pad+station+100-rev geometry almost never recurs, even though the PLAYER's 100 revs existed precisely to phase-match an arbitrary launch time. The fix reuses two shipped primitives, generalized: **(1) promote `ReaimLoiterCompressor.ComputeCuts` from re-aim-only to a general Missions knob** - it is already PURE and general (whole-period cuts on any same-body closed-orbit loiter run, keepRevs parameter, cuts excised from the run START so the exit phase and therefore the recorded rendezvous approach geometry are preserved seamlessly; today it is only invoked inside `MissionLoopUnitBuilder`'s cross-parent re-aim branch, :442); **(2) make the kept-rev count PER-CYCLE** (the quantized subtractive twin of the per-loop hold `W_N`): per window, solve (launch window w, kept revs k_N) so the station sits at its recorded-relative phase at the dock UT - a two-frequency (T_pad, T_park) near-coincidence over the achievable set `{w*T_pad + k*T_park + const}`, i.e. the EXISTING zero-drift near-coincidence search, not new math. Whole-rev quantization keeps the render seamless by construction (an extra rev on a closed orbit is visually identical to the recorded loiter; no frozen-ghost dead time), with the station capture tolerance absorbing the residual. Same knob = M-MIS-2 P4's destination-loiter re-timer (the `keepRevs` API) and the cadence win for logistics: a compressed cycle delivers per PAD window (~daily) instead of per rare joint coincidence, and the chosen k_N must surface through the loop state into the route cycle id (M-MIS-11 item 3). Design decisions for the note: automatic vs a per-mission "Trim repeated orbits" toggle; k_N bounds (allow k_N > recorded revs, i.e. loiter EXTENSION for windows cutting alone cannot reach?); first play stays the faithful full recording, compression applies to loops only. NOTE the knob generalizes beyond stations: ANY mission with a long parking loiter before a departure burn (e.g. waiting in LKO for a Mun window) has the same two problems today (dead time replayed every loop + rare faithful windows because the loiter inflates the span), and the same per-window rev solve fixes it with the existing `Orbital(C)` constraint in place of `VesselOrbital` - so scope the design note as a general Missions looping tool with the station route as the prime consumer, not as a rendezvous-only feature.
  - **Decide the moving-target policy FIRST (short design note):** a LIVE station drifts (player boosts it, orbit changes) while the recorded anchor is the recording's truth - define which anchor source the constraint reads, when it re-derives, and what happens when the live station's orbit has diverged from the recorded one (likely: re-derive from live, amber-flag when the divergence exceeds tolerance, fail closed to faithful).
  - **Anchor lifecycle classes (2026-06-10 online scenario sweep):** the moving-target policy must cover three anchor classes, not just a drifting station: (a) a recorded Parsek vessel (live-PID on loops; the recorded-trajectory fallback via `anchorRecordingId` exists only on NON-loop paths today, so the design note must decide whether loops gain it); (b) a save-unique LIVE-ONLY object with NO recording - rescue-contract derelict pods and asteroids/comets (both ARE vessels in KSP; a claw grab is the couple) - where the recorded-anchor fallback does not exist and a VANISHED anchor (recovered rescue pod, redirected asteroid) must fail closed to faithful; (c) a station that changes BETWEEN loops (multi-launch assembly, other docked traffic) - divergence tolerance must cover composition/mass change, not only orbit drift. Asteroid-redirect missions themselves are one-shot by nature: looping one replays the ghost faithfully; no re-aim of an already-moved asteroid is attempted.
- **Design note SHIPPED (2026-06-10, branch `design-mission-phasing-alignment`):** `docs/dev/design-mission-phasing-alignment.md` records the nine decisions (D1-D9): anchor must EXIST in the save, live orbit only, no recorded-orbit derivation fallback, vanished anchors fail closed (resolves the period-cell-vs-retired-member UX incoherence); loops keep the live-PID anchor contract; the phasing-loiter knob is FULLY AUTOMATIC (kept revs derived from the solved relaunch schedule; no toggle, an opt-out is added only on playtest demand), first play always faithful; per-cycle k_N is a NEW small (pad window x kept revs) enumeration on top of the existing zero-drift primitives (no new solver math), k_N in [1, recorded+10], cuts restricted to BEFORE the first rendezvous (a timeline-rigidity guard that also auto-aligns undock/redock events); honest window math recorded: without the knob a 1-degree station tolerance admits ~0.5% of pad windows (tens of Kerbin days between aligned launches), so the knob is load-bearing for routes, not an optimization; Tier 1 = `VesselOrbital` constraint + extraction flip for exactly-one same-parent closed-orbit anchor; Tier 2 = arrival hold with T_station, dual-constraint destinations stay fail-closed with `SolveArrivalWindow` wiring as a post-M4c follow-up. Build order: M4a Tier 1 -> M4b knob (own plan doc; the per-launch-cuts span-clock seam; shared with M-MIS-2 P4's keepRevs API) -> M4c Tier 2.
- **Viability:** high for Tier 1 (a third constraint in an existing solver); moderate for Tier 2. Priority is HIGH because logistics (the M1-M6 roadmap, PR #1113) is the active downstream consumer and station resupply is its headline profile.

### M-MIS-5 - Dock as an interval boundary + docked composition counts [GATED: after logistics v0 integration]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** confirmed still unimplemented - `MissionCompositionBuilder` interval edges come only from structural-peel UTs (MissionComposition.cs:132-143), never Dock/Board merge UTs, so a docked "AB" stretch cannot be looped in isolation and docked labels undercount (controllers gained at dock are never added). FEASIBLE with data already present: every leg carries `OriginBranchPointType` (set at MissionStructure.cs:378, includes Dock/Board), so the builder can emit a merge-UT edge on the continuing line when a leg begins via Dock/Board (+ add the joining vessel's controllers to the interval label).
- **Requirements:** keep the recorded decision (no auto Mission lifecycle on dock; topology-only). Do the boundary + the label undercount TOGETHER (they are one model change). Stays deferred until logistics/supply-routes v0 integration settles what a "docked stretch loop" must mean for routes - do not fix piecemeal (see the "docking/undocking effect on mission structure" entry below).
- **Logistics cross-link (2026-06-10, PR #1113 section 19 review):** logistics M4 ships multi-stop with mid-recording START-trims (the undock->undock shuttle runs of scenario family 3) as a DOCUMENTED LIMITATION surfaced in the rejection reason - explicitly NOT a Missions edit on their side. THIS milestone is the Missions-side fix that later lifts that limitation; schedule it after logistics M4 so the rejection text and the lift land coherently.
- **Viability:** high mechanically; gated on logistics sequencing, not on missing data.

### M-MIS-6 - Multi-moon destinations: the looped "Jool-5" mission, window-alignment cut [needs a short design note first]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (answers the open uncertainty):** today a Jool-5 recording loops on the FAITHFUL path only: `ReaimClassifier` supports the Kerbin->Jool transfer (Jool is a direct Sun child) but `DestinationConstraintExtractor` fails closed at 2+ SOI-entered moons, so nothing aligns the moons; each moon-relative block self-anchors to the LIVE moon while the Jool-centric inter-moon arcs replay inertially, so every encounter seam renders disconnected (the Mun-desync mechanism, once per moon). What makes it tractable WITHOUT new math: (a) all encounters shift TOGETHER under one arrival hold, so alignment needs the moons' joint CONFIGURATION to recur, not each moon independently; (b) stock Laythe:Vall:Tylo are a near-exact 1:2:4 resonance (period ratios off by ~1e-5 from rounded SMAs), so the inner-three configuration recurs every Tylo period (~211,926 s) to well within SOI tolerance - a per-loop hold in `[0, T_config)` aligns an inner-three tour exactly like the shipped `W_N` destination-rotation hold (substitute T_config for T_rot); (c) the stock major moons are tidally locked, so landing-rotation constraints collapse into orbital phase (the tidal-lock collapse `MissionPeriodicity` already implements); (d) Bop/Pol are incommensurate with the inner three - a full 5-moon tight alignment is effectively non-recurring, so those legs get Loose tolerance via the near-coincidence search or the mission fails closed to faithful (a VALID outcome, surfaced in the UI, never silent).
- **Requirements:** (1) short design note first (this is the "2+-moon mini star systems" deferred item, design doc sect. 14.4); (2) REUSE: wire the existing unwired `DestinationArrivalSolver.SolveArrivalWindow` (multi-constraint window pick over k*synodic) + generalize the per-loop hold from T_rot to a joint configuration period; (3) build the failing synthetic multi-moon test BEFORE any knob math (re-aim seam guidance); (4) intra-SOI re-aim (per-leg Lambert re-solves inside the destination system) is explicitly the SECOND cut, tracked as M-MIS-7 - only justified if this hold-based model proves insufficient in playtest.
- **Viability:** moderate - the resonant-inner-three + tidally-locked case maps onto shipped primitives; the general (Bop/Pol, non-resonant packs) case intentionally degrades to loose/faithful.

### M-MIS-7 - Intra-SOI re-aim and multi-hop targets (Jool-like systems second cut; Ike-class targets) [GATED: on M-MIS-6 playtest evidence]

- **What it is:** the recursive "mini star system" model - re-solving transfer legs INSIDE a destination system instead of only the heliocentric leg. Two consumers: (a) **moon-to-moon legs of a multi-moon tour** when the M-MIS-6 hold-based joint-configuration model is insufficient (non-resonant moon packs, Bop/Pol legs, long inter-moon loiters): per-leg Lambert re-solves in the gas giant's frame + per-leg holds at each moon-SOI seam; (b) **multi-hop TARGETS** - a target that is not a direct child of the common ancestor (Ike via Duna; rejected today by the `ReaimClassifier` single-hop guard, ReaimClassifier.cs:124-130): re-aim the heliocentric leg to the parent, then the in-SOI hop to the moon is the same intra-SOI machinery.
- **Requirements:** REUSE everything - `UvLambert` is body-agnostic (mu is a parameter), so the same `ITransferSolver` seam serves Jool-centric solves; the per-loop hold clock primitives generalize per leg. This is a genuine new subsystem (per-leg seams, recursive window scheduling): budget a full design note + the failing-test-first discipline, and do NOT build it speculatively - M-MIS-6's playtest decides whether it is needed at all.
- **Viability:** hard; deliberately last among the solver milestones.

### M-MIS-8 - Cross-tree foreign dock: loop a shared docked journey from the partner's side

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** playback ALREADY follows cross-tree dock links via PID matching - `GhostChainWalker.MergeCrossTreeLinks` (GhostChainWalker.cs:487-574) merges chains across trees. The Missions side is single-tree by construction (`Mission.TreeId`; `MissionStructureBuilder.BuildBranchLinks` walks one tree's BranchPoints, MissionStructure.cs:331-392). The gap is a Missions-view + selection-model change (a selection spanning two trees), not a data problem.
- **Requirements:** follow the same PID dock-link pattern `GhostChainWalker` uses; decide the persistence shape (multi-tree mission vs linked-mission pairing) before building - it touches `Mission` serialization. Lowest functional urgency (UX nicety; the controller-side loop already works).
- **Viability:** moderate; bounded but touches persistence + UI.

### M-MIS-9 - New-branch inclusion policy (re-fly supersede splits default to INCLUDED) [revisit with logistics route persistence]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** confirmed by design - `Mission` persists only the EXCLUDED sets (Mission.cs), there is no definition-time head-id snapshot, and `MissionStore.ReconcileSelections` (MissionStore.cs:101-162) only drops stale excluded ids (one-way). A genuinely new branch silently joins every Mission on the tree.
- **Requirements:** becomes a real (not cosmetic) issue the moment logistics persists routes on top of Missions (a supersede split silently joining a route-backing selection changes deliveries). Fix shape when scheduled: record the known head-id set at definition time, or a per-mission "new branches: include/exclude" toggle. Small, but coordinate with logistics M1 (scenario lifecycle) scheduling.
- **Viability:** high; deliberately parked.

### M-MIS-10 - Scenario verification sweep: believed-supported archetypes, never explicitly verified [not sequenced - run incrementally alongside any milestone]

A 2026-06-10 online sweep of what KSP players actually fly (stock career contract types: satellite/relay, rescue, tourism, asteroid redirect, station resupply / crew rotation; the classic community challenges: Jool 5, Elcano, K-Prize, grand tours, Eve return; and the automation prior art Parsek overlaps with: Routine Mission Manager, KSTS, FMRS, MKS supply chains) found NO missing alignment subsystem beyond M-MIS-1..9 - but it surfaced a set of archetypes the recorder/missions stack should support TODAY that have no explicit test or playtest. Each needs a cheap in-game verify (file a todo entry where it breaks):

- **Constellation deployment** (resonant-orbit carrier releasing N relay sats, the CommNet career staple): an N-fork controlled-decouple tree where every branch ends in a perpetual-orbit terminal. Verify the fork-tree records, the Missions window renders N branches, selection/trim behaves, and N real satellites materialize at recording end.
- **Reusable booster flyback** (FMRS-class profile - the recorder's home turf): booster = controlled-decoupled child flown back to a landing. Verify the branch loops with the main mission and the booster's landed terminal spawns/recovers correctly.
- **Launch from a NON-Kerbin body** (Eve return ascent, Mun surface -> orbit, Laythe spaceplane): `Rotation(B)` / `launchBodyName` handling is generic by construction through the zero-drift scheduler, but every test and playtest to date launches from Kerbin. Verify phase-lock + pad anchoring for an off-Kerbin launch site (also exercises rewind-from-surface there).
- **Claw couples** (asteroid / derelict grabs): verify a claw `OnPartCouple` records as a Dock-equivalent branch point, and that a claw-coupled asteroid (PotatoRoid part) survives ghost-visual building and the snapshot part-name path.
- **Long surface expeditions** (Elcano-class rover circumnavigation, days of driving): no alignment problem (surface sections are rotation-locked and render correctly at any UT) but a recording-size / optimizer / polyline-budget STRESS case; measure before declaring supported.
- **Round-trip resupply with vehicle reuse** (the Routine Mission Manager marquee profile: outbound dock, return, recover): the Missions side (whole-tree span loop incl. the return leg) should already work; the delivery-AND-recovery-per-cycle economics are logistics-roadmap territory - verify the rendering half here, leave the ledger half to logistics M1-M6.
- **Suborbital tourist hop** (career tourism staple): atmospheric-only -> unconstrained free loop; should be the trivial case - one verify run.

### M-MIS-11 - Missions -> Logistics loop-unit API hardening [schedule alongside logistics M3-M5; nothing here blocks logistics M1/M2]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (PR #1113 section 19 + seam code review).** The route-on-Missions consumption WORKS and the locked-layer doctrine held: a route synthesizes a PRIVATE `Mission` via `RouteBackingMission.BuildMission` (never stored in `MissionStore`), feeds it through the unchanged `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build`, and reads the span clock through `RouteLoopClock` -> `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryComputeSpanLoopUT`; delivery fires once per dock-phase crossing with warp-skip handled fire-once-snap-forward, and `cycle-N` ids stamp all three ledger rows. Verified NON-needs: logistics does not need multi-loop-per-tree (one route binds one tree via `RouteTreeGuard`, so the design-doc sect. 12 "one ghost of one recording on several Mission clocks" deferral stays moot), and round-trip-in-one-recording is logistics M4's widened render window, not a Missions change. The friction an API pass should target, in value order:
  1. **First-class loop-unit build seam:** `RouteOrchestrator.ResolveLoopUnit` (RouteOrchestrator.cs:766) re-synthesizes the throwaway Mission and re-runs the FULL builder pipeline on every orchestrator tick and again per eligibility check, and `RouteBackingMission.ComputeExcludedIntervalKeys` re-walks the composition with its own trim logic (a second walker of the same tree). Provide a `BuildLoopUnitForSelection(treeId, trimWindow)` entry point + build-signature caching so consumers stop paying for (and duplicating) the Mission-pipeline shape.
  2. **Loop milestones as events, not polling:** expose span-clock cycle events (cycle started / UT-marker crossed / cycle completed) carrying the cycle index, with the warp-skip semantics (fire once, snap forward) centralized in the emitter instead of re-implemented per consumer. Serves the route dock crossing today, logistics M3's N loading-window markers per cycle tomorrow, and the Missions-window TTL display.
  3. **Cycle-index semantic typing (CORRECTED 2026-06-10 - NOT a logistics M5 blocker):** the scheduled-launch index IS already exposed - on the schedule path `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` returns it as the out `cycleIndex` (`cycleIndex = sIdx` from `MissionRelaunchSchedule.TryResolveActiveLaunch`, GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7258-7262) and `RouteLoopClock.TryGetRouteLoopState` surfaces it, so M5's "`CadenceMultiplier` as a modulo on the scheduled-launch index" is route-side-only work. The real (minor) gap is SEMANTIC: `cycleIndex` means flat-cadence index on a null-schedule unit and scheduled-launch index on a scheduled unit, distinguished only by `unit.RelaunchSchedule != null`. The hardening item is a typed exposure (an enum/flag or distinct fields) so consumers cannot misread one as the other - a nice-to-have, not a prerequisite.
  4. **Span-clock parameter object:** `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` (GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7198) has grown to 13 parameters (5 in + 3 out + 5 optional), reached directly by the flight engine, `RouteLoopClock`, and `ReaimPlaybackResolver`, and through the 15-parameter `DecideUnitMemberRender` wrapper (GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7478) by the KSC / TS / map-marker surfaces; fold the unit-derived inputs into one context struct built off the `LoopUnit` so a consumer cannot mis-thread schedule / cuts / hold fields.
  5. **Member identity contract:** loop-unit members are POSITIONAL indices into the raw `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings` (supersede/ERS-blind by design; the orchestrator carries an [ERS-exempt] comment re-stating the alignment invariant). Either formalize the invariant as a tested contract for all unit consumers, or move membership to recording-id keys with one positional resolve at the engine boundary.
  6. **Phase-anchor read-back:** the builder floors the anchor to spanEnd and overrides the route's `LoopAnchorUT`, so routes (and the TTL UI) re-derive the effective anchor; expose the EFFECTIVE anchor on the built unit.
  7. **(Stretch, gameplay) Parallel shipments / fleets:** route loops are single-instance today (cadence raised to >= span). A fleet profile (dispatch interval < route duration, several cycles in flight at once) maps onto the EXISTING per-instance overlap rendering (Integration 2) but needs per-INSTANCE marker crossings, per-instance cycle ids, and per-instance cargo escrow before logistics could adopt it. Park until a player route profile demands it.
- **Cross-note for logistics M2 (harvest provenance, PR #1113):** the harvest-attribution capture plan names `ModuleResourceHarvester` / `ModuleResourceConverter`; stock asteroid/comet mining uses the SEPARATE `ModuleAsteroidDrill` / `ModuleCometDrill` modules. Include them in the M2 capture surface or asteroid-mining routes (the asteroid variant of scenario family 4) will fail flow closure with an untracked-gain rejection.

### Explicitly out of scope (faithful replay is the accepted, UI-surfaced behavior; revisit only on playtest demand)

- **Gravity-assist / multi-heliocentric-leg transfers** - `ReaimClassifier` rejects more than one heliocentric leg (ReaimClassifier.cs:141-146); re-aiming a chained assist is a different problem class (the assist geometry constrains every leg jointly).
- **Atmo-direct / aerocapture arrival alignment** - no captured destination orbit means no boundary to insert an arrival hold at; the body-fixed entry/descent already self-anchors to the live rotation and lands at the correct geographic site on loop, so only the approach-to-entry seam misaligns.
- **Porkchop-style dv-optimal window planning** - evaluated in the 2026-05-28 survey and deliberately not needed by the congruent-window model (recorded tof + synodic spacing; M-MIS-3 adds geometry-aware tof centering, still not a porkchop grid).
- **Grand tours / multi-destination single missions** (land-on-every-body challenge flights) - joint faithful recurrence across many transited bodies is effectively never; the accepted loop behavior is faithful replay plus whatever per-leg alignment M-MIS-6/7 provide. No whole-tour alignment is planned.
- **Crew rotation / tourism as DELIVERABLES** - the mission loop renders a crew ferry fine today; counting kerbals as route cargo (crew manifests, rotation credit) is logistics-roadmap territory (`docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` section 19, added by PR #1113), not a Missions milestone.
- **Off-world construction launches** (Extraplanetary Launchpads-class mods: vessels rolled out from a base instead of KSC) - modded compatibility tier; revisit only on demand.

---

## Done 2026-06-09 - TS Fly canary never ran: SetVessel reflection probe used a nonexistent one-arg signature (branch `fix-ts-fly-canary-probe`)

The manual-only in-game canary `TrackingStationMaterializedOrbit_FlyLoadsMaterializedVessel_NotStaleSelection` (#554/#550) always skipped with "SpaceTracking selection/Fly reflection helpers are unavailable", confirmed in the 2026-06-09 isolated run (`../logs/2026-06-09_2319_pr1104-test-isolation/`). Decompiling KSP 1.12.5 `Assembly-CSharp.dll` (ilspycmd) showed the cause: stock `SpaceTracking.SetVessel` is `SetVessel(Vessel v, bool keepFocus)`; the test probed `GetMethod("SetVessel", ..., new[] { typeof(Vessel) }, ...)`, which has no match. `selectedVessel` and `BtnOnClick_FlySelectedVessel()` exist as probed.

**Fix:** the canary now resolves `SetVessel` through `GhostMapPresence.FindTrackingStationSetVesselMethod` (widened to `internal`; prefers the two-arg stock signature, falls back to one-arg) and builds invoke args via the already-tested `BuildTrackingStationSetVesselArguments`. The graceful skip is kept for genuinely missing members and now names which probe failed. Note: decompile shows `SetVessel` has a same-frame re-entry guard (`lastSetVesselFrame == Time.frameCount`); the canary's ghost-focus call is prefix-blocked (original body skipped), so the follow-up materialized-vessel call still passes the guard. Unit tests: 2 new direct resolver tests in `GhostTrackingStationPatchTests`. In-game verification: pending next Tracking Station test session (run Isolated; the canary is `AllowBatchExecution=false`).

## Done 2026-06-09 - Logistics Tier-1: Mission / Route structure-list window aka the Log window (0.10.1, PR #1107 / M-MIS-0)

**Feature (roadmap Phase 13 Tier-1, first bullet; now M-MIS-0):** a popup that lists a run step by step (launch, staging / separation, dock, undock, deliveries, terminal), each with its time, status (vessel situation), and location (always "SOI/body, biome" order), complementing the Missions-tab composition tree. One reusable window covers both a mission (Missions-tab "Log" button, first in the header group) and a supply route (Logistics route-detail "Log (Route)" + "Log (Mission)" buttons next to Rename; the latter opens the source mission's log).

**Implementation:** two pure, headless-tested builders feed a reusable IMGUI sub-window. `MissionStructureListBuilder.Build(tree, structure)` flattens the cached `MissionStructure` (root launches + branch-point dock/undock/decouple/eva/breakup events + terminal legs) and supplements it with debris-staging `PartEvents` (`Decoupled` / `FairingJettisoned` / `ShroudJettisoned`), de-duplicating a `Decoupled` event against a controlled Separation branch point by **decoupler part PID**, and cross-recording duplicates of one physical staging by (pid, eventType) with a **5s UT tolerance** (UT-tolerant, NOT UT-blind: a craft-baked PID re-staged hours later by a Re-Fly fork in the same tree is a distinct event and survives; recordings iterate in RecordingId order so the surviving representative is save/load-stable). Staging Status/biome honesty: the owning recording's start context is used only within 30s of the recording start, else Status blanks and Location keeps the segment-stable body only. A post-sort `CollapseSimultaneous` pass folds identical same-instant events (0.25s window, head-anchored) into one "xN" row (e.g. "Shroud jettisoned x4"), confirmed against collected logs (`logs/2026-06-09_2135_mission-log-dups`: staging=17/20 per mission from same-frame multi-shroud/decoupler separations). `RouteStructureListBuilder.Build(route, sourceLookup)` emits Origin -> Dock -> Delivery(per stop) -> Undock from `Route.Origin` / `IsKscOrigin` / `RecordedDockUT` / `Stops` plus the dock-member recording's `RouteConnectionWindow`; the source recording is resolved through an injected `Func<string,Recording>` so the builder stays free of the store singleton. `StructureListWindowUI` (owned by `ParsekUI`, drawn in KSC + Flight) renders a scrollable Time / Event / Status / Location / Vessel table (header reserves the scrollbar gutter so columns align with the scrolled rows) reusing the existing opaque-window + resize + input-lock scaffolding (`SpawnControlUI` pattern). Per-step location is the coarse body + biome / launch-site / terminal context; per-step coordinate resolution from `TrajectoryPoint`s is deferred.

**Notes:** read-only over already-recorded data, no capture / scheduler / serialization / route-model change, nothing runs per frame except the window draw while open. `StructureListWindowUI` is allowlisted in `scripts/ers-els-audit-allowlist.txt` for the by-id dock-member resolve (physical connection-window proof, not a visibility-scoped enumeration; same rationale as `MissionsWindowUI` / `TimelineWindowUI`). `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth` bumped by one header-button width so the looped-period label still fits; the Logistics "Next" delivery column widened 90 -> 135.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/MissionRouteStructureList.cs` (read model + both builders + location formatter + simultaneous-collapse), `Source/Parsek/UI/StructureListWindowUI.cs` (renderer), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/StructureListRuntimeTests.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/StructureListBuilderTests.cs` (14 cases), plus button wiring in `UI/MissionsWindowUI.cs` + `UI/LogisticsWindowUI.cs`, ownership in `ParsekUI.cs`, host draws in `ParsekFlight.cs` + `ParsekKSC.cs`. Plan: `docs/dev/plan-structure-list-window.md`.

## Done 2026-06-08 - Bug 1 (funds-economy-divergence): a stock contract re-fire baked N copies of the reward into the ledger

**Symptom (log-verified):** a single contract completion fired the stock award sequence 4 times within 22 ms (and a second contract 3 times), and Parsek recorded a `ContractCompleted` row per fire. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-08_2110_funds-bug/KSP.log`. `KSP.log:17201, 17227, 17250, 17271` (19:15:43.089-.111): four `Awarding 63250 funds to player for contract completion` STOCK lines for ONE contract (`1eb2baf9-afce-48c7-82d6-364dae85f57a`, "Science data from surface of The Mun"), live funds 305131 -> 494881. `KSP.log:17225, 17247, 17269, 17289` (`AddEvent: ContractCompleted ... total=33..36`): four store rows, same contractId / UT 475409.6 / recordingId tag. At commit those convert to four `ContractComplete` ledger rows (4 x 63250 = 253000).

**Root cause:** Parsek faithfully emits one `ContractCompleted` event per stock `Contract.onCompleted` fire (`GameStateRecorder.OnContractCompleted`, subscribed via `GameEvents.Contract.onCompleted`). Parsek never calls `Contract.Complete()` and no Parsek Harmony patch touches the award path, so the re-fire is STOCK / external re-entrancy (each repeat re-emits the full stock banner + a fresh stock `ContractOffered`); the precise stock trigger is NOT pinned (the log does not capture it). The carried resource events DID coalesce (`GameStateStore.AddEvent` collapses same-type/same-tag resource deltas within `ResourceCoalesceEpsilon = 0.1s`), but `ContractCompleted` is not a resource event so it was not coalesced; `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvents` had no intra-batch dedup and `DeduplicateAgainstLedger` only dedups candidates against the EXISTING ledger, so all four survived and `Ledger.AddActions` appended them blindly. The no-recorder direct path (`OnKscSpending`) was equally vulnerable.

**Fix (branch `fix-funds-economy-divergence`):** DEFENSIVE observation-time de-dup (no stock cause-fix; Parsek does not own the stock contract system). (1) **Recorder debounce (primary chokepoint).** New pure helper `GameStateRecorder.IsDuplicateContractCompletion(contractGuid, ut, lastSeenByGuid, window)` returns true (suppress) when the same guid completed within `window` (= `GameStateStore.ResourceCoalesceEpsilon`, 0.1s, now `internal const`), otherwise records `lastSeenByGuid[guid] = ut` and returns false. A static `lastContractCompletionUtByGuid` map mirrors the `PendingMilestoneEventById` precedent and is cleared via a new `ClearContractCompletionDedup(reason)` called from `Subscribe()`, `Unsubscribe()`, and `ResetForTesting()` (NO `onGameSceneSwitchRequested` hook), so a legitimate re-completion in a different session / timeline is not suppressed. `OnContractCompleted` calls the helper at the TOP and RETURNs before BOTH the `Emit` store write AND the `ShouldForwardDirectLedgerEvent -> OnKscSpending` direct forward, covering both inflation paths; a single Info "DEDUPED" line logs the drop. Scope is `ContractCompleted` only (the only observed re-fire / positive-reward inflation; ContractFailed/Cancelled left as a possible follow-up, not gold-plated). (2) **Converter belt-and-suspenders (§3.2a).** `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvents` now tracks converted contract-lifecycle actions by `(Type, ContractId, UT-bucket)` (bucket = floor(UT / `ResourceCoalesceEpsilon`)) within the batch and skips a duplicate, logging a summary count, so even a pre-existing burst already in the store cannot double-bake at the single commit chokepoint.

**Limitation:** recordings / ledgers already inflated by a past burst stay as-is (immutable, matches the no-modify-recordings rule); they are not repaired by this fix, and the original burst's extra payouts already hit live funds in real time (a separate, explicitly-authorized save repair if ever wanted). Bug 2's symmetric uplift clamp independently STOPS the inflated ledger from re-inflating live funds further on a future non-authoritative recalc (it caps a too-high target down to live), but it does NOT undo the past live inflation.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameStateStore.cs` (`ResourceCoalesceEpsilon` promoted to `internal const` as the single source of truth), `Source/Parsek/GameStateRecorder.cs` (`IsDuplicateContractCompletion`, `lastContractCompletionUtByGuid`, `ClearContractCompletionDedup`, `OnContractCompleted` debounce, Subscribe/Unsubscribe/ResetForTesting clears), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/GameStateEventConverter.cs` (intra-batch contract-lifecycle dedup + summary log), `Source/Parsek.Tests/ContractCompletionDedupTests.cs` (`IsDuplicateContractCompletion_*`: first-seen / within-window / outside-window / different-guid / null-guid), `Source/Parsek.Tests/GameStateEventConverterTests.cs` (`ConvertEvents_DuplicateContractCompletedSameUt_ConvertsOnce` + distinct-contracts + far-apart re-completion). Plan: `docs/dev/plans/fix-funds-economy-divergence.md`.

## Done 2026-06-08 - Bug 2 (funds-economy-divergence): a plain scene change silently REFUNDED a facility-upgrade spend (asymmetric drawdown guard)

**Symptom (player-reported, log-verified):** the player upgraded a facility (live funds 517386 -> 66387), then a normal SPACECENTER -> EDITOR scene change refunded most of the spend. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-08_2110_funds-bug/KSP.log`. `KSP.log:164416` `FundsChanged -451000 (StructureConstruction) -> 66387`; `KSP.log:166417` `RecalculateAndPatch: drawdown-guard authoritativeReduction=False (rewinding=False, reFlyMarker=False, mergeJournal=False, tombstone=False, rewindResAdjust=False)` (no time-travel authority); `KSP.log:166422` `PatchFunds: 66386.5 -> 415466.3 (delta=349079.8, target=415466.3)` (the refund). The SAME recalc clamped reputation DOWN (`KSP.log:166423` `PatchReputation: GUARDED DRAWDOWN clamped ... clampedTo=71.61`), capturing the asymmetry in one frame.

**Root cause:** the "keep what you earned" drawdown guard (the entry below) was DOWNWARD-ONLY. `IsGuardableDrawdown(running, live, eps) = running < live - eps` fires only when the ledger running balance is BELOW live and `ApplyDrawdownGuard` floored the target UP to live. When the player spends on a facility, `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvent` returns null for `StructureConstruction` `FundsChanged` (only the two Bail-Out-Grant strategy reasons convert), so the spend is patched as a facility LEVEL change but never enters the funds ledger as a spending. The ledger funds model is therefore structurally `running > live` after any facility spend, and the asymmetric guard did nothing in that direction: `PatchFunds` applied the full upward delta and refunded the spend. `PatchScience` / `PatchReputation` share the same `ApplyDrawdownGuard` call shape and the same upward hole.

**Fix (branch `fix-funds-economy-divergence`):** made the no-authority guard SYMMETRIC on the same running-balance discriminator (NOT a blanket clamp-to-live, which would re-enable a legitimate reservation). New pure predicate `KspStatePatcher.IsGuardableUplift(running, live, eps) = running > live + eps` mirrors `IsGuardableDrawdown`. `ApplyDrawdownGuard` gained a 2-out overload `(out bool clamped, out ClampDirection direction)` (`enum ClampDirection { None, Up, Down }`); the existing 1-out signature is kept as a thin delegating wrapper so the existing `DrawdownGuardTests` call sites compile unchanged. Logic when `!authoritativeReduction`: `running < live - eps` -> clamp UP to `max(target, live)`, direction Up (UNCHANGED, incl. flagging clamped even when target>live); `running > live + eps` -> cap DOWN to `min(target, live)`, direction Down, flagging clamped ONLY when the value actually LOWERED (`min < target`) so a partial-reservation-on-top-of-a-leak no-op does not emit a misleading WARN/toast; otherwise unchanged (reservation: running at live, target below live -> written through). The authoritative path is untouched, so a genuine time-travel restore still moves funds either way. `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp` takes a `direction` and logs `GUARDED UPLIFT clamped ... spent value held` (vs `GUARDED DRAWDOWN clamped ... earned value preserved`); a dedicated `fundsUpliftClampToastShownThisSession` latch (+ science/rep analogs, reset in `ResetDrawdownGuardSessionLatches`) toasts "Held your funds at the spent value" once per session independently of the drawdown latch. All three `Patch*` sites pass `out direction` and branch the toast/latch on it. This bounds FUTURE non-authoritative recalcs; it does NOT claw back funds the original spend / a prior burst already applied live (immutable past).

**Safety invariant preserved (plan §2.5):** the DOWN clamp is correct only because two existing gates guarantee live is ground truth on every non-authoritative recalc: the patch-deferral gate (`LedgerOrchestrator.GetKspPatchDeferralReason` defers the patch entirely while a recording / uncommitted-or-pending tree is in flight, so stock earnings reach live in real time and never hit a clamp) and the cold-load deferred-seed wait (`PatchFunds` early-returns on `!HasSeed`). A future change that lets a commit-time recalc fire while the ledger genuinely LEADS live (an earning Parsek recorded that stock did NOT apply live) must re-evaluate this guard.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`IsGuardableUplift`, `ClampDirection`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard` 2-out overload + 1-out wrapper, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp` direction wording, uplift latches), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (`DrawdownGuard_RefundLeak_ClampedDownToLive`, `DrawdownGuard_ScienceRunningEqualsLive_NoSpuriousDownClamp`), `Source/Parsek.Tests/DrawdownGuardTests.cs` (`IsGuardableUplift_*`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard_RunningAboveLive_*`, `Reservation_RunningEqualsLive_TargetBelowLive_NoUpliftClamp`, science/rep down-clamp facts, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp_Funds_Down_WarnsWithUpliftWordingAndToastsOnce`). Extends the downward-only "Recalc-patch drawdown guard" entry (2026-06-07) below to symmetric. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/fix-funds-economy-divergence.md`.

## Done - BUG-H (2026-06-07 vessels-disappearing): a stock Revert silently deleted the player's REAL landed/orbiting craft from unrelated missions

**Symptom (player-reported):** after a normal forward-play flight, hitting stock Revert (Esc -> Revert to Launch / Prelaunch, NOT a Parsek rewind) made several of the player's real, separately launched vessels vanish from the save. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-07_2312_vessels-disappearing/KSP.log`; the 21:49:46 Revert-to-Prelaunch (reverting the fresh mission `L4-B2-U1-S8`) logged `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels: removed 7 vessel(s)` (`R3-B2-U1-S7` LANDED, `R2-B2-S5` ORBITING, `R.2-S.3`, `R.1-S.3`, `R.1-S.2` x2, `R.1-S.1` SPLASHED) - all real craft from unrelated prior missions. Pre-strip `saves/c1/persistent.sfs` had 8 vessels; the live save dropped to 3.

**Root cause (`persistentId` is craft-baked, NOT launch-unique - see CLAUDE.md):** on a stock Revert, `RevertDetector` arms `RevertKind`, `ParsekScenario.OnLoad` collects the `VesselName` of EVERY committed recording with `SpawnedVesselPersistentId != 0` into a GLOBAL name set, and `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels` removed any flightState protoVessel whose `vesselName` was in that set (matcher was NAME ONLY, skipping only PRELAUNCH + ghost-map). ProtoVessels carry the craft-baked name/pid, which KSP reuses on every launch of a design, so a real, separately launched craft was indistinguishable from a recording's spawned vessel and got deleted on ANY revert that loaded a quicksave containing it. Cross-checking the 7 by launch Guid: 6 had `SpawnedVesselPersistentId` == live pid but a CONCLUSIVE Guid MISMATCH (a different launch wrongly deleted); the 7th (`R3-B2-U1-S7`, pid 364626662) was a real vessel Parsek had legitimately ADOPTED (`SpawnedVesselPersistentId == VesselPersistentId`, Guid match) but from an unrelated mission. The adoption path itself (`VesselSpawner.MaterializedSourceVesselExists` -> `VesselLaunchIdentity.LiveVesselIsRecordedLaunch`) was already Guid-gated; the STRIP threw that gating away by keying on name, and `ReconcileSpawnStateAfterStrip` keyed on bare pid.

**Fix (branch `bug-h-revert-vessel-strip`):** two corrections plus a centralized guid-aware deletion predicate so no strip/cleanup path can match a relaunch of the same craft. (1) **Launch-Guid gate.** New `VesselLaunchIdentity.LiveVesselIsRecordedSpawn` (genuine Parsek spawns use a KSP-unique spawn pid -> pid match conclusive; adoption stamps reuse the craft-baked pid -> require the launch Guid to not conclusively differ) + `CandidateMatchesRecording` / `FindMatchingRecording`. Every deletion routes through the centralized pure predicate `ParsekScenario.ShouldStripVesselForRecordings`, which resolves the candidate's pid + `Vessel.id`/`ProtoVessel.vesselID` Guid (the stale "ProtoVessel doesn't expose pid" comment was wrong and is removed) and only strips on a same-launch match. A conclusive Guid mismatch is NEVER stripped. (2) **Scope to the reverted flight.** The stock revert events fire with the state being left, not the target, so `RevertDetector` now captures the revert-target vessel pids from `FlightDriver.PreLaunchState` (Prelaunch) / `PostInitState` (Launch) `GameBackup.Config` (`ExtractFlightStateVesselPids`: GAME -> FLIGHTSTATE -> VESSEL[] persistentId) as a pre-existing whitelist; the revert strip removes only vessels NOT in that whitelist (i.e. they appeared during the reverted flight) and FAILS CLOSED (strips nothing) when the whitelist is unavailable.
