This protects the legitimately-adopted same-launch vessel (the 7th) that a pure Guid gate alone would still delete. `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels` was rewritten to take the committed recordings + flags + whitelist; both callers updated (revert: matchSource=false, requireWhitelist=true; rewind: matchSource=true, requireWhitelist=false to preserve the rewind contract - genuinely future-timeline vessels are still removed via the launch-identity match plus the existing `StripFuturePrelaunchVessels` pid-whitelist pass). The whitelist is applied as a protect-set whenever supplied (not just on revert): the rewind path passes `RewindContext.RewindQuicksaveVesselPids` so a vessel that pre-existed the rewind point is never deleted even for the rare guidless adoption-stamp recording where the Guid gate falls back to pid-only (adversarial-review follow-up; `requireWhitelist=false` keeps identity-only behaviour when the quicksave pids are absent). `ReconcileSpawnStateAfterStrip` gained a guid-aware overload (a surviving same-pid DIFFERENT-launch vessel no longer keeps a recording's spawn state alive); the revert reconcile routes through it. `ParsekFlight.CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels` (OnFlightReady belt-and-suspenders for FLIGHT->FLIGHT launch revert) now uses the same predicate + scope instead of name/pid recovery. `ShouldStripFuturePrelaunch` audited: pid-whitelist-based (keep-if-present), not in the defect class, behaviour unchanged. Tests: `VesselLaunchIdentityTests` (spawn/adoption/source matchers), `RevertVesselStripTests` (pid-collision-different-Guid not stripped; same-launch adoption protected by scope; genuine during-flight spawn stripped; fail-closed; rewind matchSource contract; guid-aware reconcile; `ExtractFlightStateVesselPids` parser), and in-game `RuntimeTests.RevertStrip_LiveGuidGate_ProtectsDifferentLaunch`. Note: recovering the already-deleted vessels in save `c1` is a separate manual repair, not part of this code fix.

**Known residuals (from two adversarial Opus reviews; accepted, not blockers):** (a) Fail-closed trade-off - when the revert-target snapshot is unavailable the revert strip removes NOTHING, which trades a rare contamination risk (a genuine Parsek-spawned orphan persisting into the next quicksave, the original #109/#110 concern) for never deleting a real vessel; this is the deliberate data-safe direction. (b) `RecordingStore.PreProcessRewindSave` still strips the rewind-target `.sfs` by NAME (`removedByName`) - the same defect class, but narrowly scoped to one `BuildRewindStripNames(owner)` (not the global set) and operating on the rewind-target save rather than the live save, so far lower risk; left as a follow-up to migrate onto the same launch-identity predicate. (c) The OnFlightReady cleanup can consume a stale whitelist across a prelaunch-revert -> EDITOR -> relaunch sequence; benign because the Guid gate is the real backstop (a fresh launch's fresh Guid will not match an adoption-stamp recording).

## Done - BUG-F (2026-06-07 career-load regression): cold-loading an established career wiped the stock economy (funds to seed, science to 0)

**Symptom (player-reported):** loading the `c1` career save (build 0.10.1, all recent fixes merged) collapsed funds to 20095 (= seed 25000 - 4905 spent) and science to 0, with NO Parsek feature in use. The live save was overwritten on first cold-load. New-session log: `logs/2026-06-07_1934_career-load-regression/KSP.log`; pre-wipe backup `Kerbal Space Program/saves/c1_backup_pre_fix_20260607` (funds 72906, sci 1.0).

**Root cause (latent, not a 0.10.0->0.10.1 regression):** the load-time ledger recalc applies a "current-UT cutoff" that filters committed actions to the live game clock (built for post-rewind / future-timeline saves so future rewards are not paid out early). During a cold `ScenarioModule.OnLoad` the universe clock is not yet initialized, so `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` returns 0; the load passes `maxUT=0`. `LedgerOrchestrator.OnKspLoad` then took the cutoff path because `HasActionsAfterUT(0)` is true (every committed action is after UT 0), filtering 141 of 144 actions and patching funds/science down to the seed (`Current-UT ledger recalculation: reason=ksp-load cutoffUT=0` -> `PatchFunds: 72906 -> 20095`, `PatchScience: 1.0 -> 0.0`). The `DeferredSeedAndRecalculate` coroutine that was supposed to re-seed correct values fired with the same UT=0 (it waited for resource singleton VALUES, which were already loaded, not for the clock) and re-confirmed the wipe (`reason=deferred-seed cutoffUT=0`). The 0.10.0 session (`logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/`) only looked fine because that load had an empty ledger (`before=0, validRecordingIds=0` -> `HasActionsAfterUT(0)=false` -> safe full replay); both builds ran identical code with `maxUT=0, preserveFutureTimelineActions=True`. The in-session FLIGHT->FLIGHT load path was already guarded (`ShouldUseCurrentUtCutoffForPostRewindFlightLoad` checks `planetariumReady`); only the cold-load `OnKspLoad` + `DeferredSeed` paths were unguarded.

**Fix (branch `bug-f-coldload-wipe`, PR #1092):** added `LedgerOrchestrator.IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff(double ut) => ut > 0.0` and gate every load-time cutoff/prune decision on it. (1) `OnKspLoad` (`LedgerOrchestrator.cs`) applies the current-UT cutoff only when `useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions && IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff(maxUT) && HasActionsAfterUT(maxUT)`, otherwise falls back to the safe full replay (`RecalculateAndPatch`, cutoffUT=null) that replays every committed action; logs an `OnKspLoad recalc decision` line. (2) Both `Ledger.Reconcile` calls now pass `preserveFutureTimelineActions: useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions || !currentUtReady`, so a not-ready clock preserves all committed rows regardless of scene. This closes a sibling catastrophe found in review: a cold-load into a NON-cutoff scene (TRACKSTATION / EDITOR, where `useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions` is false) at maxUT=0 would otherwise let Reconcile PERMANENTLY PRUNE the whole career's spend history (not just mis-patch it). (3) The shared `RecalculateAndPatchForCurrentTimelineIfFutureActions` helper got the same guard (in-session callers pass a valid UT via `GetCurrentTimelineUTForLedgerRecalc`, so only the not-ready path changes - belt-and-suspenders against any future caller passing UT<=0). (4) `DeferredSeedAndRecalculate` (`ParsekScenario.cs`) now adds a bounded Phase-3 wait for the universe clock to report a positive UT before deciding, then routes through the guarded helper; a timed-out wait falls back to full replay. The per-frame clock poll reads through `TryReadReadyUniverseTime`, which wraps `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` in a try/catch (it can throw during very early load - same precedent as `Update()`), so a throw cannot kill the coroutine. This preserves the legitimate post-rewind case: a valid positive UT with committed actions still ahead of it keeps the cutoff (future rewards stay filtered). Tests: `IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff_*` predicate; `OnKspLoad_ColdLoadWithUnreadyClock_ReplaysEntireCareer_NoWipe` (the regression test: maxUT=0 -> full replay, actionsAfterCutoff=N, no `reason=ksp-load` cutoff); `OnKspLoad_ColdLoadNonCutoffScene_PreservesCareerRows_NoPrune` (the prune sibling); `OnKspLoad_ReadyClockWithFutureActions_StillAppliesCutoff` (post-rewind case still cuts off); `OnKspLoad_ReadyClockPastAllActions_ReplaysFullLedger` (guard does not over-trigger); `RewindUtCutoffTests.CurrentTimelineIfFutureActions_NotReadyClock_ReplaysFullLedger` (shared helper guard); plus the existing `OnKspLoad_WithFutureLedgerActionsAndCurrentUtCutoff_RecalculatesAtLoadUt`.

**Follow-up (NOT in this fix, separate save/ledger repair):** after BUG-F lands, the `c1` save recalcs back only to its pre-wipe state (sci ~1.0, funds ~72906); fully restoring the lost Mun science (~124.8 - a BUG-A symptom) is a separate save repair.

## Done 2026-06-07 - Recalc-patch drawdown guard (defense-in-depth, BUG-A follow-up)

**Source:** The anticipated BUG-A follow-up (see the BUG-A entry below: "a defense-in-depth guard that refuses a large negative drawdown when no rewind/re-fly is active is a sensible follow-up but was not needed to fix the root cause"). Plan: `docs/dev/plans/recalc-patch-drawdown-guard.md`.

**What it does:** When a ledger recalc would patch live funds / science / reputation DOWN past the per-resource rounding epsilon (funds 0.01, science 0.001, rep 0.01) AND no time-travel context is active, the patch is CLAMPED so the player's value is preserved (`max(patchTarget, currentLive)`), a single session-scoped native `ParsekLog.ScreenMessage` ("Kept your earned funds/science/reputation") is posted per resource, and a WARN with the full numbers fires on every guarded recalc. Always on, no setting.

**Predicate (Blocker 2 / plan §3.3):** The guard keys on the NON-RESERVED running balance (`FundsModule.GetRunningBalance` / `ScienceModule.GetRunningScience` / `ReputationModule.GetRunningRep`), NOT the reservation-aware patch target (`GetAvailableFunds` / `GetAvailableScience`). A reservation legitimately lowers `available` below `running` on cutoff walks (committed future spends), so keying on the target would defeat overspend prevention; a missing-earning leak lowers `running` itself below live. Reputation has no reservation, so its running balance IS its target. Per-subject science (`PatchPerSubjectScience`) stays unclamped (a documented limitation called out in the pool clamp WARN, MINOR 5).

**Authoritative-reduction bypass (five signals, plan §3.2):** the clamp is suppressed when any of `RewindContext.IsRewinding`, `ParsekScenario.Instance.ActiveReFlySessionMarker != null`, `ParsekScenario.Instance.ActiveMergeJournal != null`, the tombstone path (`RecalculateAndPatchAfterTombstones` -> `tombstonePath: true`), or the NEW `RewindContext.RewindResourceAdjustmentInProgress` is set. The fifth signal (Blocker 1) is the ONLY one true at the deferred plain-Rewind-to-Launch authoritative recalc (`ApplyRewindResourceAdjustment` -> `RecalculateAndPatch(adjustedUT)`): it is set synchronously in `HandleRewindOnLoad` before `StartCoroutine`, cleared in the coroutine's try/finally around that patch (authoritative), and cleared as a race-free fail-safe in the next scene's `ParsekScenario.OnAwake` (NOT a blanket scene-switch clear, which would race the coroutine's ~2s singleton wait).

**Plumbing:** `RecalculateAndPatchCore` computes `authoritativeReduction` from the five signals and threads it (plus a new `tombstonePath` Core param) through `ApplyRecalculatedStateToKsp` -> `KspStatePatcher.PatchAll` -> `PatchScience` / `PatchFunds` / `PatchReputation`, parallel to the existing `suppressSuspiciousDrawdownWarnings`. The legacy log-only `IsSuspiciousDrawdown` 10% WARN is untouched.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`IsGuardableDrawdown`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard`, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp`, session-scoped toast latches, three patch methods), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/LedgerOrchestrator.cs` (`IsAuthoritativeReduction`, Core/Apply threading), `Source/Parsek/RewindContext.cs` (signal 5 + Begin/End + ResetForTesting), `Source/Parsek/ParsekScenario.cs` (HandleRewindOnLoad arm, coroutine finally, OnAwake fail-safe, save-boundary latch reset), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (live clamp + signal-bypass test), `Source/Parsek.Tests/DrawdownGuardTests.cs`.

**Status:** Fixed for v0.10.1. Full xUnit suite green (14559, +25). In-game validation pending: a clean career playtest must produce ZERO guarded clamps; a deliberately-leaked / forced-too-low ledger must clamp + preserve live + toast on funds/science/rep; a real rewind / re-fly / tombstone reduction must still apply (authorized). Run `RuntimeTests.DrawdownGuard_ClampsLeakAndAuthorizesSignal` (Ctrl+Shift+T, SPACECENTER) to verify the live patch path.

## Done - Rewind read-back divergence guard (audit rec #1, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §8)

**Source:** Recommendation #1 (highest leverage, most self-contained) of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit. At the Rewind-to-Separation apply boundary, detect (loudly log; optionally abort) when the recalc would write the career economy BELOW the real career economy, turning a silent career-corruption clobber into a caught, logged event.

**Design - two-witness "economy floor", downward-only, realized-vs-realized.** The §6 oracle premise was CORRECTED: the loaded quicksave is the OLD at-RP economy, NOT the live-tip the recalc targets, so a naive "target vs quicksave" check false-flags every healthy rewind (legit post-RP earning/spending), and the `authoritativeReduction` flag is true at this boundary (ReFly marker armed) so it cannot be used to excuse the drop. Instead the guard captures TWO independent witnesses of the real career economy and flags only when the recalc's realized target falls below BOTH: `E_before` (live funds/science/rep captured in `RewindInvoker.StartInvoke` BEFORE `GamePersistence.LoadGame`, parked on the surviving `RewindInvokeContext`) and `E_rp` (live economy captured post-load in `RunStripActivateMarker` immediately before the recalc = the loaded quicksave economy). `floor = min(E_before, E_rp)` per resource (finite witnesses only). The min-floor structurally encodes legit drawdown (post-RP spending lowers `E_before`) and absorbs uncommitted-in-flight effects (#466: older quicksave `E_rp` approximately equals target, so floor = `E_rp`, no false flag), so the guard does NOT gate on `authoritativeReduction` (but logs it). Compared against the recalc's REALIZED running value: funds `GetRunningBalance()`, rep `GetRunningRep()`, science the SAME pending-adjusted running value `PatchScience` uses (extracted into `KspStatePatcher.ComputePendingAdjustedRunningScience` and called from both so they are byte-identical). `FlaggedDivergence iff target < floor - tolerance` (downward only; upward restore is Verbose-only); a NaN/Inf target is itself corruption -> FlaggedDivergence; no finite witness -> NotEvaluated (logged skip). Per-resource absolute tolerances `funds 1.0 / science 0.1 / rep 0.1` (a touch looser than the patch no-op epsilons).

**Default = warn-only, never alters a successful rewind.** Abort is opt-in via `RewindReadbackGuard.AbortRewindPatchOnDivergence` (default OFF). When abort is enabled and a divergence is flagged, `PatchAll` early-returns before the `Patch*` dispatch (crew roster already applied by `kerbalsModule.ApplyToRoster`; loaded quicksave economy values stand). The guard is armed only for the post-load recalc and cleared in a `finally` so it never leaks onto an ordinary recalc patch.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/RewindReadbackGuard.cs` (new: `EconomySnapshot` struct + `RewindReadbackGuard` holder), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`RewindReadbackVerdict`, pure `ResolveRewindDivergence`, `RunRewindReadbackGuard`, `ComputePendingAdjustedRunningScience` extraction, PatchAll wiring + tolerances), `Source/Parsek/RewindInvokeContext.cs` (`ReadbackPreRewind` runtime-only field + Clear), `Source/Parsek/RewindInvoker.cs` (E_before capture + arm/finally-clear), `Source/Parsek.Tests/RewindReadbackGuardTests.cs` (20 tests), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (`RewindReadbackGuard_WarnsOnDivergence_LeavesLiveUnchanged`, warn-only).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green except the known `InjectAllRecordings` environmental flake (KSP.log lock). In-game validation pending: run `RuntimeTests.RewindReadbackGuard_WarnsOnDivergence_LeavesLiveUnchanged` (Ctrl+Shift+T, FLIGHT) to confirm the WARN fires and live values are untouched; a real healthy rewind should log only within-range / Verbose lines (no FLAGGED DIVERGENCE).

## Done - Per-identity logging at the apply boundary (audit rec #2, gaps 1-3, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §4.2)

**Source:** Recommendation #2 of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit: promote the three HIGH-risk per-identity logging gaps from Verbose-only to the default (Info) apply line so a per-subject-science / tech-node / contract corruption is diagnosable from a normal `KSP.log`, not only Verbose.

- ~~**Gap 1 - per-subject science (`KspStatePatcher.PatchPerSubjectScience`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries a bounded `changedSubjects=[subjectId:old->new, ...]` clause (old read before the write), full list at Verbose.
- ~~**Gap 2 - tech-node availability flips (`KspStatePatcher.PatchTechTree`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries bounded `madeUnavailableIds=[...]` (the dangerous re-lock direction, listed first) and `madeAvailableIds=[...]` clauses, full lists at Verbose. (The `...Ids` suffix keeps the identity-list clauses distinct from the existing `madeAvailable=`/`madeUnavailable=` count fields on the same line.)
- ~~**Gap 3 - contract remove/restore (`KspStatePatcher.PatchContracts`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries bounded `removedIds=[...]` (targeted removal keys, current set before finished set) and `restoredIds=[...]` clauses, full lists at Verbose.

**Mechanism:** shared pure formatter `KspStatePatcher.ComposeBoundedIdentitySample(list, cap=10)` returns `string.Empty` for a null/empty list (steady-state Info lines stay byte-identical), joins under the cap, and appends ` (+N more)` over the cap; each clause is appended only when the sample is non-empty. Contract removed-identity derivation is the pure `DescribeRemovedContractIdentities`. Logging-only, no schema/serialized-field change.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (formatter + `DescribeRemovedContractIdentities` + the three Info-line clauses + paired Verbose full-list lines), `Source/Parsek.Tests/KspStatePatcherTests.cs` (6 pure-helper tests).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green except the known `InjectAllRecordings` environmental flake (KSP.log lock).

## Done - xUnit apply-boundary tests (audit rec #5, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §5.1 layer (e) / §5.3 risk 1-3)

**Source:** Recommendation #5 of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit. `KspStatePatcherTests` run with `SuppressUnityCallsForTesting = true`; the real mutation sites sit behind `if (Funding.Instance == null) return;` / `ResearchAndDevelopment.Instance == null` / `Reputation.Instance == null`, so under xUnit every "apply" test hit the early-return and only the pure target-computation helpers + null-guard logging were covered. The compute-delta -> clamp -> no-op / write decision (the code that actually writes funds / science / per-subject science / reputation / tech tree / facility levels) was exercised live by only 2 in-game tests with synthetic inputs.

**Approach (Option A - extract the numeric core, no runtime behavior change).** Each `Patch*` wrapper now delegates its "given currentValue + target, produce the delta / clamp decision and the resulting value" logic to an `internal static` PURE function that takes the live value as a PARAMETER instead of reading the KSP singleton. The thin Unity-call wrapper (read singleton -> call pure core -> apply result via AddFunds / AddScience / SetReputation / SetTechState / SetLevel + read-back + logs) is unchanged in behavior. Verified behavior-preserving: every pre-existing test passes unchanged. Option B (an injectable economy seam) was assessed and rejected - the only semantic the audit flagged as a possible Option-B trigger (the drawdown guard's running-vs-available distinction) is already plumbed as the two pure parameters `runningBalance` / `target` that `ApplyDrawdownGuard` takes, so Option A captures it directly.

This branch was rebased onto the `0.10.1` apply-boundary stack (rec #4 LedgerTrace #1100, rec #3 ground-truth #1102, and the SYMMETRIC drawdown guard #1101): the pure cores now compose the symmetric guard and the wrappers keep both the up/down latch+toast and the LedgerTrace Tier-C read-back hook.

**Pure cores extracted:**
- `KspStatePatcher.ResolveFundsPatch` / `ResolveSciencePoolPatch` / `ResolveReputationPatch` (result structs `*PatchDecision`): compose the existing SYMMETRIC `ApplyDrawdownGuard` (the 2-out overload returning a `ClampDirection` Up/Down/None) + `IsSuspiciousDrawdown` primitives into the full decision (clamp keyed on the running balance in BOTH directions, the `ClampDirection` carried on the decision so the wrapper picks the up vs uplift session latch + toast, delta against the post-clamp target, 0.01 / 0.001 no-op gate, clamp->no-op collapse, suspicious >10% flag, the float-cast boundary for science, the Set-not-Add absolute semantics for rep). The DOWN (uplift) direction is the #1101 Bug-2 path that holds the spent value when the ledger leads live without time-travel authority.
- `KspStatePatcher.ResolveSubjectSciencePatch` (struct, audit gap 1 - the HIGH-risk path): the UNCLAMPED per-subject science - target written verbatim even on a drawdown, scientificValue = 1 - target/cap (cap>0) floored at 0. A regression test fails the instant anyone adds a `max(current,target)` clamp here.
- `KspStatePatcher.ClassifyTechNodeForPatch` (enum `TechNodePatchAction`, audit gap 2): the node-set 2x2 (MakeAvailable / AlreadyAvailable / MakeUnavailable / AlreadyUnavailable); the live wrapper resolves `currentlyAvailable` per branch from the proto / static tech state and dispatches the mutation.
- `FacilityStatePatcher.ResolveFacilityLevelPatch` (struct, audit gap 4): the ledger-tier -> KSP-level map (`ToKspFacilityLevel`) + the level-change gate, catching the off-by-one of comparing a ledger tier directly against a zero-based KSP level.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (5 pure cores + result structs/enum, 5 wrappers rewired), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/FacilityStatePatcher.cs` (1 pure core + struct, level loop rewired), `Source/Parsek.Tests/KspStatePatcherApplyBoundaryTests.cs` (new, 31 tests; each asserts the computed delta AND the resulting value AND, for the clamp sub-path, the WARN log line via `TestSinkForTesting` - including the symmetric Up/Down `ClampDirection` and the #1101 Bug-2 uplift hold).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green (14784). Pure testability refactor: no gameplay change, no schema / serialized-field change. The live AddFunds / AddScience / SetReputation / SetTechState / SetLevel write + read-back stays covered by the existing in-game `RuntimeTests`; the in-game ground-truth harness (audit rec #3) remains the separate follow-up for the full live round-trip.
## Done - LedgerTrace: event-driven ledger-apply tracer (audit rec #4, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §7 + §8 rec 4)

**Source:** Recommendation #4 of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit: a gated, EVENT-DRIVEN ledger-apply tracer modeled on the render tracer (`MapRenderTrace.cs`) but adapted to discrete recalc events (no per-frame MonoBehaviour probe), so career-corruption bugs are traceable from `KSP.log`. Landed after rec #2 (per-identity logging) so Tier-B reuses, not duplicates, the #1098 changed-sets.

- ~~**Gate (`ledgerTracing` setting):**~~ DONE. New off-by-default `ledgerTracing` flag mirrors `mapRenderTracing` across all of `ParsekSettings.cs` (field + `[CustomParameterUI]`), `UI/SettingsWindowUI.cs` (Diagnostics toggle + defaults-reset + record call), and `ParsekSettingsPersistence.cs` (key + field + load/load-summary/Save/save-summary/`ApplyTo`-restore/`RecordLedgerTracing`/`ResetForTesting`/`GetStored`/`SetStoredForTesting`). The persistence layer is the OnSave/OnLoad durability path (the flag rides KSP's GameParameters deserialize like `mapRenderTracing`; no `ParsekSettings.OnSave/OnLoad` line needed). `LedgerTrace.IsEnabled = ForceEnabledForTesting || ParsekSettings.Current.ledgerTracing`.
- ~~**Tier-A structural (`EmitStructural` -> Info, one per recalc):**~~ DONE. `LedgerOrchestrator.ApplyRecalculatedStateToKsp` calls `LedgerTrace.BeginRecalc()` at entry (bumps the owned `recalcSeq`, clears the Tier-B steady-state dict) and `EmitStructural` ONCE after `PatchAll` returns (never inside a Patch* -> no 7x double-emit; the patch-deferral gate returns before this method so deferred recalcs emit nothing). The grep-stable snapshot (`funds/science/rep/facilities=[name:level]/techNodes/contracts/cutoff/authReduction`) is built from module getters + the local `targetTechIds`/`techPatchCutoff`/`authoritativeReduction` (no direct `Ledger.Actions` / `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings` read - ERS/ELS rule).
- ~~**Tier-B change-based (`EmitOnChange` -> Verbose):**~~ DONE. Per-identity change lines at the five Patch* sites: per-subject science (`PatchPerSubjectScience`), tech-node availability flips (`PatchTechTree`), facility levels (`FacilityStatePatcher.PatchFacilities`), and contracts (`PatchContracts`). Four of these reuse the existing #1098 changed-sets (`changedSubjects` / `madeUnavailableIds`+`madeAvailableIds` / `removedIds`+`restoredIds`); facilities are the ONLY NEW changed-set (a local `LedgerFacilityChange` list at the `SetLevel` site, since facilities had no #1098 set). The owned `lastValueByKey` dict is the secondary steady-state guard. Milestones (gap 6) are DEFERRED from Tier-B v1 (a one-line code comment marks it at the milestone patch site; the Prompt-4 enumeration omits milestones and they have no #1098 set).
- ~~**Tier-C anomaly (`EmitAnomaly` -> Warn, `ledger-vs-truth`):**~~ DONE. After each live write the patcher reconciles the computed target against the read-back via pure Unity-free predicates (`IsResourceDrift` / `IsSubjectScienceDrift` / `IsFacilityLevelMismatch` / `IsTechNodePresenceMismatch` / `IsContractPresenceMismatch`). Funds/science/rep reuse the already-read after-value (no second read); per-subject science checks the UNCLAMPED gap-1 write; tech-node and contract read-backs (`GetTechnologyState` / live-contract-guid set) are guarded by `IsEnabled` so the extra KSP calls only run when tracing. NaN/Inf semantics mirror `RewindReadbackGuard`: NaN/Inf actual -> not flagged (no trustworthy read-back); NaN/Inf target -> flagged (a corrupt computed target IS the bug). Tolerances reuse the Patch* no-op deltas (funds 0.01, science 0.001, rep 0.01).

**Mechanism:** self-contained `LedgerTrace.cs` (gate, owned `recalcSeq` + `lastValueByKey` lifecycle, pure predicates, the three tier emitters, and formatters DUPLICATED from `MapRenderTrace` - not shared, per the render-tracer convention). Every emit early-returns on `!IsEnabled` AND each call site is wrapped in `if (LedgerTrace.IsEnabled)`, so a disabled tracer costs one bool. No detailed-window registry (no per-frame stream to window), no MonoBehaviour probe (the read-back reconcile runs synchronously inside each Patch*).

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/LedgerTrace.cs` (new), `Source/Parsek/ParsekSettings.cs`, `Source/Parsek/UI/SettingsWindowUI.cs`, `Source/Parsek/ParsekSettingsPersistence.cs` (the `ledgerTracing` flag), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/LedgerOrchestrator.cs` (Tier-A BeginRecalc + EmitStructural + snapshot builder), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (Tier-B/C in PatchScience/PatchFunds/PatchReputation/PatchPerSubjectScience/PatchTechTree/PatchContracts + the milestone deferral comment), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/FacilityStatePatcher.cs` (the new facility changed-set + Tier-B/C), `Source/Parsek.Tests/LedgerTraceTests.cs` (45 tests).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green except the known `InjectAllRecordings` environmental flake (KSP.log lock).

## Done - In-game ledger ground-truth verification harness (audit rec #3, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §5.2/§6, design `docs/dev/design-ledger-groundtruth-harness.md`)

**Source:** Recommendation #3 of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit: the closed rewind/recalc-vs-actual-save loop that did NOT exist. §5.2 showed there was no end-to-end test reconstructing career state and comparing it to a ground-truth save (incl. vessels); the only in-game check, `TopBarReflectsLedgerAfterRecalc`, is circular (module-getter vs live-singleton AFTER patch, a tautology). §6 noted the natural oracle: a real KSP save serialized at the current UT holds the actual economy + vessels, and nothing read it back to verify the recalc agrees.

**Design - two layers; NON-CIRCULAR comparison.** Layer A (pure, headless, xUnit-tested): `CareerSaveParser.Parse(ConfigNode)` parses a `.sfs` GAME node INDEPENDENTLY of the ledger into a `CareerSaveSnapshot` (funds, science pool + per-subject, reputation, facility level fractions, active + all-state contract guids, completed + all milestone ids built by a recursive qualified-id `Progress` walk, and the VESSEL set with per-resource totals summed across parts); `LedgerGroundTruthDiff.Compare(save, recon, tolerances, facilityMaxLevels)` diffs it against a `LedgerReconstructionSnapshot` read off the recalc modules and returns a structured `LedgerDivergenceReport`. Layer B (in-game): `LedgerGroundTruthHarness.VerifyReconstructionAgainstGroundTruthSave` (`[InGameTest(Category="LedgerGroundTruth", Scene=FLIGHT)]`) quicksaves the live career to a dedicated slot, parses it via Layer A, runs `LedgerOrchestrator.RecalculateAndPatch()`, reads the reconstruction from the RAW running readers (`GetRunningBalance`/`GetRunningScience`/`GetRunningRep` - NOT the reservation-aware `GetAvailable*`, matching the production rewind read-back guard and bypassing drawdown-guard masking), and diffs the two. This compares recalc output to KSP's OWN on-disk serialization, not module-vs-live-after-patch, so it is non-circular.

**Facet policy (mixed-history-safe).** HARD failures = the seeded pools (funds/science/reputation, within tolerance) + a guid-corroborated vessel-recovery consistency violation (a recovered vessel must be ABSENT from the save). The per-identity facets (per-subject science, facilities, contracts, milestones), phantoms, pid-only recovery (craft-baked-pid caveat), and vessel parse-sanity are REPORT-ONLY by default, because the player's real career is mixed-history (Parsek installed partway) so the delta-only modules legitimately differ from KSP's full history; `LedgerGroundTruthDiff.StrictPerIdentityForTesting` promotes ALL report-only divergences to hard for a clean test career. Every facet is still compared and emitted to the structured report (Warn-logged); the hard-fail subset is the one that cannot legitimately diverge on a real career. Guards (Skip): non-career, any null pool singleton, and the full deferral set (`HasPendingTree || HasActiveUncommittedTree() || HasLiveRecorder()` - when a live/pending tree exists the save would include uncommitted state). Live pools restored in a `finally`; `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution=true` gives a batch reload backstop. ERS/ELS routing honored (recovery scan via `ComputeELS()`, recording resolution via `ComputeERS()`).

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/LedgerGroundTruth.cs` (data types + `LedgerDivergenceReport`), `Source/Parsek/CareerSaveParser.cs`, `Source/Parsek/LedgerGroundTruthDiff.cs`, `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/LedgerGroundTruthHarness.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/LedgerGroundTruthParserTests.cs` + `LedgerGroundTruthDiffTests.cs` (31 pure parser/diff tests).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green (14686). In-game validation pending: load a career, enter FLIGHT, STOP recording, Ctrl+Shift+T, run the `LedgerGroundTruth` category. A healthy career passes (per-identity divergences are report-only Warn lines); a corrupted pool fails with the structured per-facet report in `parsek-test-results.txt` + `KSP.log`.

## Done 2026-06-07 - BUG-G: tech-purchase affordability gate contradicted the drawdown guard AND blocked destructively (double science loss)

**Source:** 2026-06-07 career playtest, `logs/2026-06-07_2110_tech-purchase-bug/KSP.log` (~lines 13027-13045). Pure-stock play, no Parsek feature used. The player had live science 124.8 but Parsek blocked a 45-cost tech unlock as "insufficient science" AND the science was deducted anyway, twice (`ScienceChanged -45.0 -> 79.8`, block, `ScienceChanged -45.0 -> 34.8`, block; ~90 science lost, no node unlocked). This is the missing OTHER HALF of the drawdown guard above: the guard preserves live above a leaked ledger running balance, but the affordability gate read the leaked ledger value.

**Two facets.**

**Bug 1 (gate vs guard inconsistency):** `LedgerOrchestrator.CanAffordScienceSpending` / `CanAffordFundsSpending` computed `available` from the ledger (`GetAvailableScience` / `GetAvailableFunds`). With a missing-earning leak (running below live, no time-travel context, no reservation: `futureActions=0` in the log) `available` was 1.0 while the drawdown guard had preserved live at 124.8, so the gate blocked a purchase the player could afford. Fix: new pure helper `LedgerOrchestrator.ComputeEffectiveAffordable(available, running, live, authoritativeReduction)` returns `authoritativeReduction ? available : available + max(0, live - running)`, adding back exactly the guard-preserved leak gap while a GENUINE reservation (`available < running`) still reduces spendable below the leak-corrected base (so it is NOT a plain `max(available, live)`, which would defeat overspend prevention). The live wrappers apply it only when the KSP singleton exists (real game); xUnit keeps the pure-ledger contract so the existing reservation/cutoff `CanAfford*` tests stay authoritative. `IsAuthoritativeReductionForAffordability` reads the same five drawdown-guard signals (tombstonePath=false).

**Bug 2 (block was destructive):** stock `RDTech.ResearchTech` deducts science (`host.AddScience(-scienceCost, RnDTechResearch)`) and ONLY THEN calls `UnlockTech`, so the prior `UnlockTech`-prefix block fired AFTER the deduction and returned false without refunding (silent loss). The facility equivalent is the same: `SpaceCenterBuilding.UpgradeFacility` deducts funds then calls `SetLevel`. Fix: gate BEFORE the deduction. New `TechResearchSpendPatch` (prefix on `RDTech.ResearchTech`) and `FacilityUpgradeSpendPatch` (prefix on `SpaceCenterBuilding.UpgradeFacility(bool)`) run the block pre-deduction; returning false skips the original entirely (no deduction, node/level unchanged, `RDController.ActionButtonClick` discards the result and `RefreshUI` re-reads the unchanged state). The shared decision lives in `TechResearchPatch.TryBlockTechResearch(tech, includeAffordability)` / `FacilityUpgradePatch.TryBlockFacilityUpgrade(facility)`. The post-deduction `UnlockTech` / `SetLevel` prefixes are kept as non-destructive backstops for direct callers and now block COMMITTED items only (the destructive affordability re-check was removed from `UnlockTech`).

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/LedgerOrchestrator.cs` (`ComputeEffectiveAffordable`, `IsAuthoritativeReductionForAffordability`, both `CanAfford*` wrappers), `Source/Parsek/Patches/TechResearchPatch.cs` (`TryBlockTechResearch`, UnlockTech committed-only backstop), `Source/Parsek/Patches/TechResearchSpendPatch.cs` (NEW), `Source/Parsek/Patches/FacilityUpgradePatch.cs` (`TryBlockFacilityUpgrade`), `Source/Parsek/Patches/FacilityUpgradeSpendPatch.cs` (NEW), `Source/Parsek.Tests/SpendingGateConsistencyTests.cs` (NEW), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (`SpendingGate_RespectsLiveAndBlocksNonDestructively`).

**Status:** Fixed for v0.10.1. Full xUnit suite green (14596 pass; only the environmental `InjectAllRecordings` flake fails when KSP holds the install). In-game validation pending: run `RuntimeTests.SpendingGate_RespectsLiveAndBlocksNonDestructively` (Ctrl+Shift+T, SPACECENTER); also confirm in a real R&D scene that a leaked-ledger career can still buy affordable nodes and that any block leaves science/funds unchanged. Note: the affected `c1` save was repaired by hand (ledger seeds bumped so running matches live); this fix prevents recurrence + stops the destructive block, it does not heal saves.

## Done - BUG-B (2026-06-07 career playtest): Parsek auto-spawned ghosts, map icons, and duplicate recorded vessels during a normal playthrough (no rewind/playback used)

**Symptom (player-reported):** a Parsek ghost icon was visible in map view, and Parsek spawned then re-recovered real vessels named after recordings, during a pure-stock career where NO Parsek feature (rewind, re-fly, loop, preview) was used. Bug list + 76 MB log: `logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/BUGS.md` (BUG-B).

**Root cause:** the ghost-playback engine (`ParsekFlight.UpdateTimelinePlaybackViaEngine`, every frame) and the Space Center path (`ParsekKSC`) evaluate every committed recording purely by comparing the live game UT to the recording's recorded window. Per the README "How It Works", a recording replays (and spawns its terminal vessel) only AFTER the player rewinds to before it, so its window lies in the player's forward path again. There was no gate distinguishing that from normal forward play, where KSP's UT only advances, so every committed recording's window is already historical the moment it is committed. The engine therefore treated "live UT > recorded end" as "playback finished" and fired `PlaybackCompleted` -> terminal-vessel spawn for every spawnable recording (the log shows `needsSpawn=True` with `ghostWasActive=False`, an impossible combination for a genuine replay), while orbital recordings whose recorded/extrapolated END runs ahead of the live UT (e.g. `R2-B2-S7` recUT=[203566.8,210582.4] at liveUT ~203585) rendered a live ghost + map icon of the player's still-orbiting vessel. The duplicates were re-recovered each scene by `CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels`, and the auto-spawned terminal-orbit vessels are the UPSTREAM trigger for BUG-C's terminal-orbit spawn-death / abandonment churn: BUG-C signatures 2-3 (`R2-B2-S5` abandoned 3x; fresh-rollout craft-baked-pid mis-identification) are fallout of this auto-spawn and are removed at the root once historical recordings stop auto-spawning, while BUG-C signature 1 (NaN debris -> stock `FlightIntegrator` throw) is pure stock KSP and unaffected. (The earlier "orphan-recovery refunds feed BUG-A's funds clawback" hypothesis was investigated separately and RULED OUT: those recoveries fired for unrelated `R.1` vessels and BUG-A's -47840 was dropped Mun-firsts milestone funds, not recovery credit.)

**Fix (branch `bug-b-ghost-autospawn`):** new `PlaybackScopeTracker` per-recording latch keyed by recordingId. A recording enters "replay scope" the first frame the live playhead is observed at or before its activation-start UT (the post-rewind case). The discriminant keys on the recording's START, which stays behind the playhead during forward play even when the orbital-extrapolated END runs ahead, so the orbital-icon case is caught too. A recording NOT in scope, whose window the playhead only ever moved forward through/past, is `HistoricalNotReplayed`: flight `ComputePlaybackFlags` sets `skipGhost` (new `GhostPlaybackSkipReason.HistoricalNotReplayed`, reusing the existing skip-render path so there is no ghost and no deferred map presence) and `needsSpawn=false` (no policy terminal spawn); `ParsekKSC` suppresses the non-loop render and the playback-disabled past-end spawn. Looping / chain-loop / mission-unit members (explicit live-replay opt-in) and the active re-fly session are exempt and keep rendering. Rewind-to-launch naturally re-arms scope (the playhead drops below the target's start); a rewind to a LATER launch correctly leaves earlier recordings historical (a single global "replay active" flag would get this wrong, which is why the latch is per-recording). The gate is wired in all three ghost-rendering scenes: flight (`ComputePlaybackFlags` -> skipGhost + needsSpawn=false), Space Center (`ParsekKSC` non-loop render + disabled past-end spawn), and Tracking Station (icon path: `GhostMapPresence.ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore`, gated on `batch != null` so only the live create / lifecycle paths are affected and the pure `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSource` predicate keeps its old behaviour; spawn path: the per-frame `TryRunTrackingStationSpawnHandoffs` driver also skips the historical terminal-vessel spawn, exempting the adoption case where a matching live vessel is still present, while the explicit "Warp to Spawn" action `TryRunTrackingStationSpawnHandoffForIndex`/`ForRecordingId` stays ungated as a deliberate user action). Tests: `PlaybackScopeTrackerTests` (pure discriminant incl. orbital-extrapolation, rewind-to-later-launch, and tolerance-boundary cases) + three `FlightPlaybackExplainabilityTests` end-to-end cases (historical -> skip + no spawn, rewound-into-scope -> renders + spawns, looping -> exempt).

Known limitations / residual edges (all OUTSIDE the reported no-Parsek-feature case, which is fixed unconditionally): (1) the in-memory latch is keyed by recordingId and cleared only on main-menu transition, so it survives a quickload (F9). A replay paused mid-flight and quickloaded reverts its recordings to historical (benign: a replay stops); conversely a quickload to a forward-play state AFTER a rewind keeps the stale in-scope mark, so the rewound recordings can render again until the next main-menu cycle. (2) On the single frame a Mission first begins looping, `ComputePlaybackFlags` reads the previous frame's `cachedLoopUnits` (rebuilt after the flag pass), so a mission-unit member can flicker its ghost for one frame before re-rendering. (3) Flight exempts `loopingLike` from the historical flag while the KSC playback-disabled past-end branch does not, so a `LoopPlayback=true` + `PlaybackEnabled=false` recording is gated at the Space Center but not in flight; the suppress-during-forward-play behaviour is the more correct of the two. (4) FIXED (2026-06-11, branch `fix-timejump-scope-latch`): discrete time-jump latch race. The scope latch was per-frame only, so a discrete UT jump (`TimeJumpManager.ExecuteJump` / `ExecuteForwardJump`) could cross a recording's activation start before any per-frame `NotePlayhead` sweep observed the pre-jump playhead (a recording committed and warped past within the same frame), misclassifying a legitimately-ahead recording as historical and silently suppressing its end-of-recording real spawn. Hit by the Real Spawn Control warp-to-end path (the `RealSpawnControl_WarpToRecordingEnd_OnPad_DoesNotAutoStartLaunchRecording` canary failed in every Isolated run since BUG-B landed: the synthetic recording's spawn was suppressed as `historical-never-replayed`, so no situation-change flicker occurred inside the suppression window and `skipCount` stayed 0). Fix: `TimeJumpManager.NotePlayheadSweepBeforeJump` observes the playhead one final time at the PRE-jump UT (routed through `EffectiveState.ComputeERS()`) before `SetUniversalTime` in both jump paths, latching any still-ahead recording into replay scope. Tests: `TimeJumpManagerTests.NotePlayheadSweepBeforeJump_*` (ahead-window latch, true-historical not rescued, already-latched, null/missing-id counting, empty/null list).

## BUG-C (2026-06-07 career playtest) - `R2-B2` tree instability + NaN debris -> stock exceptions

Source: `logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/` (KSP.log, `BUGS.md` BUG-C section). Build `Parsek V0.10.0` @ `07dea8fac`. The player used NO Parsek features this session (no rewind / re-fly / loop / playback); Parsek was only background-recording. Three log signatures, separable root causes. BUG-C is largely fallout of BUG-A (ledger recalc) and BUG-B (passive ghost / vessel auto-spawn), which are tracked separately.

### 1. NaN debris -> stock `FlightIntegrator.UpdateOcclusionSolar` throw - STOCK KSP, not Parsek data (no fix)

Two `ArgumentOutOfRangeException` throws in stock `FlightIntegrator.UpdateOcclusionSolar` (KSP.log lines 205423 @15:46:42, 218683 @15:50:46), each immediately around `R2-B2M-S6 Debris had a NaN Orbit and was removed` + an on-rails Kerbin->Sun SOI transition.

Origin is **pure stock physics**, confirmed:
- `R2-B2M-S6 Debris` (pids 1333358833 / 2800168062) is the player's **real staging debris**, created at 15:42:22 by a real decouple (`Decouple created vessel during recording ... rootPart=radialDecoupler`), with real drag cubes, terrain collision (`crashed through terrain on Kerbin`), and explosions. It is NOT a Parsek ghost/spawn: line 204856 `CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels: no match for 'R2-B2M-S6 Debris'` is Parsek explicitly disclaiming ownership.
- Parsek background-recorded the debris and then **finalized + deleted** those recordings as non-persistable (`canPersist=False`, `DeleteRecordingFiles`) at 15:42:39, ~4 minutes before the NaN. No Parsek recording carried or authored the NaN orbit.
- The throw is the well-known stock pattern: debris clips through terrain, is packed on rails with a degenerate velocity, the resulting hyperbolic orbit escapes Kerbin->Sun, and `UpdateOcclusionSolar` indexes a body list off a NaN-derived value and throws before stock's own NaN-orbit removal runs.

Decision: do **not** Harmony-patch stock `FlightIntegrator` to swallow this. It is not Parsek data, it reproduces without Parsek, and guarding a stock NaN path from a mod is high-risk for little gain (the proper home for a stock-bug shim is KSPCommunityFixes). Filed as known-stock, no Parsek code change.

### 2. Terminal-orbit ghost "permanently abandoned" 3x - BUG-B fallout + a real durability gap (FIXED here)

`[Policy] Spawn-death detected for terminal orbit and will not be retried: #32 "R2-B2-S5" ... reason=spawned-terminal-orbit-vessel-died` fires 3x (15:46:17, 15:56:43, 15:58:58), each with a fresh Parsek-spawn pid (3390689712 / 3495642311 / 3732877540) and `deathCount=1`.

Traced each cycle: `SpawnAtPosition: vessel spawned (ORBITING, body=Sun, alt~13.4 Gm)` -> Parsek's own `CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels: recovering 'R2-B2-S5' (matched by name)` immediately recovers it -> `RunSpawnDeathChecks` sees it gone -> `MarkCannotSpawnSafely`. The spawn itself is **BUG-B**: Parsek auto-materializes a committed terminal-orbit `vessel`-type recording during passive play, then orphan-recovers it.

The durability gap (the part fixed here): `RunSpawnDeathChecks` sets `Recording.TerminalSpawnCannotSpawnSafely = true` ("will not be retried"), and `VesselSpawner.SpawnOrRecoverIfTooClose` (`VesselSpawner.cs:1688`) honours that flag as a pre-spawn guard. But the flag was **transient** (`Recording.cs`, "do not serialize"), so every scene reload reset it to false and the vessel re-spawned. The first spawn each session happens before the flag is set, and `TryPassTerminalOrbitSpawnSafety`'s live orbit-geometry re-check passes (a 13.4 Gm heliocentric coast is geometrically "safe"), so only the recorded spawn-death can stop it - and that was being forgotten.

Fix: persist `TerminalSpawnCannotSpawnSafely` + `TerminalSpawnSafetyReasonCode` so the abandon survives a reload, on BOTH load paths. (1) Cold start (fresh game load, `RecordingStore.ClearCommittedInternal` then `LoadRecordingTrees`): the `RecordingTreeRecordCodec` save/load (`SaveMutablePlaybackState` / `LoadRecordingResourceAndState`) round-trips the keys when the committed trees are rebuilt from disk. (2) In-session load (scene change / quickload / revert, the `returned-scene-change` branch of `ParsekScenario.OnLoad`): that path reconciles the in-memory committed recordings instead of rebuilding them - it resets every recording's terminal spawn-safety via `TerminalOrbitSpawnSafety.Clear` (~line 2320) then restores only the saved subset, so the new `ParsekScenario.RestorePersistedTerminalAbandon` re-applies the flag from the saved RECORDING node (absent on a revert quicksave, so the abandon correctly does not carry across a revert). Either way the flag is true on the next scene, so the existing `VesselSpawner.cs:1688` pre-spawn guard blocks the re-spawn and the "will not be retried" log becomes truthful across reloads. The observed 3x repro went through path (2), so the codec change alone would not have fixed it. The soft altitude-deferred hold (`TerminalSpawnSafetyDeferred`) is deliberately left transient so it re-evaluates against the propagated orbit. Tests: `RecordingTreeTests.RecordingTree_TerminalSpawnCannotSpawnSafely_RoundTrips` / `RecordingTree_NoTerminalSpawnAbandon_StaysFalseOnLoad` (codec path) + `SpawnStateReconciliationTests.RestorePersistedTerminalAbandon_*` (in-session path). This is defense-in-depth; the upstream cure (don't auto-spawn during passive play at all) is BUG-B. Note: each orphan recovery runs a stock vessel-recovery (`Recovery processing captured ... recoveryFactor=...`), a candidate contributor to BUG-A's funds drift - flagged for the BUG-A session.

### 3. Active-tree save skipped - correct-by-design merge-consent guard, root is BUG-B-adjacent identity collision (no fix here)

`[Scenario] SaveActiveTreeIfAny: skipped active tree 'R2-B2-S5' because at least one recording could not be written with current v0 sidecars` + `skipped dirty sidecar save for committed-restore overlap recording 'bb53...'` (lines 165907-165925, 15:04).

This is the merge-consent guard in `SaveActiveTreeIfAny` (`ParsekScenario.cs:1380-1390`): a dirty recording that is an `IsCommittedTreeRestoreAttemptRecordingId` (and not a marker-owned switch segment) is skipped to avoid overwriting committed history before merge consent. **No committed sidecar is corrupted**, and in this log only one recording was dirty (the overlap clone `bb53...`, 1 buffered point), so there is no meaningful new-data loss - the guard behaved correctly.

The real defect is upstream and BUG-B-adjacent: the active tree was created by `TryRestoreCommittedTreeForSpawnedActiveVessel` treating the player's **fresh-rollout real vessel** `R2-B2-S5` (pid 590316933) as a committed-spawned-clone. This is the documented craft-baked-`persistentId` collision (a new launch of the same craft reuses the baked pid that prior committed recordings of that craft also carry). The fresh-rollout fast-path ("matches captured scene-entry pid") correctly skipped restore at 14:55, but after the 15:04 scene reload the captured scene-entry pid no longer matched and it fell through to committed-tree restore - routing a normal flight into the re-fly merge-consent path. The correct cure is launch-identity (`RecordedVesselGuid` / `VesselLaunchIdentity`) discrimination at the restore site, which belongs with BUG-B / the identity subsystem, not the save guard. No safe save-path change here.

Latent secondary (noted, not fixed): `SaveActiveTreeIfAny` early-returns and skips the WHOLE active-tree node when any one recording is a committed-restore overlap, even if a legitimately-new marker-owned switch-segment recording in the same tree had its sidecar written - that would orphan the sidecar (no tree node references it). Not triggered destructively in this log; flagged for the switch-segment owner.

---

## Done 2026-06-07 - BUG-A: scene-change recalc wiped stock career science + funds earned after a time-warp (career-corruption)

**Source:** 2026-06-07 long career playtest (`logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/`), pure-stock play, no Parsek feature used. On return to the Space Center: `[KspStatePatcher] PatchScience: 124.8 -> 1.0 (delta=-123.8)` wiped all Mun science, and `[KspStatePatcher] PatchFunds: suspicious drawdown delta=-47840.0 ... earning channel may be missing` clawed back the Mun world-first funds. Recurred 5x across the session with growing magnitude as the loss compounded (each recalc replays the whole ledger from seed).

**Root cause:** A Mun mission recording (`3ec1090f...`, `R3-B2-U1-S7`) recorded trajectory only for its 143s pre-time-warp launch window (`[203697.7, 203840.7]`); the on-rails warp to the Mun emits no per-frame `TrackSection`s, so `Recording.EndUT` (derived from `TryGetActualTrajectoryBounds`) stopped at 203840.7 even though the recorder stayed live and tagging until UT 241435.9. All Mun-phase career captures (10 science subjects, the `Mun/Flyby` / `Mun/Landing` / `Suborbit` / `Mun/Science` milestones with their progression funds/rep) were captured at UT 234349-241406 and tagged to `3ec1090f...`, but the two ledger converters dropped them purely because their `captureUT` fell past the stale trajectory window:
- `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertScienceSubjects` -> `TryResolveTaggedScienceWindowStart`: a tagged subject whose `captureUT > endUT` returned false -> `skippedOutsideWindow=10` (`converted=0 from 10 subjects`).
- `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvents`: the UT-range check ran before the tag-scope check, so all 45 tagged Mun events were `outOfRange=45` (`converted=0`), losing the milestone funds (the entire -47840).

The committed ledger for `3ec1090f...` therefore had `science=0` and no Mun milestone funds. On the scene-change `RecalculateAndPatch`, `KspStatePatcher` computed a target excluding those legitimate earnings and patched live science/funds DOWN to match. The "suspicious drawdown" guard is log-only (it WARNs but still applies `AddScience` / `AddFunds`), and `PostWalkActionReconciler.ReconcilePostWalk` is log-only too, so neither protected captures that were never converted into actions in the first place.

**Why the recalc patched down during pure-stock play:** `RecalculateAndPatch` runs on every recording commit / scene change to keep KSP state in sync with Parsek's ledger (the same mechanism that applies time-travel deltas). Its invariant is "ledger mirrors live," so with no time-travel the patch should be a no-op (delta ~ 0). It only patched down because the ledger was missing legitimately-earned channels (this conversion bug). The fix restores ledger correctness so the patch is a no-op; a defense-in-depth guard that refuses a large negative drawdown when no rewind/re-fly is active is a sensible follow-up but was not needed to fix the root cause.

**Fix:** The recording's `[StartUT, EndUT]` trajectory window is a heuristic for attributing UNTAGGED captures only; a capture explicitly tagged to the committing recording is authoritatively owned by it (the tag was set at capture time when that recording was the live recorder). The fix is asymmetric to preserve the #528 pre-start rule:
- `TryResolveTaggedScienceWindowStart` still rejects tagged captures BEFORE `StartUT` (#528 stale launchpad science with a drifted tag), but now keeps tagged captures AFTER `EndUT`, anchored at `EndUT`.
- `ConvertEvents` now bypasses the upper bound for events tag-scoped to the committing recording (`recordingId` non-empty AND `evt.recordingId == recordingId`); the lower bound and untagged / cross-recording filtering are unchanged, so whole-store conversions (empty `recordingId`) keep both bounds. Double-counting is prevented by the existing committed-science max-merge, `DeduplicateAgainstLedger`, and post-commit `PruneProcessedEvents`.
- `ReconcileEarningsWindow` / `ComputeEarningsWindowStoreDeltas` apply the same tag-ownership upper-bound rule on the store side, so the #394 / #440B earnings reconciler stops firing a false "missing earning channel" WARN on exactly the time-warp-gap commit the converters were fixed to handle. A genuinely unmatched late tagged delta (no emitted action) still WARNs, and cross-recording late events stay excluded.

**BUG-B cross-link:** ruled OUT as the funds-mismatch driver. The orphan ghost-vessel recoveries (`CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels`) fired at 15:58 for unrelated `R.1` vessels, long before the 16:35 return; the -47840 corresponds exactly to the dropped Mun-firsts milestone funds (the ledger UNDERcounting legitimate stock earnings), not orphan recovery inflating live funds.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/GameStateEventConverter.cs`, `Source/Parsek/GameActions/LedgerOrchestrator.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/GameStateEventConverterTests.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/EarningsReconciliationTests.cs`.

**Status:** Fixed for v0.10.1. Full xUnit suite green (14534).

## Done - Log spam audit of the 2026-06-07 career playtest (top three per-frame offenders)

The `logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/KSP.log` was 363,790 lines, 94.8% Parsek output, 327,667 of them `[VERBOSE]`, despite the session doing no re-fly and having no supply routes. Full ranked family report: `docs/dev/log-spam-audit-2026-06-07.md` (analyzer: `logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/_spam_analyze.py`). Fixed the three highest-volume families (logging-only, no runtime-behavior change), ~236,600 lines / ~65% of the whole log:

- `ReFlySettleStabilityTracker.RecordFloatingOriginShift` (185,303 lines, ~56% of all verbose). `FloatingOrigin.setOffset` fires nearly every physics frame the world re-centres; the non-settle branch logged `Verbose` unconditionally. The shift STATE is still recorded unconditionally (it feeds `LastFloatingOriginShiftFrame`, read by the GhostRenderTrace large-delta detector); only the LINE changed. Settle-window branch still INFO-emits every shift; non-settle branch is now a 30s shared-key `VerboseRateLimited` heartbeat, message built lazily so suppressed frames pay no format cost.
- `GhostMapPresence.LogOverlapGateDecision` (48,109 lines, ~15%). The verdict is stable ("not-driven") almost always, so the old per-index 3s time limit re-emitted the same line forever for every committed recording. Now `VerboseOnChange` keyed on the stable `RecordingId` with a boolean-facet state key (cadence/span/cycle floats excluded so a driven recording still coalesces); emits only on a verdict flip.
- `RouteGhostDriverSelector.SelectGhostDrivingBackingMissions` (3,184 lines). Already 2s-rate-limited but all-zeros (no routes). Now `VerboseOnChange` on the counts tuple.

Lock-in tests: `FloatingOriginSetOffsetPatchTests.RecordFloatingOriginShift_NoSettleActivity_IsRateLimited`, `OverlapPerInstanceTests.LogOverlapGateDecision_StableVerdict_CoalescesAndReEmitsOnFlip`, `RouteGhostDriverSelectorTests.Summary_StableCounts_CoalescesAndReEmitsOnChange`. Full xUnit suite green (14,516).

Deferred follow-ups (runtime-frequency or higher-risk, see the report): trajectory sidecar re-reads (~18k lines, repeated-load driven), ledger-recompute re-walks (Funds / ScienceModule / Milestones / LedgerOrchestrator / per-module `Reset: cleared 0` lines, ~25k combined), per-save per-recording resource lines, and the `MapRender shadow frame` / `Anchor candidates` per-frame zero emits.

## Done (triage) - BUG-D: high-volume recorder-quality WARNs in the 2026-06-07 career playtest

Source: `logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/` (BUGS.md BUG-D). Player used NO Parsek features this session (background recording only), so these are recorder-side log warnings, not gameplay faults. The recordings themselves are correct; the warnings are a mix of by-design conditions and one mis-calibrated threshold. Triage verdict per family:

- **`[Recorder]/[BgRecorder] TrackSection sparse sampling largeGaps` (x123 WARN)** - REAL log mis-calibration, FIXED. The adaptive sampler's max-interval backstop (`ParsekSettings.GetMaxSampleInterval`: 8.0s Low / 3.0s Medium / 1.0s High) is the longest gap the recorder emits by design during a low-dynamics coast (`TrajectoryMath.ShouldRecordPoint` only force-samples once `elapsed >= maxInterval`). The old large-gap WARN threshold was a hard-coded 0.50s, 6x below the Medium backstop, so every coast and every parked vessel tripped it (playtest WARN maxGaps clustered right at 3.0s). Fix: `FlightRecorder.ResolveSparseGapWarningThreshold(maxSampleInterval)` returns `max(0.50s floor, maxInterval * 1.5)` and is threaded into both `ComputeSectionGapStats` call sites (active + BG) plus the logged `threshold=` field. Only a gap well past the backstop (a genuinely stalled sampler / severe frame-budget lag, e.g. the one 5.92s outlier) now warns. Pure helper unit-tested in `AdaptiveSamplingTests` (per-density thresholds, degenerate-interval floor, 3.04s coast no-warn vs 5.92s stall warn). No recorded-data behavior change.
- **`[PatchedSnapshot] solver unavailable` (x149)** - ACCEPTABLE, no change. KSP only keeps a `PatchedConicSolver` on the active vessel, so snapshotting any non-active vessel (main stages AND debris) at scene exit returns NullSolver by design. Already documented + per-vessel rate-limited (#576); the NullSolver `FailureReason` is the intended fingerprint feeding the live-orbit reseed fallback (228 successful "recovered ... live-orbit fallback" lines downstream). Confirmed none hit a piloted active vessel mid-flight (the case the WARN is deliberately kept loud for).
- **`[Extrapolator] Terminal reason=horizon-cap` (x27)** - ACCEPTABLE, no change. These are the minority outcome of the same NullSolver -> live-orbit reseed recovery: the reseeded ballistic tail found no impact / SOI event inside the look-ahead horizon and terminates as `Orbiting`, which the finalizer ACCEPTS (`FinalizerCache Refresh accepted ... status=Fresh`). Intentionally WARN alongside `degenerate-state` / `soi-transition-cap`. Latent low-priority nuance (NOT fixed, deferred): a few caps reseed sea-level debris (alt 0, ~187 m/s) and classify it `Orbiting` rather than impact; only matters if such a ghost is ever played back, and changing the reseed/scan would destabilize a working recovery path. Revisit only with a concrete playback-visible repro.
- **`[Merger] boundary discontinuity` (x12 measurable WARN)** - ACCEPTABLE, no change. All 12 have `ratio` 0.98-1.00, i.e. the position jump is fully explained by velocity x dt (cause `unrecorded-gap` or `frame-mismatch`); ZERO `sample-skip` (the genuine-bug bucket). This is the deliberate #449 "warn-with-classification" design (entangled with the #580 unrecorded-gap healer); the classifier already self-triages each line, so the WARNs are working as intended and low volume. Left as-is.

## Done - In-game test-run triage (2026-06-09 career playtest: Mission Control hang, launch clamps, logistics/TS)

Ran the full in-game suite from a real career and triaged ~13 failures (logs: `logs/2026-06-09_2014_post-testrun-investigate/`). All fixes are TEST-SIDE; no product code changed.

- **Mission Control / Astronaut Complex hang (real test-runner bug).** Three facility-row waits (`WaitForMissionControlOfferedContractRow`, `WaitForMissionControlRowOverlay`, `WaitForCrewListItemOverlay` in `RuntimeTests.cs`) used `Time.time` deadlines. Entering a facility pauses the game (`timeScale = 0`), which freezes `Time.time`, so on a save with no offered contracts the wait spun forever; the test coroutine never returned, so the player was left stuck inside the paused building and `ForceCloseOpenSpaceCenterFacilities` never ran. Decompilation confirmed `onGUIMissionControlDespawn` IS a sufficient close (the force-close was correct, just never reached). Fix: those three waits now use `Time.realtimeSinceStartup` (mirroring `WaitUntilTrue`).
- **Launch clamps held the test vessel on the pad (real robustness gap).** The career launch vessel had launch clamps in a later stage, so staging ignited the engines but never released the clamps; the vessel stayed in `PRELAUNCH` and four launch/revert/scene-exit tests timed out (10s) because the existing thrust-based skip is bypassed when a clamped craft DOES produce thrust. Fix: new `ReleaseLaunchClampsOnActiveVessel()` / `ActiveVesselHasLaunchClamps()` helpers; the two launch waits release clamps so the craft lifts off (real coverage), `RealSpawnControl_WarpToRecordingEnd_OnPad` skips when clamps are present (it must not move the pad vessel), and `LogContractTests.RecordingStopMetricsValid` exempts a never-left-pad single-point `Landed` recording from the >=2-point contract.
- **Follow-up (2026-06-09 isolated run, logs `logs/2026-06-09_2319_pr1104-test-isolation/`): clamp release alone was not enough.** The release shipped and fired (4 clamps), but the career craft's first stage is four Shrimp SRBs with marginal TWR: it burned on the pad and needed ~8s after release to leave `PRELAUNCH` (`AutoRecordOnLaunch_StartsExactlyOnce` passed at 8.5s of its 10s window; `RevertToLaunch_SoftUnstashesPendingTree_WithoutMergeDialog` and the two `ExitToSpaceCenter_Deferred*` tests timed out at exactly 10s while the craft was still creeping upward, engines burning the whole window). Fix: both launch waits (`WaitForLaunchAutoRecordStart`, `WaitForRecordingToLeavePrelaunch`) now use a 30s deadline, and the timeout outcome routes through the pure `RuntimeTests.ClassifyLaunchWaitTimeout` (xUnit `LaunchWaitTimeoutClassifierTests`): still-`PRELAUNCH` with thrust produced now Skips (clamps are already released, so only craft performance can hold it down; environmental, not a regression), still-`PRELAUNCH` with no thrust keeps the existing no-ignited-engine Skip, and a timeout after leaving `PRELAUNCH` stays a Fail (the recording-side conditions never came true). Separately, `LogContractTests.RecordingStopMetricsValid` failed on a committed single-point EVA recording in the career save ('Lars Kerman': 1 point, `terminal=null`, but a splashed `TerminalPosition`, sealed on board-back); the exemption was broadened from `IsNeverLeftPadSinglePointRecording` (terminal `Landed` only) to `IsNeverLeftGroundSinglePointRecording` (terminal `Landed`, or no terminal stamp plus a recorded surface `TerminalPosition`, which is only ever set for landed/splashed endpoints), xUnit-covered in `NeverLeftGroundExemptionTests`.
- **Follow-up 2 (2026-06-10 retest, logs `logs/2026-06-10_0011_pr1104-launchwait-retest/`): the real blocker was a zeroed throttle, not TWR.** With the 30s deadline 2 of 3 launch tests passed; `ExitToSpaceCenter_DeferredDiscardButton` failed the NEXT wait in the chain (`WaitForRecordingToClearPad`, 80m in 10s; vessel LANDED at 30.5m). Engine forensics: the craft's stage 5 holds ALL five launch engines (Swivel + 4 thrust-limited Shrimps; clamps in stage 4), yet the three manual-recording launch tests ignited only the 4 SRBs (engines=4 terminal events) while the ready-gated tests (`Quickload_MidRecording`, `AutoRecordOnLaunch`) lit the Swivel at full throttle (engines=5, `EngineIgnited liquidEngine2.v2 val=1.00`) and flew. The difference: the working tests run `InGameTestRunner.WaitForStockStageManagerReady` + `RuntimeTests.WaitForFlightInputStateReady` BEFORE writing `mainThrottle = 1f`; without them the write does not stick after a batch-baseline quickload and the liquid core idles at zero thrust (SRBs ignore throttle). Fix: the three tests now mirror the ready-gated sequence; all three launch waits (`WaitForLaunchAutoRecordStart`, `WaitForRecordingToLeavePrelaunch`, `WaitForRecordingToClearPad`) re-assert full throttle every frame via `ReassertFullLaunchThrottle` and log a "re-asserted full throttle on N frame(s)" summary when a correction fired, so any remaining zeroing source shows up as log evidence; `WaitForRecordingToClearPad` gets the same 30s deadline + thrust-aware Skip classification (classifier param renamed `stillPrelaunch` to `stillOnPad`). xUnit: `LaunchThrottleReassertTests` + updated classifier tests. Note: the craft CAN clear the pad on boosters alone (passed twice across runs), so stage-walking down to the clamp stage was not needed; it remains the fallback design if a future craft spreads its launch engines across multiple stages above the clamps.
- **Logistics delivery (2) + TS synthetic ghost (3): test/fixture, not product bugs.** The logistics deliveries correctly took the unloaded proto-snapshot path because the active pad vessel reported unloaded, while the tests assert the live `PartResource`; added a loaded+unpacked skip-guard. The TS synthetic-orbit ghost tests built a recording 60s in the past, which the BUG-B historical-never-replayed guard correctly suppresses; the fixture now anchors `startUT = currentUT` (NEEDS IN-GAME RE-VERIFY — the decisive create-path log line was rate-limited; `LoopPlayback=true` is the fallback if anchoring is insufficient).
- **Stray `.loadmeta` (real cleanup bug).** `LogisticsRouteStoreRuntimeTests` deleted its slot's `.sfs` via raw `File.Delete` but left the `<slot>.loadmeta` in the save (found in c1 after the run: `parsek_logistics_ingame_test_*.loadmeta`). Now routes deletion through `QuickloadResumeHelpers.TryDeleteSaveSlot`, which sweeps the sidecar.

**Ledger ground-truth + TopBar funds divergence — NO product bug, career safe; fixed test-side via demote-on-uplift.** `LedgerGroundTruthHarness` reported SciencePool recon=119.3 vs save=29.3 (+90), ~19 phantom milestones, and `TopBarReflectsLedgerAfterRecalc` funds off by ~123. Investigation (KSP.log recalc lines): funds and reputation reconstruct to the cent; only science over-runs, and the production drawdown guard **clamped the uplift** (`PatchScience: GUARDED UPLIFT clamped running=119.30 live=29.30 ... spent value held`, `authoritativeReduction=False`), so the live save was never over-credited. This is an artifact of running the harness against `c1` (704 accumulated recordings from many sessions) whose reconstruction legitimately exceeds a small real career; the guard is the safety net working as designed. c1's actual economy is healthy (funds dropped by a manual vessel-launch cost, science stable). The `Vessel pid-only` recovery line is the known `guidCorroborated=false` report-only facet.

Fix (owner chose demote-on-uplift; TEST-SIDE only, no production change): new `DivergenceKind.UpliftClampedExpected`; the harness recomputes the production guard's `authoritativeReduction` (via the existing `internal static LedgerOrchestrator.IsAuthoritativeReduction`, `tombstonePath: false` since tombstones never run in the harness) and threads it into the pure `LedgerGroundTruthDiff.Compare`. `ClassifySeededPoolKind` tags a seeded-pool divergence `UpliftClampedExpected` (report-only via `IsAlwaysHard`) when `recon > save + tol && !authoritativeReduction` (the uplift-clamp case); a DOWNWARD divergence (recon < save) stays a hard `ValueMismatch`, and an upward divergence WITH an authoritative context (guard does not clamp) also stays hard. `TopBarReflectsLedgerAfterRecalc` skips (rather than false-fail on both the value and one-event-per-delta assertions) when the post-patch running balance still exceeds live with no authoritative context (the clamp held the value). Four new `LedgerGroundTruthDiffTests` cover: upward+non-authoritative → report-only, downward → hard, upward+authoritative → hard, and strict-promotes-report-only. Downward save-corruption detection is preserved as hard for all three pools.

## Done - Test suite run from the main menu created a phantom save folder

Running `Run All` from the MAIN MENU (no game loaded) created a stray `saves/<lastPlayedSave>/Parsek/Recordings/` folder that lingered in the load list. With no game loaded, `HighLogic.CurrentGame` is null but `HighLogic.SaveFolder` retains the last-played save name (a 2026-06-09 playtest from the menu had it stuck at `DestructiblesTest`), so two save-I/O tests wrote into that stale folder: `SaveLoadTests.RecordingsDirectoryExists` (called `RecordingPaths.EnsureRecordingsDirectory()`, which mkdir's the tree) and `SerializationTests.VesselSnapshotRehydratesFromSidecar` (writes a `_vessel.craft` sidecar there; it deletes the file in `finally` but the created directory remained). `RecordingsDirectoryExists` already guarded on `string.IsNullOrEmpty(HighLogic.SaveFolder)`, but that is non-empty at the main menu, so the guard missed.

Fix: both tests now skip (`InGameAssert.Skip`) when `HighLogic.CurrentGame == null || string.IsNullOrEmpty(HighLogic.SaveFolder)` — the root-cause "no loaded game" signal (`ScenarioInstanceActive` uses the same check). They still run normally in any scene with a real loaded save (FLIGHT / Tracking Station / Space Center), where writing under `saves/<save>/Parsek/Recordings/` is legitimate. Audited the other in-game save-scoped writers: `LogisticsRouteStore` already skips on null `CurrentGame`, `PartPersistentIdStability` / scene-exit / ground-truth are FLIGHT/career-gated, and the remaining `ResolveSaveScopedPath` callers only READ (no mkdir/write), so these two were the only main-menu offenders. A pre-existing stray `saves/<save>/Parsek/Recordings/` from before this fix is deleted manually once.

## Done - Test runs must leave the campaign save untouched (defensive audit)

Audited every disk write the in-game test framework makes under `saves/<save>/` and closed the campaign-mutating gaps:

- **`persistent.sfs` was unprotected.** `RuntimeTests.TriggerSaveAndExitToSpaceCenter` writes `persistent` directly (used by the two scene-exit merge tests now in the isolated batch), and any scene-change auto-save also rewrites it; the baseline restore only reloaded the baseline *slot* into memory, leaving the campaign's main save dirty on disk. Fix: `CaptureFlightBatchBaseline` now backs up `persistent.sfs` to a sibling `<slot>-persistent.bak` (non-`.sfs` so it never lists as a save), and `CleanupBatchFlightBaselineSave` restores it via the atomic `FileIOUtils.SafeWriteBytes` path before deleting the backup. Defensive throughout: never throws (a failed backup just disables the revert with a warning; a failed restore keeps the `.bak` for manual recovery). Covers batch-end and cancel teardown (both route through `CleanupBatchFlightBaselineSave`).
- **Player's stock `quicksave` slot was clobbered.** `BridgeSurvivesSceneTransition` and `QuickloadMidRecordingDoesNotLoseTrajectoryState` called `TriggerQuicksave()`/`TriggerQuickload()` with no slot name (defaults to the stock `"quicksave"`). Both now use a unique `parsek-test-*` slot deleted in `finally`.
- **`parsek_ledger_groundtruth.sfs` was left behind.** `LedgerGroundTruthHarness` (runs in normal Run All) now deletes `GroundTruthSlot` in its `finally`.
- **`.loadmeta` sidecars.** `QuickloadResumeHelpers.TryDeleteSaveSlot` now also sweeps the `<slot>.loadmeta` sidecar (via `FileIOUtils.DeleteSaveSidecarLoadMeta`).

Already-safe (verified, no change): `LogisticsRouteStoreRuntimeTests` and `PartPersistentIdStabilityTest` use unique Guid slots deleted in `finally`; the baseline slot + Parsek-sidecar snapshot dir + restore/backup staging dirs are already cleaned by `CleanupBatchFlightBaselineSave` / the `using` staging scope; test-created RewindPoints + recordings live under `saves/<save>/Parsek/` which the baseline Parsek-dir snapshot swaps back to batch-start; `parsek-test-results.txt` is written to the KSP root, not the save dir.

~~Known residual (LOW, follow-up): the `persistent.sfs` revert runs at batch end / cancel (`CleanupBatchFlightBaselineSave`). If KSP is force-killed mid-batch after a test wrote `persistent.sfs` but before teardown, the campaign main save stays in the test-mutated state on next launch — the batch-start `<slot>-persistent.bak` is preserved (intentionally, for manual recovery) but there is no load-time auto-reconciler.~~ Closed by the universal-isolation crash reconcile below: a `TestBatchMarker` written into `persistent.sfs` at batch start (plus the clean `.bak`) is detected on the next OnLoad in a DIFFERENT process and auto-restored. The earlier worry that auto-restoring from an orphaned `.bak` could clobber a save the player intentionally continued after a crash is addressed by the process-mismatch + save-folder + backup-path guard (`TestBatchMarker.ShouldReconcileOnLoad`): a same-process load never reconciles, and a wrong-save marker is dropped without touching `persistent.sfs`.

**NOT YET VALIDATED IN-GAME** (no .NET/KSP toolchain here): the `persistent.sfs` backup/restore and slot-cleanup wiring are runtime-only file I/O and need a build + playtest. All paths are defensive (try/catch, atomic safe-write, preserve-on-failure) so a failure degrades to a warning rather than corrupting the campaign.

## Done - Universal test-runner campaign isolation (all scenes + cancel + crash)

Extended the FLIGHT/TS-only batch isolation to a universal, automatic, no-player-action campaign revert in any scene with a loaded game, on every exit path. Test-runner code only; no product/ledger/recalc/guard behavior changes, and the existing per-test FLIGHT/TS restore path is byte-identical (same slot, snapshot, persistent backup; `PrepareBatchFlightRestoreExecution` only reuses the already-captured baseline).

- **Universal baseline capture.** `CaptureBatchBaseline(mode)` runs at batch start from ALL FIVE entry points (`RunAll`, `RunCategory`, `RunSingle`, and the two `...IncludingFlightRestore`), not only when a `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution` test exists. The pure `ClassifyBatchIsolationMode(scene, hasGame, hasSave, hasVessel)` (unit-tested) picks the mode: FLIGHT-with-vessel / TRACKSTATION -> `InMemoryAndDisk` (quicksave slot + Parsek sidecar snapshot + clean `persistent.sfs` `.bak`); SPACECENTER / EDITOR / FLIGHT-no-vessel -> `DiskOnly` (clean `.bak` only, no in-memory reload); MAINMENU / no game / no save -> `None`. A capture failure downgrades to `None` + warn (batch still runs, no auto-revert).
- **Guaranteed final restore at batch end AND on cancel.** New `RunFinalBatchRestore` fires once at batch end when the pure `ShouldRunFinalBatchRestore(hasInMemoryBaseline, stateDirtySinceLastRestore, aborted)` (unit-tested, 8-row table) says state may have changed since the last successful restore. Correctness rests on `stateDirtySinceLastRestore`, NOT on restore-backed tests sorting last — a RunLast-after-restore (or future non-restore RunLast) test re-arms the dirty flag and produces one safe extra restore. For a plain `RunAll` FLIGHT batch (no restore-backed test) there is now exactly ONE final restore where before there was none. Cancel routes the in-memory baseline through the recovery wrapper; DiskOnly reverts `persistent.sfs` synchronously.
- **Recover-on-failure (replaces warn-and-preserve).** `RestoreBatchBaselineWithRecovery` retries the load once (skips are not retried — structural absence), and on a persistent in-memory failure forces the on-disk save back to baseline so the DISK is always correct. The two-part disk revert (`ForceRevertCampaignDiskToBaseline` -> `RestoreCampaignPersistentSave` + `RestoreParsekSidecarsFromSnapshot`) returns a `DiskRevertResult`; a fully-reverted disk gets a "load to recover in-memory" alert, a partial/failed disk takes the true last-resort branch (preserve every artifact + loud `PopupDialog`). Alert message factored to the pure `BuildRestoreDegradedAlertMessage` (unit-tested) via a tiny `FlightBatchBaselineState_SlotInfo` DTO.
- **Crash reconcile (sidecar revert + cold in-memory reload, NOT bare disk overwrite).** A `TestBatchMarker` (new `Source/Parsek/TestBatchMarker.cs`) is written into `persistent.sfs` at batch start (after the clean `.bak`, fire-and-forget durable save so autosave-disabled players still get the in-memory + disk revert, just not crash reconcile). The marker carries BOTH the clean `persistent.sfs` `.bak` path AND the on-disk Parsek sidecar snapshot dir (`<slot>-parsek`, set from `batchFlightBaseline.ParsekSaveSnapshotDirectory`; null in DiskOnly mode), so a NEW process can revert the career LEDGER (`Parsek/GameState/events.pgse`), not just `persistent.sfs`. The snapshot is a durable directory under `saves/<save>/` that survives a process kill. On the next `ParsekScenario.OnLoad` in a DIFFERENT process, `RunTestBatchCrashReconcile` (called after `LoadTimeSweep.Run()` on both OnLoad branches, mirroring the re-fly finisher; wrapped in a defensive try/catch so it can never throw out of OnLoad) (1) reverts `persistent.sfs` from the `.bak`, (2) reverts the live `Parsek/` sidecar dir from the snapshot, (3) forces a clean in-memory reload by setting `initialLoadDone = false` and running the SAME `*.ResetForTesting()` set the success path (`PrepareForIsolatedBatchFlightBaselineRestore`) uses, and (4) schedules a one-frame-deferred REAL `GamePersistence.LoadGame` of the reverted save. Because `initialLoadDone` was reset, the deferred reload's OnLoad takes the COLD branch and `LoadExternalFiles -> LedgerOrchestrator.OnLoad` RE-LOADS the ledger from the now-clean `events.pgse` (instead of the scene-change branch, which skips `LoadExternalFiles` and would `RecalculateAndPatch` from the STALE in-memory ledger and re-corrupt the career).
