The artifact sweep (`.bak` + slot + `.loadmeta` + snapshot) runs INSIDE the deferred coroutine AFTER the reload has consumed the disk, so the snapshot survives until the clean reload reads it; a reload or revert failure preserves every artifact for manual recovery. The finisher NEVER calls `SaveGame` from inside OnLoad. The reconcile decision is the pure `TestBatchMarker.ShouldReconcileOnLoad` (unit-tested): fires only on process-mismatch + save-folder match + backup-path present; a same-process load never reconciles (in-process teardown owns it), a wrong-save / stale marker is dropped without touching `persistent.sfs`.
- **Complete artifact sweep.** Success path reverts `persistent.sfs` from the clean `.bak` then sweeps slot + `.loadmeta` + `.bak` + Parsek snapshot dir (InMemoryAndDisk) or `.bak` (DiskOnly); crash path sweeps `.bak` + derived slot/loadmeta + the marker's recorded snapshot dir AFTER the deferred reload commits (so the snapshot survives until the clean reload consumes it). Test-created RewindPoints are still reaped by `RewindPointReaper.ReapOrphanedRPs()` on the baseline reload's OnLoad (intentional dependency; DiskOnly scenes create no RPs).
- **SPACECENTER ships DiskOnly** (safety `.bak`, no in-memory reload) behind the new skipped in-game gate `RuntimeTests.SpaceCenterBatchIsolationInMemoryRestore`; flip `ClassifyBatchIsolationMode` SPACECENTER -> `InMemoryAndDisk` only after that passes in a manual playtest. **EDITOR** is DiskOnly with the contract enforced by the always-run in-game `RuntimeTests.NoEditorSceneTestsExistContract` (fails if any `[InGameTest]` declares `Scene=EDITOR`). Note: batch start now writes the player's `persistent.sfs` once (the `.bak` is provably taken first; xUnit source-gate `CaptureBaseline_CapturesBeforeWritingMarker` / `WriteMarker_BuildsMarkerBeforeDurableSave` pin the ordering).

Files: `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/InGameTestRunner.cs` (marker carries `ParsekSnapshotDir`), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/Helpers/QuickloadResumeHelpers.cs` (`TriggerCampaignPersistentSave`), `Source/Parsek/TestBatchMarker.cs` (new; `ParsekSnapshotDir` field + Save/Load), `Source/Parsek/ParsekScenario.cs` (marker field + OnSave/OnLoad + finisher: sidecar-dir revert + cold-reload prep + deferred-reload artifact sweep), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (two new tests). xUnit: `Source/Parsek.Tests/TestBatchIsolationTests.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/TestBatchMarkerTests.cs`.

**NOT YET VALIDATED IN-GAME** (no KSP runtime in the authoring environment): all new orchestration is runtime/scene-bound file I/O + reload wiring and needs a build + playtest. Every path is defensive (try/catch, atomic safe-write, preserve-on-failure, fire-and-forget durable save) so a failure degrades to a warning rather than corrupting the campaign. The SPACECENTER in-memory path is deliberately NOT shipped (DiskOnly) until its gate test passes manually. The deferred crash-reconcile reload (`DeferredReloadAfterTestBatchCrashReconcile`) needs an interrupted-batch playtest in particular: verify the new-process cold reload re-loads the ledger from the reverted `Parsek/GameState/events.pgse` (the COLD-branch `LedgerOrchestrator.OnLoad`, not a scene-change-branch `RecalculateAndPatch` from stale statics) and that the career economy ends byte-identical to the pre-run save; confirm both the FLIGHT (`StartAndFocusVessel`) and non-FLIGHT (`Game.Start`) reload branches.

## Done - Generalized batch baseline isolation to the Tracking Station

The automatic batch baseline restore (`InGameTestRunner.RestoreBatchFlightBaselineCore`) was FLIGHT-only: `GetBatchFlightBaselineUnavailableReason` hard-required the FLIGHT scene + an active vessel, and the restore committed via `FlightDriver.StartAndFocusVessel` (always FLIGHT). That left `TrackingStationMaterializedOrbit_FlyLoadsMaterializedVessel_NotStaleSelection` (TRACKSTATION scene, clicks stock Fly → FLIGHT) as the lone `AllowBatchExecution = false` test with no isolation — all 34 others already carry `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution = true`.

Generalized the baseline to FLIGHT **or** TRACKSTATION, keeping the FLIGHT restore-core scene-commit path byte-identical (the FLIGHT capture/cleanup later also gained the persistent.sfs backup/restore — see the campaign-safety entry above) and branching only the scene-specific steps on a new `FlightBatchBaselineState.CapturedScene`:
- `BatchBaselineUnavailableReasonForScene` (pure, unit-tested) + `IsBatchBaselineRestoreSupportedScene` (pure, unit-tested) gate FLIGHT/TRACKSTATION and require an active vessel only for FLIGHT.
- `CaptureFlightBatchBaseline` records the scene and tolerates a null active vessel outside FLIGHT.
- Restore step 1a passes `requireValidActiveVessel: false` for non-FLIGHT (a TS save can carry `activeVessel = -1`); step 1b realises via the vessel-tolerant `QuickloadResumeHelpers.LoadGameForSceneRestore`; steps 4/5 commit via the new `CommitNonFlightSceneLoad`, which replays stock KSP's own in-game load sequence (`HighLogic.CurrentGame = game` → `GamePersistence.UpdateScenarioModules` → set `startScene` → `Game.Start()`, decompiled from the `PauseMenu` Load button), then `WaitForBatchBaselineNonFlightScene` (waits for the target scene AND a freshly-rebuilt `ParsekScenario`, so a same-scene TS→TS prime reload is not reported ready on frame 1). The wipe (step 3) and Parsek-snapshot staging (step 2) are scene-agnostic and unchanged; `ParsekScenario.OnLoad` rebuilds the wiped stores in the destination scene either way. The TS test now carries `RunLast = true, RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution = true` and runs under `Run All + Isolated` launched from the Tracking Station (returning there afterward).

**NOT YET VALIDATED IN-GAME** (no .NET/KSP toolchain in the authoring environment): the FLIGHT restore-core scene commit is byte-identical and the new APIs are all real/used in-repo, but the TRACKSTATION scene-return, the `activeVessel = -1` tolerance, and OnLoad store-rebuild in the TS scene need a build + playtest before relying on them. The non-FLIGHT commit (`CommitNonFlightSceneLoad`) replays stock KSP's `PauseMenu` Load-button sequence verbatim (`HighLogic.CurrentGame = game` → `UpdateScenarioModules` → set `startScene` → `Game.Start()`, decompiled from `Assembly-CSharp` 1.12.5). An earlier draft mirrored `RuntimeTests.TriggerSaveAndExitToSpaceCenter`'s `Game.Updated()` + `SaveGame` shape, but that was wrong here: `TriggerSaveAndExitToSpaceCenter` saves the ALREADY-STARTED live game, whereas this loads a fresh unstarted `Game`, and decompiled `Game.Updated()` does not round-trip its receiver (in a planetarium scene it rebuilds `flightState` from the LIVE scene and pulls `scenarios` from the global `ScenarioRunner`), so it would publish the post-test session and re-saving it into the baseline slot would corrupt the slot for every later restore. The FLIGHT branch is unaffected if the TS branch misbehaves (a failed TS restore degrades through `FailAndAbortBatchAfterRestore`).

## Done - Facility force-close safety net in the in-game test runner

The Phase-5 `StockUiOverlay` tests (R&D / Astronaut Complex / Mission Control, SPACECENTER scene) enter a facility building, which pauses the game (`FlightDriver.SetPause -> timeScale 0`) and opens the facility canvas. Each test closes its building in its own try/finally, and the runner disposes the test iterator via `RunCoroutineSafely` so that finally fires even on a failed assertion — but a user **Cancel** stops the coroutine with Unity `StopCoroutine`, which does NOT run the iterator's finally, leaving the player stuck inside the building with the game paused and no automatic return to the Space Center (SPACECENTER batches capture no FLIGHT baseline to restore). A despawn event that no-ops in some game state has the same effect.

Added `InGameTestRunner.ForceCloseOpenSpaceCenterFacilities(reason)`: gated to the SPACECENTER scene via the pure `ShouldForceCloseSpaceCenterFacilities`, it detects any open `RDController` / `AstronautComplex` / `MissionControl` / `Administration` (FindObjectOfType) and fires the matching stock despawn GameEvent (`onGUIRnDComplexDespawn` etc.) — exactly what UISpaceCenter's exit button does, so UISpaceCenter unpauses and tears down the canvas. Wired into three call sites: `PerformBetweenRunCleanup` (start of every batch — recovers a prior stuck/cancelled run), `Cancel()` (closes on cancel), and per-test `RunCleanup` (closes before the next test). Each fire is gated on the facility being open so a despawn is never fired into an empty scene; swallow-on-throw so one broken close cannot abort cleanup. Pure helpers (`ShouldForceCloseSpaceCenterFacilities`, `FormatFacilityForceCloseSummary`) unit-tested in `InGameTestRunnerTests`. The Unity FindObjectOfType + GameEvents.Fire wiring is runtime-only (needs in-game validation).

## Done - Promoted the scene-exit merge-dialog in-game tests into the Isolated batch

The two `SceneExitMerge` in-game tests (`ExitToSpaceCenter_DeferredMergeButton_CommitsPendingTree` and `ExitToSpaceCenter_DeferredDiscardButton_ClearsPendingTree`) were the last `AllowBatchExecution = false` FLIGHT tests without a restore flag, so both `Run All` and `Run All + Isolated` skipped them as manual-only. They now carry `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution = true` (mirroring the already-isolated `RevertToLaunch_SoftUnstashesPendingTree_WithoutMergeDialog`), so `Run All + Isolated` captures a FLIGHT baseline before the batch and quickloads it after each one. These two are notable because they end in `SPACECENTER` (stock save-and-exit), not `FLIGHT` — the restore path tolerates this because `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineCore` reloads via `GamePersistence.LoadGame` + `FlightDriver.StartAndFocusVessel`, which forces FLIGHT regardless of the current scene. Each test already had a full try/finally teardown (dismiss merge dialog, restore `autoMerge`/throttle, discard pending tree, `RemoveCommittedTreeByIdForRuntimeTest`, stop recording); the baseline quickload is the belt-and-suspenders net on top. They stay `AllowBatchExecution = false` (out of the lightweight `Run All`, which has no restore) and self-skip gracefully unless the active vessel is an idle non-EVA `PRELAUNCH` craft on the pad. `BatchSkipReason` rewritten to the standard "Isolated-run only ... Use Run All + Isolated or the row play button" wording; runner self-tests use synthetic `InGameTestInfo` fixtures so they are unaffected.

## Done - Promoted the manual logistics + staging in-game tests into the Isolated batch

The eight in-game tests that previously had to be run by hand via the test-runner row play button (they were `AllowBatchExecution = false` with no restore flag, so both `Run All` and `Run All + Isolated` skipped them as manual-only) now carry `RestoreBatchFlightBaselineAfterExecution = true`, so `Run All + Isolated` runs them automatically and quickloads the captured FLIGHT baseline afterward. Each test already had a full try/finally teardown (snapshot + restore of RouteStore / Ledger / MissionStore / committed trees / live `PartResource.amount` / the `RouteOrchestrator.LoopUnitResolverForTesting` static seam, plus disposable-slot deletion); the baseline quickload is the belt-and-suspenders net on top (and the only reset for the static seam, which a quickload does not touch, so the in-finally disarm still matters). They stay `AllowBatchExecution = false` (out of the lightweight `Run All`, which has no restore) and self-skip gracefully on the wrong vessel shape (no LF tank, fewer than two cargo containers, fewer than two command pods).

Promoted tests:
- `CaptureRPOnStagingTest.CaptureRPOnStaging` (Rewind) - was the lone staging test missing the restore flag its siblings `SavePathRootThenMove` / `WarpZeroedDuringSave` already carried.
- `LogisticsRouteStoreRuntimeTests.RouteStore_AddRoute_SurvivesKspSaveLoadRoundTrip`
- `LogisticsRouteDispatchRuntimeTests.RouteOrchestrator_Tick_ProcessesSyntheticRoute`
- `LogisticsDeliveryRuntimeTests.Delivery_LoadedVessel_AppliesResourceTransfer`
- `LogisticsRouteOnMissionsRuntimeTests.RouteOnMissions_RendersTrimmedLoop_FiresAtDock_AndMutuallyExcludes`
- `LogisticsRouteOnMissionsRuntimeTests.LoopFire_RendersAndDelivers_AtDockCrossing`
- `LogisticsRouteTreeGuardRuntimeTests.RouteTreeGuard_BindsTreeAndClearsBothLoopSurfaces`
- `LogisticsRouteProofRuntimeTests.InventoryPayloadIdentityHash_LiveStockMove_PreservesIdentity`

Each test's `BatchSkipReason` was rewritten to the standard "Isolated-run only ... Use Run All + Isolated or the row play button" wording (the old "runs out of band so a parallel batch test cannot observe partial state" rationale no longer holds: the runner is sequential and the post-test baseline quickload closes the partial-state window). The runner self-tests (`InGameTestRunnerTests`, `TestRunnerPresentationTests`) use synthetic `InGameTestInfo` fixtures, not the attribute scan, so they are unaffected; full xUnit suite green (14496).

### ~~Open~~ RESOLVED 2026-06-07 (PR #1083) - `RouteOrchestrator_Tick_ProcessesSyntheticRoute` was RED under live statics (test-setup bug, not a dispatch regression)

Root cause was an UNSATISFIABLE acceptance criterion, not a dispatch regression. The synthetic route carries an empty `SourceRefs` list, so `LiveRouteRuntimeEnvironment.RouteHasValidSourcesInErs` returns false, the evaluator yields `SourcesStale`, and `RouteOrchestrator.Tick` resolves it to a benign `Skip("sources-stale")` that correctly mutates neither `Status` (stays `Active`) nor the ledger. The old assertion required `statusChanged || ledgerRowForRoute`, which a sourceless route can never satisfy; `RouteOrchestrator.Tick` itself behaved correctly (the tick summary logged `routes=1 errored=0 skipped=1`). Fix (PR #1083, test-only): assert the benign-skip invariants instead (route still present, still `Active`, no ledger row attributed to its id), and scope the doc comment's env-NRE guarantee to env construction / pre-dispatch (the ERS / Funding probes are LAZY, inside `ProcessOneRoute`'s per-route try/catch, so a probe NRE is counted as `errored++` and would not surface here; only a construction / pre-dispatch throw fails the test). Validated in-game 2026-06-07 (PASSED, `status=Active newLedgerRows=0`).

### Open - test-runner Cancel mid-test does not run the test `finally` (pre-existing runner machinery)

Surfaced by the clean review of the batch-promotion above; pre-existing, not introduced by it. `InGameTestRunner.Cancel` (`InGameTestRunner.cs:414`) calls `StopCoroutine` on the Unity `Coroutine` handles (`activeInnerCoroutine` / `activeTestCoroutine` / `activeCoroutine`) but the runner holds only those Unity handles, NOT the underlying suspended `IEnumerator`s. Unity's `StartCoroutine` flattens the nested chain (`RunOneTest` -> `SafeEnumerator` -> `RunCoroutineSafely(testBody)`, `InGameTestRunner.cs:1694-1702`) and drives it itself; `StopCoroutine` does not `Dispose` any of those iterators, so a Cancel issued mid-test never unwinds the test body's `try/finally`. For a test that arms a process-static seam (e.g. `RouteOrchestrator.LoopUnitResolverForTesting` in `LoopFire_RendersAndDelivers_AtDockCrossing`, disarmed only in its finally) a Cancel during its single-frame `yield` would leak the armed seam into the rest of the session. Low probability (one-frame window, requires a user-initiated Cancel) and it affects every coroutine in-game test that mutates statics, not just the promoted ones. A correct fix is a focused runner refactor: store the IEnumerator chain (or the outermost `RunCoroutineSafely` iterator) so `Cancel` can `Dispose` it (cascading the test-body finally), validated in-game (cancel-path behavior is not headless-reachable). Deliberately NOT bundled into the test-attribute promotion PR.

### Open - background `RouteOrchestrator.Tick` can re-enter a logistics test's synthetic route (pre-existing)

Also surfaced by the review; pre-existing. `ParsekScenario.Update` fires `RouteOrchestrator.Tick(currentUT)` every `TickIntervalSec = 1.0` UT-second (`RouteOrchestrator.cs`). While a logistics in-game test's synthetic route is in `RouteStore.CommittedRoutes` (and, for `LoopFire`, the resolver seam is armed), a background tick during the test's single-frame `yield return null` could process the synthetic route if game UT advanced >= 1s that frame (only under time warp). Extremely low probability at normal rate; the tests use unique synthetic route ids and remove them in finally. Unchanged by the promotion (the same exposure existed on the row-play-button path). Flagged for completeness; a real fix would gate the orchestrator tick during a runner-driven test or namespace test routes out of the live tick.

---

## Done - Re-aim E2E in-game test `Reaim_KerbinToDuna_EveryWindowResolvesSaneTransfer` is FLAKY (congruent-window resolver reliability; closed by M-MIS-1, PR #1116)

**Tracked as M-MIS-1** in the Missions feature completion milestones at the top of this file (first re-aim milestone; the deterministic pinned-UT harness is the entry step).

Surfaced while fixing the five frame/anomaly in-game test models (PR #1083), where it was deliberately left untouched because it is a real product weakness, not a test-model defect like its five siblings. This SPACECENTER test (`ReaimEndToEndInGameTest`) seeds its known-good departure off the live `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` and drives `ReaimPlaybackResolver.TryResolveWindowSegments` across several consecutive synodic windows. It fails INTERMITTENTLY, with the failure mode varying by the live UT at run time:
- 2026-06-06: all 5 windows resolved but the transfer orientation did not rotate across windows (`lan0=lanLast=0.00`, failed "the transfer orientation must rotate across windows").
- 2026-06-06 (later run): `window k=2 must resolve a re-aimed transfer` (a window failed to resolve at all).
- 2026-06-07: `window k=1 must resolve` (a different window failed).

This is a reliability gap in the re-aim congruent-window resolver / synthesizer (`ReaimPlaybackResolver`, `ReaimTransferSynthesizer`), the in-game manifestation of the parked re-aim Phase-4 generalization (see the "DUNA ONE CLOSED ... Phase-4 GENERALIZATION still deferred" entry and post-cutover backlog item #1 below). PARKED / check later: per the re-aim seam guidance, build a deterministic failing case (pin the departure UT rather than seeding off live UT) and measure BEFORE any knob math, and treat "the faithful render is good enough" as a valid outcome - do not stack speculative fixes on a working baseline. A cheap first step would be to make the test deterministic (fixed seed UT) so the failure is reproducible.

**Deterministic harness SHIPPED (branch `reaim-resolver-reliability`, 2026-06-10):** the test now scans from a pinned base UT (geometry pinned: stock ephemeris elements are functions of UT and nothing in the driven path reads the live clock). Root causes split: the `lan0=lanLast=0.00` mode was the LAN assertion being degenerate for the near-equatorial plane-constrained transfer (fixed: rotation asserted on longitude of periapsis, LAN+AoP); the `window k must resolve` modes were the first-scan-success departure sitting on the feasibility-band EDGE, where eccentric-target drift leaves the +/-6% recorded-tof search (now pinned as a separate band-edge test asserting the designed resolve-or-decline-cleanly contract, plus a manual `Reaim_KerbinToDuna_FeasibilitySweep_Diagnostic` that logs the full departure x window map).

**VALIDATED + CLASSIFIED in-game 2026-06-10 (logs `2026-06-10_2213_reaim-mmis1-sweep`): CLOSED.** All four Periodicity tests passed across two batch runs + the sweep. The LAN/AoP split flipped between runs for the same transfer (lan=0.00/aop=36.99 vs lan=259.52/aop=137.46) while LPe stayed 36.99, proving the mode-A fix; the sweep showed every contiguous-band departure resolving all 5 windows with declines only at isolated knife-edge departures, classified unresolvable-by-design (no tof widening; the fail-closed faithful fallback is correct). Residual nuance: determinism is per-frame, not absolute (KSP re-bases body-orbit epochs every frame; only knife-edge scan entries flip; tests are insensitive by design). Full results: plan section 9. See the M-MIS-1 milestone entry at the top of this file.

## Done - Space Center ghost orphaned (frozen above the pad, engines running) when CommittedRecordings empties/shrinks

- ~~After the scene-exit merge **commit** in-game test (`ExitToSpaceCenter_DeferredMergeButton_CommitsPendingTree`) ran, a "Jumping Flea" ghost hung frozen above the launch pad with engines running and audio playing until the next scene change (~56 s later). Observed in the 2026-06-06 frozen-ghost playtest: ghost `#0` spawned at 23:43:13.05, never repositioned, finally reaped on the SPACECENTER→MAINMENU change at 23:44:09.~~ FIXED (this branch, `ParsekKSC.cs`).
- **Root cause:** `ParsekKSC.Update` keys `kscGhosts` / `kscOverlapGhosts` by committed-recording index and early-returns at `if (committed.Count == 0) return;` (`ParsekKSC.cs`). The test commits a recording (KSC spawns a ghost for it on scene entry), then its `finally` removes the committed tree via `RemoveCommittedTreeByIdForRuntimeTest`, emptying `CommittedRecordings`. From that frame on, the per-index loop never iterates the now out-of-range key, and the empty-list early-return skips any teardown, so the already-spawned ghost is orphaned: never repositioned (frozen at its last launch pose), engine FX/audio never stopped, destroyed only when `OnDestroy` fires on the next scene change. Not test-only: any path that empties or shrinks `CommittedRecordings` while a KSC ghost is live (Wipe All in Data Management, removing the last recording) leaks the same way.
- **Fix:** added `ReapOrphanedKscGhosts(committedCount)`, called every frame in `Update` BEFORE the empty-list early-return. It destroys (via the existing `DestroyKscGhost` / `DestroyAllKscOverlapGhosts` paths, so engine FX/audio stop) any primary or overlap ghost whose index key is now outside `[0, committedCount)`, and removes the stale `kscGhosts` / `kscOverlapGhosts` / `loggedGhostSpawn` / `loggedReshow` entries. It also prunes the per-index log-dedup dicts (`lastLoggedKscCadence` / `lastUnitSelection`, value tuples that the inactive/ineligible/disabled cleanup paths never pruned) via a generic allocation-free `PruneOrphanedIndexKeys` helper, independent of ghost presence so the "ghost destroyed, then recording removed" corner case is covered; both are also cleared in `OnDestroy` alongside the sibling dedup collections. It iterates the concrete `Dictionary.Keys` (struct enumerator, no boxing) into a reusable scratch buffer, so it is allocation-free in the steady state; the per-key decision is the pure `internal static IsOrphanedGhostIndex(key, committedCount)`. Tests: an 8-case `[Theory]` in `KscGhostPlaybackTests` (empty list, in-range incl. last valid index, shrink-from-end incl. `index == count`, sparse key past the end, negative key). Scoped to the empty/shrink-from-end leak: a non-tail removal shifts indices (the file's pre-existing `[ERS-exempt]` index-keying limitation) but does not reproduce the frozen-ghost leak because every in-range index is still revisited each frame.

---

## Done - Map-render director-shadow `ArgumentNullException(key)` on null body name (`GhostMapSceneBase` / `FlightGlobals.GetBodyByName`)

- ~~Single suppressed occurrence in the 2026-06-06 "orbital supply route DELIVERY test" playtest (13:58:33): `[VERBOSE][MapRender] shadow RunFrame threw (suppressed): ArgumentNullException: Value cannot be null. Parameter name: key`. Caught + swallowed by the try/catch around `MapRender.ShadowRenderDriver.RunFrame` in `ParsekFlight.cs:19314` (and the mirror in `ParsekTrackingStation.cs:264`), rate-limited, so it fired once.~~ FIXED (this branch, `GhostMapSceneBase.cs`).
- **Root cause (decompiled, not guessed):** `FlightGlobals.GetBodyByName(string)` (KSP 1.12.5, decompiled) resolves through `private Dictionary<string,CelestialBody> bodyNames` and calls `bodyNames.ContainsKey(bodyName)` with NO null guard. `Dictionary<string,_>.ContainsKey(null)` throws `ArgumentNullException` with `paramName == "key"` - the exact observed message. The shadow's scene adapter `GhostMapSceneBase` called `FlightGlobals.GetBodyByName` UNGUARDED from three sites: `IsStarBody` (every shadow frame, via `ShadowRenderDriver.RunFrame`'s `scene.IsStarBody(intent.FrameBodyName)` - evaluated before the short-circuiting `ShouldSkipReaimSegment`), the `BodySurface`/`ResolveBodySurface` provider (per orbit segment during `ChainAssembler.Build`, on a chain cache-miss), and `ResolveBody`. The null arrives normally: `GhostRenderIntent.Hidden` carries `FrameBodyName == null` (a present-but-out-of-window ghost - the parent-anchored Depot between route legs is the likely trigger), and an `OrbitSegment` can lack a recorded body. Build is cached (`ShadowRenderDriver.GetOrBuildChain`) and a hidden-intent ghost in `ghostMapVesselPids` is only transient, so either path fits the single rate-limited occurrence.
- **SHADOW-specific, but the shadow is the SURVIVING path (NOT moot):** the same null-key path does NOT exist in the primary/legacy map-render path. The autonomous polyline `Driver` (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs`) guards `string.IsNullOrEmpty` before its lookups (`ResolveBodyByName` :2345, `ResolveBodySurface` :2383) and uses its own pre-populated `bodyByName` dict, never the throwing `FlightGlobals.GetBodyByName`. The SAME shared helpers (`ComputeOrbitalCoverIntervals` / `IsOrbitSegmentBelowSurface`) run in both paths, but the Driver feeds a guarded surface provider while the shadow fed `GhostMapSceneBase.ResolveBodySurface` (unguarded). However the "shadow" (`ShadowRenderDriver`) is NOT slated for removal - per `docs/dev/plans/maprender-rewrite-status.md` it is the Phase-8a default-on (`mapRenderDirectorDrive = true`) Director seed producer whose StockConic seeds drive the live icon, and at 8e it becomes the SOLE path (the LEGACY draw is what gets deleted). So this was a latent fault in default-on, live-consumed code: each throw aborted that frame's seed production and dropped every ghost's icon drive to the legacy (off-orbit) path for the frame.
- **Fix:** routed `GhostMapSceneBase`'s three body lookups through a private `ResolveBodyByNameSafe(string)` that returns null for a null/empty name (mirroring the Driver's guard) before touching `FlightGlobals`, with a `VerboseRateLimited` "scene-null-body-name" skip diagnostic. Gate-neutral, behaviorally identical for any real body name. Tests: `GhostMapSceneBaseNullBodyGuardTests` (5) - null/empty into `IsStarBody` / `ResolveBody` / the `BodySurface` provider return the not-found result without throwing (the null/empty inputs short-circuit before any `FlightGlobals` ECall, so the tests run headless), plus a log-assertion on the skip diagnostic.

## Done - Logistics window tooltip-echo IMGUI control-count storm

- ~~Hovering any tooltip-bearing control in the Logistics (Supply Routes) window threw a continuous `ArgumentException: Getting control N's position in a group with only N controls when doing repaint` at the Close button (256 times over ~45s in the 2026-06-06 orbital-route playtest log), aborting the rest of the window's draw every frame.~~ FIXED (branch `fix-logistics-tooltip-echo`). Root cause: the QW6 bottom tooltip-echo block (`LogisticsWindowUI.DrawWindow`) emitted a different GUILayout control count between the Layout pass and the Repaint pass. When `GUI.tooltip` was empty it drew 1 control (a zero-height Label); when populated it drew 2 (a `GUILayout.Space` plus a Label). `GUI.tooltip` is empty during Layout and only populated during Repaint, so the count diverged and the trailing Close button overran its layout group. Fix: extracted the emit into `DrawTooltipEchoBox(string guiTooltip)`, which now always emits exactly one `GUILayout.Space` plus one `GUILayout.Label` (varying only spacing/content/style by hover state), matching the invariant-count pattern in `SettingsWindowUI`. The pure decision `ResolveTooltipEcho` is unchanged and still unit-tested; added an in-game probe test (`LogisticsTooltipEchoImguiTest`) that drives a real IMGUI Layout+Repaint cycle with the same tooltip divergence and a trailing button, asserting no exception. (Note: `SpawnControlUI` carries the same conditional-Space shape but does not throw because nothing in its layout group follows the echo box; only Logistics has a trailing control.)

## Done - Supply-route backing-mission pipeline log flood

- ~~A single supply-route delivery playtest (save "orbital supply route DELIVERY test", 2026-06-06) wrote 60,351 `[Parsek]` KSP.log lines, about 85% of them from the route's backing-mission pipeline. Breakdown from that log: `BuildMission:` 21,141 (per-frame, unconditional `Verbose` in `RouteBackingMission.BuildMission`, called every render frame by `RouteGhostDriverSelector`); `BuildMissionStructure` / `ExtractConstraints` / `ReaimDiag` / `PhaseLock SKIPPED` about 4,240 each plus `MissionLoopUnit:` 8,480 (the full structure / periodicity / re-aim build); `IsTreeBoundToActiveRoute` BOUND 2,026. The delivery itself worked; this was pure logging / perf hygiene.~~ FIXED (branch `fix-route-loop-log-flood`). Root cause (NOT signature churn, contrary to the first hypothesis): the render path's `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` is correctly signature-gated and rebuilt only 7 times all session (5 flight + 2 KSC, per the "loop units rebuilt" logs). The flood came from `RouteOrchestrator.ResolveLoopUnit` (used by the delivery clock `ProcessLoopRoute` AND the Logistics-window countdown via `TryComputeSecondsToNextDockCrossing` / `ComputeRouteLegibility`), which rebuilds the route's backing Mission and runs the whole structure / periodicity / re-aim pipeline UNGATED and UN-suppressed on every call. `RouteOrchestrator.Tick` (`ParsekScenario`) is throttled by GAME UT (`TickIntervalSec`), so under time warp the tick fires roughly 20x per real second (4,242 builds over 3 min). Fix (logging / perf hygiene only, the functional delivery path is untouched): `ResolveLoopUnit` now wraps the build in the three builder `SuppressLogging` flags (`MissionStructureBuilder` [new flag, mirrors the existing two] plus `MissionPeriodicity` plus `MissionLoopUnitBuilder`), mirroring `MissionsWindowUI`'s display-mirror build, so the computed loop unit is byte-identical but the pipeline emits no diagnostics; `RouteBackingMission.BuildMission` and `RouteTreeGuard`'s BOUND line are now `VerboseRateLimited` (per-route / per-tree keys); and `PhaseLock SKIPPED` is demoted from INFO to `VerboseRateLimited` (INFO bypassed verbose-off). The three flags gate Verbose / Info plus two pre-existing `MissionPeriodicity` diagnostic Warns (degenerate-period filter and over-constrained Tier-1 residual); the `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` owner / member collision Warns stay un-gated. Silencing the `MissionPeriodicity` Warns inside the per-tick resolve is intentional (at Warn they ignore verbose-off and would flood every tick), and the signature-gated render build (`DriveMissionLoopUnits`) plus the Missions window still surface them un-suppressed for the same config. Tests: `MissionStructureTests.Build_SuppressLogging_SilencesBuildMissionStructureLine`, `MissionPeriodicityTests.Build_AllSuppressFlags_EmitsNoPipelineDiagnostics` plus the no-INFO guard on the existing `PhaseLock SKIPPED` test, `RouteBackingMissionTests.BuildMission_RateLimitsItsPerFrameLog`, `RouteTreeGuardTests.IsBound_BoundLog_IsRateLimitedPerTree`.

## Done - Missions window backing-mission pipeline log flood (sibling of the route flood)

- ~~While the Missions window was open it rebuilt the same backing-mission pipeline every OnGUI frame and leaked the `BuildMissionStructure:` / `ExtractConstraints` / `Solve` `Verbose` lines (the 2026-06-06 orbital-route playtest log shows about 5,174 `BuildMissionStructure:` lines from this UI path). Two display-path call sites in `MissionsWindowUI` were the source: `GetMissionView` called `MissionStructureBuilder.Build(tree)` directly with no suppression (per-frame-cached, so once per frame per tree), and `GetLoopUnitSet` wrapped its `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` call in `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.SuppressLogging = true` ONLY, so the INNER `MissionStructureBuilder.Build` and `MissionPeriodicity.ExtractConstraints` / `Solve` lines still emitted once per frame per looping mission.~~ FIXED (branch `fix-missions-window-log-flood`, sibling of `fix-route-loop-log-flood`). Logging-only / display-path change, no behavior change: `GetMissionView`'s direct `MissionStructureBuilder.Build` call and `GetLoopUnitSet`'s `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` call are now each wrapped in the builder `SuppressLogging` flags via try/finally that restores the previous values (`MissionStructureBuilder` + `MissionPeriodicity` for the structure build; all three including `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` for the loop-unit build, since `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` internally rebuilds the structure and runs the periodicity solver), mirroring `RouteOrchestrator.ResolveLoopUnit`. The structure / loop unit built is byte-identical, so the data the window shows is unchanged; only the per-frame diagnostics are gated. As in the route fix, suppressing `MissionPeriodicity` also silences its two diagnostic `Warn`s during the display build, which is fine for a display mirror (the signature-gated render build still surfaces them un-suppressed for the same config). Test: `MissionStructureTests.Build_DisplayMirrorSuppressFlagPair_SilencesLineAndRestoresFlags` (the GetMissionView flag pair silences the line, still builds, and restores both flags); the GetLoopUnitSet all-three-flags contract is already covered by `MissionPeriodicityTests.Build_AllSuppressFlags_EmitsNoPipelineDiagnostics`.

## Done - Map/TS render tracer `gap-vs-retire` / `decision-vs-old-truth` anomaly missing its per-frame rate-limit

- ~~With `mapRenderTracing` on (an opt-in debug instrument, never on for players), a sustained intent-vs-old-truth divergence re-emitted the byte-identical `phase=Anomaly reason=gap-vs-retire` (or `decision-vs-old-truth`) line every frame for the affected pid. A 2026-06-06 looped-recordings session logged ~2,844 of these lines from just 3 pids (one per consecutive frame, ~16/s) - the dominant non-VERBOSE map-tracer volume. `GhostRenderReconciler.CheckIntentAgainstOldTruth` was the ONLY `EmitAnomaly` path in the probe with no `Passes*RateLimit` guard; its 4 siblings (`icon-jump` 0.5s, `icon-off-orbit` 1.0s, `polyline-orbit-overlap` 1.0s, `unaccounted-drawn` 1.0s) all had one. `EmitAnomaly`'s own docstring already said "the caller soft-rate-limits per pid+reason" - 4 of 6 callers honored that, these two did not. Persistent-condition oversight, not a design choice.~~ FIXED (branch `fix-maprender-anomaly-ratelimit`). Diagnostic-only / opt-in-tracer change, no player-facing or default-play behavior change: added a per-(pid, class) soft rate-limit on the anomaly LINE (`IntentReconcileAnomalyMinIntervalSeconds = 1.0` wall-clock, separate dict per class) so a sustained divergence logs onset + a 1/s heartbeat instead of one line per frame. No debugging signal is lost: the detailed window that drives the per-frame `phase=Snapshot` detail is refreshed SEPARATELY (`OpenDetailedWindow`) on every divergent frame, decoupled from the rate-limited line. This decoupling is load-bearing (review catch): the line limiter is wall-clock but the window is UT (`AnomalyWindowSeconds = 5.0`), so under time warp a 5 UT-second window would lapse between 1 wall-second heartbeats and the snapshots would gap; refreshing it every divergent frame keeps the stream continuous at any warp (matching the pre-fix every-frame `EmitAnomaly`). Per-class keying means a class transition still emits immediately, and per-pid keying means a second diverging pid is never suppressed by the first. State is cleared on scene switch (`MapRenderProbe.OnGameSceneSwitchRequested` -> `GhostRenderReconciler.ClearRateLimitState`) so a stale timestamp cannot suppress the first divergence after a TS <-> flight re-entry. Tests (+5): same-class within-interval suppression (5 frames -> 1 line), after-interval re-emit (2 lines), per-class transition emits immediately, per-pid independence, and a suppressed frame still refreshes the UT detail window so a `phase=Snapshot` still emits (the warp case); the 5 existing wiring tests thread the new `realtime` arg. Full suite green (14501).

## In progress - v0.10.0 Map/TS render tracer SECOND CUT: recordingId keying + decision-vs-truth reconciliation

- Branch `maprender-second-cut` (off origin/main, which has the probe-only MVP from PR #1005). Design: `docs/dev/design-map-ts-render-tracer.md` (the second-cut sections). Builds the deferred reconciliation / shared-window / reverse-map work on top of the merged MVP.
- **Done (foundation):** completed the `vesselPidToRecordingId` reverse map for CHAIN ghosts (was timeline-only) - write in `CreateGhostVessel` keyed by the live ghost pid + remove in `RemoveGhostVessel`. Unblocks recordingId-keyed windows/correlation. **Two intended rendering-behavior ripples to validate in playtest:** (1) chain ghosts now participate in polyline-ownership icon hiding (same as timeline ghosts); (2) Tracking-Station ghost selection (`GhostTrackingStationPatch.SelectGhost` via `FindRecordingIdByVesselPid`) now resolves the chain-tip's backing recording (StartUT/EndUT/terminal fields) where it previously returned empty - a latent-gap fix surfaced by the final review. In-game test `ChainGhost_ReverseMap_WrittenOnCreate_ClearedOnRemove`. Reviewed clean-context (SHIP AS-IS); SHOULD/CONSIDER items applied (test + fresh-create comment + doc-line softening).
- **Done (reconciliation core):** decision-vs-truth for the proto orbit-line / icon surface. `GhostOrbitLinePatch.LogOrbitLineDecision` (the per-render-frame decision point that MOST branches route through; the transient grace-defer + missing-line branches do NOT re-record intent, which is harmless at freshness 0 - see below) records the intended `{lineActive, drawIcons, reason}` via new `MapRenderTrace.RecordLineIntent` (frame-stamped, gated). The end-of-frame `MapRenderProbe.Sample` (order 10000, same LateUpdate frame as the Postfix) reconciles via pure `MapRenderTrace.ReconcileLineState` and emits a Tier-C `decision-vs-truth` anomaly on a same-frame mismatch (KSP / another patch toggled line.active or drawIcons AFTER our Postfix). Same-frame staleness rule (`TryGetFreshLineIntent`, `IntentFreshnessFrames=0`) reconciles ONLY on the exact frame the intent was recorded; any other frame is dropped, never a false positive. **Final-review fix:** freshness was originally 1, which admitted a stale frame-N `OBJ` intent reconciled against frame-N+1's legitimate `drawIcons=NONE` from a grace-defer branch (a false `drawIcons-changed-after-decision`); freshness=0 closes it while preserving every true-positive (the only recorder is the same-frame Postfix, delta 0). +9 unit tests. Full suite green (13179).
- **Dependency RESOLVED (merge from main):** the parallel `line.active` reflection fix (PR #1007 - `MapRenderProbe.ReadLineActive` now reads via `OrbitRendererBase.OrbitLine`) and the body-relative icon-jump fix (PR #1009) merged to `main` and are now in this branch. So the line.active facet of decision-vs-truth / line-blink / polyline-overlap is LIVE alongside the drawIcons facet (the "unknown actual token -> skipped" guard remains as defence but no longer triggers). It activated automatically on merge - the second cut was built data-driven for exactly this. Full suite green after the merge (13188).
- **Done (polyline-orbit-overlap anomaly):** pure `MapRenderTrace.ReconcilePolylineOverlap(polylineOwns, lineActive, drawIcons)` flags the double-draw seam (proto orbit line + icon must not draw while the trajectory polyline owns the recording's non-orbital leg). Wired in `MapRenderProbe.Sample` via `GhostMapPresence.IsPolylineOwningGhostPhase(pid)` -> Tier-C `polyline-orbit-overlap` anomaly. A higher-level invariant check independent of the patch's intent. Both facets live (drawIcons always; line.active live after the PR #1007 OrbitLine-read fix merged from main). +5 unit tests.
- **Done (IMGUI marker-surface coverage):** new `MapRenderTrace.EmitMarker(surface, key, currentUT, details)` (gated + rate-limited per surface/key) instruments the two previously-uninstrumented marker surfaces - `ImguiLabeledMarker` (flight `ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers`) and `AtmosphericMarker` (TS `ParsekTrackingStation.DrawAtmosphericMarkers`) - with a `phase=MarkerDraw` line at each draw point. Decision-only by construction: these draw in OnGUI (after the order-10000 probe), so the projected world position IS the truth - no end-of-frame reconciliation. All five `RenderSurface`s are now instrumented. +2 unit tests.
- **Deferred (deliberate scope calls for this PR; final-review to adjudicate):**
  - **Shared `RenderTraceWindow` + recordingId-keyed window (cross-tracer correlation):** deferred. It touches the merged, separately-tested `GhostRenderTrace.cs` and cascades the window key from pid to recordingId across the probe + structural/anomaly emit sites, for marginal map-side value (a map ghost is ~1:1 with a recordingId, so within-tracer cross-surface grouping is near-equivalent to the existing pid keying; the real payoff is mesh+map correlation). The design's open-question explicitly offered the separate-registry alternative and the first reviews flagged the shared extraction as the riskiest piece. MapRenderTrace keeps its own pid-keyed window for now.
  - **Per-pid pre-event ring buffer:** deferred as an anomaly-lead-up nicety. The anomalies already open a forward detail window (subsequent frames emit `Snapshot` lines), so the "after" context is captured; the ring would add the "before" frames. Low marginal value vs the per-frame buffering cost.
- Clean-context review of the second cut (reconciliation core + overlap + IMGUI + the reverse-map foundation) before the PR.

---

## ~~OPEN~~ RESOLVED 2026-06-06 - v0.10.0 Rewind-to-Launch target never re-materialized its recorded vessel when the player did not re-fly it

- **Reported in playtest** (log `logs/2026-06-06_1819_rewind-no-spawn`): the player did a plain Rewind-to-Launch on a standalone landed "Kerbal X" flight (rec #10, `c15b0c4f`, terminal=Landed), then flew an unrelated fresh mission ("Jumping Flea", a NEW_FROM_FILE rollout) instead of re-flying Kerbal X. When the Kerbal X ghost replayed to its end, no real vessel spawned: `PlaybackCompleted index=10 ... needsSpawn=False`. The landed Kerbal X was stuck as a ghost for the rest of the session.
- **Root cause:** the #573 `same-recording` `SpawnSuppressedByRewind` marker (applied to the rewind-target recording during rewind OnLoad) was an ABSOLUTE spawn block in `GhostPlaybackLogic.ShouldBlockSpawnForRewindSuppression`, lifted in-session only by entering watch mode on the ghost. The block's purpose (#573/#589) is to stop the rewound vessel respawning next to a live RE-FLIGHT of the same launch. When the player does not re-fly it (and does not watch it), the block leaves a legitimately spawnable recording permanently un-materialized.
- **Why a naive fix would regress #573:** two independent agents cross-examined this. The original #573 phantom was a Re-Fly CHAIN leaf (downstream, pid-continuation), not the rewind target; under post-#589 code it is already `same-tree-future` and spawn-eligible. A "lift when no live launch identity matches" rule is true in the #573 repro too, so it would reintroduce the phantom. The safe discriminator is structural + live-craft combined.
- **Fix (union discriminator):** `ShouldBlockSpawnForRewindSuppression` now takes `liveSameLaunchVesselPresent` and lifts the `same-recording` block ONLY when the target is STANDALONE (`ChainId` empty) AND no live same-craft vessel is in the scene. Chain targets stay blocked (continuation tips can resurrect via the chain-tip spawn path = the #573 phantom class); any target stays blocked while a live same-craft vessel exists (a genuine re-fly / relaunch). The live-craft check uses craft-baked persistentId (deliberately broader than `LiveVesselIsRecordedLaunch`, so a relaunch of the same craft also counts and keeps the block), excluding Parsek's own map-presence ghosts. The marker is never mutated (watch-entry and next-rewind clears still apply). A `VerboseRateLimited` "[Rewind] same-recording spawn suppression lifted for standalone rewind target" line records each lift.
- **Scene-agnostic (follow-up):** the lift now applies in EVERY scene, not just flight. The flight-only first cut left the rewound vessel still stuck-as-ghost while the player watched it from the Tracking Station or Space Center (where real vessels do spawn at recording end). The live-craft scan + standalone/marker guard were extracted into shared `GhostPlaybackLogic.AnyLiveRealVesselSharesRecordedCraft` + `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveRewindSuppressionLiveLaunchPresence` (one implementation, no divergent copies); `ShouldSpawnAtKscEnd` (Space Center) and `GhostMapPresence.ShouldSpawnAtTrackingStationEnd` (Tracking Station) now compute `liveSameLaunchVesselPresent` through it exactly like the flight spawn loop. The baked-pid scan reads `FlightGlobals.Vessels` (populated in Flight and the Tracking Station; possibly empty/null at the Space Center, where the null guard reports no live craft, which is the correct outcome since a genuine re-flight only exists in the flight scene and can never collide at KSC). The scan is deliberately uncached (unlike `RealVesselExists`) because the KSC path has no per-frame cache invalidation. Conservative-default callers (`MergeDialog.CanPersistVessel` preview, the proximity spawn loop) are unchanged.
- **Discoverability:** the Rewind-to-Launch confirmation dialog (`RecordingsTableUI.ShowRewindConfirmation`) now states the flight replays as a ghost and its recorded vessel reappears at the end unless you re-fly it (watch the ghost to bring it back). The stale "lifted only by watch-entry" doc-comment on the predicate was corrected.
- **Tests:** `RewindSpawnSuppressionTests` covers the pure predicate (standalone + no live craft -> lifts and spawns; standalone + live craft present -> stays blocked; chain target + no live craft -> stays blocked) plus 3 KSC-path tests through `ShouldSpawnAtKscEnd` (same three cases, live-craft scan injected via `SetLiveSameCraftOverrideForTesting`), all asserting the marker is preserved. The Tracking Station and KSC `FlightGlobals` scan itself is not xUnit-reachable (Unity-only); it is covered by the shared resolver tests + manual playtest. Full xUnit suite green (13580).
- **Status:** RESOLVED and playtest-confirmed (PR #1070). The 2026-06-06 20:29 Tracking Station playtest (logs `logs/2026-06-06_2030_rewind-scene-agnostic`) shows the exact bug-report recording (rec `c15b0c4f` "Kerbal X" #10, standalone Landed) lift the block (`[Rewind] same-recording spawn suppression lifted`) and then materialize via the TS handoff (`[GhostMap] Tracking-station handoff spawned #10 "Kerbal X" pid=89618322`, a fresh KSP-unique spawn pid, not the baked 3620499050). The subsequent SPACECENTER load correctly reports rec #10 `already spawned (VesselSpawned=true)` with no duplicate.

## ~~OPEN~~ RESOLVED 2026-06-06 (off-orbit fix true for ALL members; coverage gap closed; cutover COMPLETE at S4 - legacy ownership deleted + `mapRenderDirectorDrive` gate dropped; 8f icon-floor deletion REASSESSED + the floor KEPT as a permanent no-conic fallback) - v0.10.0 Looped ghost map icon rotated ~96.5 deg off its orbit lines (root cause CONFIRMED 2026-06-02; Phase-8a epoch-bake fix, now the single modular render path)

- Reported in playtest: on a looped re-aimed mission ("Kerbal X", rec 30), the map icon glided the parking orbit and the orbit-raise polyline correctly, then when the circular loiter orbit appeared the icon jumped ~90 deg to the wrong point on it instead of continuing from where the ascent ended. Permanent (not a transient).
- **Diagnosis (instrumented, not guessed):** added `GhostIconTruth` (mna + inc/LAN/argPe + body-relative `orbit.pos` + body-fixed lat/lon), a full-rate `GhostIconJump` step detector, and a `GhostIconDiverge` detector comparing the orbit-line longitude (`orbitLon`, computed fresh from `orbit.pos` this frame) against the vessel-transform longitude (`transformLon`, from `GetWorldPos3D`). Findings, in order: (1) `orbit.pos` inertial longitude is perfectly smooth across the seam (21.88 -> 22.66 -> ...), so the orbit math and the effUT/`DecompressSpanUT` clock are NOT the bug, and the compressor stays innocent; (2) the `GetWorldPos3D` lat/lon "jump" was a stale-within-frame read (red herring); (3) the real divergence: at the loiter takeover `orbitLon` = 161.78 (orbit line) vs `transformLon` = 64.94 (raise end), `lonDiv` = 96.84 deg, at a loop shift of 845,044,936 s.
- **Root cause:** a looped recording replays its orbits at the RAW recorded epoch under a live-frame shift. The orbit keeps its recorded INERTIAL orientation (LAN), but the reference body keeps rotating, so over the shift Kerbin turns 845044936 / 21549.425 = 39214.27 rev -> 0.268 rev = 96.62 deg, and the inertial orbit's BODY-FIXED projection at the live clock is rotated 96.62 deg from the recording. The orbit-raise gap-glide is replayed from body-fixed surface points (surface-locked, no rotation), so the orbit line and those points desync by exactly the body's rotation over the shift. Measured 96.84 deg = 96.62 deg body-rotation (the bug) + 0.27 deg legitimate forward orbital motion.
- **Deeper cause (why the shift is not a whole rotation):** this is a re-aimed INTERPLANETARY mission (Kerbin -> Duna). Its relaunch is timed for the Duna TRANSFER WINDOW, not for the launch-site-under-recorded-orbit alignment. The "relaunch when the launch site has rotated back under the recorded orbit" alignment and the transfer-window timing generally cannot be satisfied at the same time, so `kerbinRot(shift)` is some arbitrary residual (96.62 deg here), not ~0. With a whole-rotation shift the body-fixed raise and the inertial orbits would coincide and there would be no teleport; the interplanetary re-aim breaks that.
- **Why this is a single-frame seam, not multiple bugs:** in the recording the raise injection and the loiter start are the SAME point; the 96.6 deg gap is purely a rendering-frame seam between the surface-locked raise and the inertial orbits. Everything else (parking orbit, loiter orbit, hyperbolic escape, ghost mesh, sibling-stage trajectories) is in one consistent inertial frame. The raise gap-glide is the only odd-one-out. The loiter->escape boundary is already gap-free (both inertial); the ONLY seam is raise->loiter.

### CONFIRMED root cause (2026-06-02, `angleIconVsOrbitEff` metric + KSP decompile) and the implemented fix
- **What the metric proved:** with `mapRenderTracing` on, the gated `icon-off-orbit` anomaly logged (steady state, s15 "Duna One", pid 2333335827) `angleIconVsOrbitEff=96.50 angleEffVsLive=96.73 lonIcon=31.11 lonOrbitEff=-65.39 lonOrbitLive=31.34 iconR=731903 orbitEffR=731903`. Three facts: (1) `iconR == orbitEffR` -> pure rotation, same orbital altitude (NOT a body-fixed surface point); (2) `lonIcon ~= lonOrbitLive`, NOT `lonOrbitEff` -> the icon sits at the orbit evaluated at the LIVE clock, while the line is drawn at effUT; (3) `angleIconVsOrbitEff ~= angleEffVsLive` -> the whole gap IS the orbital phase advance over the loop shift. So the bug is a PHASE (clock) mismatch, not orbit elements and not a body-fixed projection.
- **Why the effUT drive never reached the icon:** decompiling `Vessel.GetWorldPos3D` -> returns `CoMD`; `VesselPrecalculate` rebuilds a packed non-landed vessel's `CoMD = mainBody.position + orbitDriver.pos` EVERY FixedUpdate, and `orbitDriver.pos` is re-propagated at the LIVE Planetarium clock. So `GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch`'s `UpdateFromUT(effUT)` + `SetPosition` is overwritten by KSP's live re-propagation; the icon always ends up at `orbit(liveUT)` regardless. The raw-epoch + per-frame-effUT-drive architecture was built on the premise that the drive controls the icon - it does not.
- **The fix (Phase-8a director-drive, gated `mapRenderDirectorDrive`, default on as of 2026-06-05):** bake the loop shift into the orbit EPOCH (`StockConicTreatment.SeedAndDriveLive`: `SetOrbit(..., epoch + shift, ...)`) and propagate at the LIVE clock. Then `M(live) = MAE + n*(live - epoch - shift) = MAE + n*(effUT - epoch)` = the recorded mean anomaly at effUT, so the live re-propagation (whatever rebuilds `orbitDriver.pos`) lands on the recorded phase. The icon rides the same orbit the line is drawn from. This is the IDENTICAL phase the legacy effUT-drive intended (raw epoch propagated at `live - shift` gives the same mean anomaly), so it is not a new orbit and moves PHASE only - LAN/inc/argPe untouched, so it is NOT the reverted per-element LAN-rotation dead-end. Re-seeded every frame in the icon-drive Prefix (which fires per FixedUpdate), so no rate-limited-reseed stall (the sawtooth the raw-epoch scheme avoided). `GhostOrbitArcPatch` clips the arc at the LIVE bounds when the epoch is baked (via `ShadowRenderDriver.IsDirectorDriveActive`; the earlier per-frame `IsDirectorEpochBaked` stamp was superseded - see Playtest 1 below), keeping the line and icon in one clock; the `MapRenderProbe` off-orbit metric compares against the live-clock orbit when the gate is on, so `angleIconVsOrbitEff -> ~0` is the success signal.
- **Hyperbolic-escape LINE clip (coverage-gap Category 1) CLOSED:** the icon already rode the hyperbolic escape correctly (`GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch` drives ecc>=1 at effUT), but the orbit LINE was not clipped - `GhostOrbitArcPatch.Prefix` bailed to stock for `ecc>=1`, so stock drew the FULL open asymptote-to-asymptote hyperbola across the whole map instead of clipping it to the recorded segment window. Fix: the patch now clips the open hyperbolic arc via the same eccentric-anomaly path as the ellipse (the stock Orbit anomaly/position helpers `EccentricAnomalyAtUT` / `GetTrueAnomaly` / `getPositionFromEccAnomalyWithSemiMinorAxis` are hyperbolic-safe), gating off the three periodicity-only steps (the full-period early-return - a hyperbolic period is +Infinity; the periapsis wraparound - a hyperbola is monotonic in anomaly; and the elliptical `r=sma*(1-ecc*cos E)` diagnostic, replaced by the hyperbolic `r=sma*(1-ecc*cosh H)` form), and keeping the same director-drive-vs-effUT frame selection so the clipped line and the icon stay in lockstep. Pure math split into `ArcAnomalyMath` (unit-tested); in-game test `HyperbolicArcClipBoundsLineToSegmentWindow`.
- **Tests:** in-game `DirectorDriveEpochBakePlacesIconOnRecordedPhase` (RuntimeTests, GhostMap, FLIGHT) drives the real "Kerbal X Probe" Kerbin orbit + the evidence shift through `SeedAndDrive` (raw, the reference) and `SeedAndDriveLive` (epoch-bake) and asserts the live-clock position lands within 0.1 deg of the recorded phase while the raw-epoch-at-live position (the bug) is > 1 deg off. `ShouldSkipReaimSegment` pure tests. Full xUnit suite green (13272).
- **Playtest 1 (2026-06-02, gate on):** "Kerbal X Probe" (elliptical Kerbin orbit) icon now sits on its line - the epoch-bake works. "Kerbal X" (hyperbolic Kerbin escape) did NOT, because the shadow skipped it: the re-aim skip was PER WHOLE TRAJECTORY (`TrajectoryHasHeliocentricLeg` saw the later Sun transfer leg and skipped the entire member), so its faithful hyperbolic Kerbin escape never got a seed. FIX (follow-up): re-aim skip is now PER ACTIVE SEGMENT (`ShouldSkipReaimSegment(intent.Visible, scene.IsStarBody(intent.FrameBodyName))`), so the faithful Kerbin escape / destination arrival legs of a single-recording interplanetary flight ARE director-driven and only the heliocentric leg is skipped. Same playtest also exposed a probe artifact (the off-orbit metric read ~118 deg on no-FixedUpdate frames because the per-frame `IsDirectorEpochBaked` stamp went stale); replaced with the seed-based `ShadowRenderDriver.IsDirectorDriveActive` (keyed on the seed the shadow refreshes in Update every render frame), shared by the icon-drive + arc-clip + probe so they never disagree, and removed the stamp machinery.
- **Metric framing (per review):** `angleIconVsOrbitEff ~= 0` under the gate proves the icon RIDES ITS OWN LINE (both sides evaluate the same orbit at the live clock); it does not by itself prove the icon sits on the RECORDED phase - that is what the in-game `DirectorDriveEpochBakePlacesIconOnRecordedPhase` test proves (independent raw-epoch-at-effUT reference). Use the metric as the necessary in-game ride-the-line signal and the visual + the test for phase correctness.
- **Playtest 2 (2026-06-02): decouple-seam flash, fixed at looped playback (NOT the recorder).** With both icons riding their lines, a transient remained: right at the Kerbal X / Probe separation, Kerbal X flashed ~90 deg off for a few frames before snapping onto the hyperbolic escape. Cause (confirmed from `.prec` data): the recorder stored ONE parking-orbit coast as FOUR same-orbit OrbitSegments (identical sma/ecc/lan/argPe to 6 sig figs, split at background/foreground transitions), the last only ~40s. The loop's span clock (`DecompressSpanUT`) compresses time, so the head sweeps that 40s fragment out of its bounds in under a render frame -> a transient `GhostOrbitArcPatch` "no orbit bounds" gap where the icon shows the stock full ellipse at the wrong phase. On the faithful first play (real time, shift 0) the same fragment is invisible, so this is loop-only. **Fix (recordings stay IMMUTABLE - hard rule):** `ReaimSegmentAssembler.CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` merges consecutive same-orbit fragments (predicate `TrajectoryMath.AreOrbitSegmentsEquivalentForMapDisplay` + `isPredicted` guard) into one continuous segment, in `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` (the existing loop-only in-memory segment edit). Its output feeds BOTH the new shadow pipeline (`ReaimedTrajectory.OrbitSegments`) and the legacy path (`ResolveEffectiveMapOrbitSegments`), so the fix is not gated and covers both renderers; the escape burn (sma differs by millions) is never merged. Scoped to re-aim members (covers the s15 repro); a non-re-aim fragmented-parking loop would need the same helper wired into the faithful branch (follow-up). Tests: 5 `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` / `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` cases; xUnit green (13277).
- **Playtest 3 (2026-06-02): the coalesce reached only the LEGACY path - the chain needed it too.** First coalesce attempt put the merge only in `ReaimSegmentAssembler.ReplaceHeliocentricLeg`. Log proved it fixed the legacy bounds (the loiter `Map-visible orbit window` became one ~11.4M-second span) but the NEW shadow/director chain still showed `segs=36 conic=20` (unchanged) and the flash persisted with the gate ON (`angleIconVsOrbitEff=96.5` on the loiter at a transition). Root cause: the two renderers do NOT share an upstream list - the legacy path resolves via `ReaimPlaybackResolver`/`ResolveEffectiveMapOrbitSegments`, but `ShadowRenderDriver` -> `ChainAssembler.Build` reads the RAW `traj.OrbitSegments` directly (the second opinion's assumption that one list feeds both was wrong). Fix: moved `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments` to `TrajectoryMath` (next to its predicate) and call it in BOTH consumers - `ChainAssembler.Build` (raw recorded segments, for the chain/director) and `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` (the re-aim list, for legacy). Added a `ChainAssembler` integration test (4 fragments -> 1 coalesced StockConic + the escape kept separate). xUnit green (13278).
- **Playtest 4 (2026-06-03): escape-burn icon TELEPORT, fixed by gate-scoped TracedPath suppression.** With the loiter fixed, the icon teleported loiter -> a long isolated eccentric arc (it dwelt on) -> hyperbolic. Tracer evidence (was there all along, I missed it): `icon-jump` ~1.18 Mm vs ~1 km expected, `polyline-orbit-overlap` (orbit-line-active-while-polyline-owns), and `body-orbit` walking through orbits NOT in the recording (ecc 0.0013 -> 0.73 -> 0.88 -> 1.07 -> 1.19). Mechanism (Opus-confirmed): the escape burn is a recorded ORBIT-RAISE GAP - the policy reseeds the proto orbit from per-frame state vectors (the synthesized eccentric arcs); the chain marks the region `TracedPath`, so the director-drive is inactive AND there are no segment bounds, so `GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch` early-returns to stock, which propagates the reseeded orbit at the live clock and teleports the icon. The `visible-body-frame` <-> `polyline-owns-phase` flicker re-shows the proto icon every other frame. **Fix (gated, Option A):** `ShadowRenderDriver` stamps `tracedPathByPid` when the active intent is `Visible && TracedPath`; `IsDirectorTracedPathActive(pid, frame)` (gate + freshness, mirrors `IsDirectorDriveActive`) is read at TWO sites - `GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch.Prefix` BEFORE the no-bounds early-return (suppress the proto icon so stock can't teleport it) and `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` as the FIRST branch (kill `line.active`/`drawIcons`, pre-empting the flicker + grace). The autonomous polyline already draws the burn; `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon` routes the marker pass to it. Recomputed per frame -> the icon re-shows cleanly at the next StockConic (hyperbolic). NOT the full Phase-8b TracedPath cutover - a narrow gate-scoped negative assertion; default play untouched. Decision input covered by `DecideForGhost_InAscentPoints_IsTracedPathVisible`; validated in-game. Also: the tracer now emits a loud `icon-teleport` line (jump as a multiple of expected + from/to orbit) and rate-limits `polyline-orbit-overlap`.
- **Playtest 5 (2026-06-03): escape-burn polyline + icon/label FIXED by conic-anchor (CONFIRMED in-game).** The isolated segment was the trajectory POLYLINE (the autonomous `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer`, body-fixed via `GetWorldSurfacePosition` = live body rotation) drawn ~96 deg off the loiter/hyperbola lines while the conics are loop-aware-inertial (Phase-8a director epoch+shift). **Pinned with a same-frame `Seam-gap PIN` diagnostic (now removed):** at the burn leg, `gapBodyFixed`~1100km AND `gapInertial`~1150km vs the recorded-conic seam (`getPositionAtUT`), and in the early region `gapBodyFixed=0km` while `gapInertial=646km`. So (a) the segment IS a loop-shift body rotation off the faithful conic, and (b) the longitude-lift (`GetRelSurfacePosition(lat, lon+initialRotation+recordedUT*360/period, alt)`) is WRONG everywhere - the same lift the reverted fix AND Fix A's gap-glide use, so both were doomed (the state-vector method seeds at that same lifted position). The faithful target is the recorded conic itself (it stores inertial Kepler elements directly, never round-trips through body-fixed lat/lon). **Fix (conic-anchor, `TryAnchorLegToConicSeam`):** for a vacuum maneuver bracketed by a conic on BOTH sides (escape burn / orbit raise / circularization, via the pure `FindBracketingOrbitSegments`), calibrate the body-fixed-vs-conic rotation DIRECTLY from `getPositionAtUT` at both seam endpoints (`Quaternion.FromToRotation`, the minimal rotation between two same-latitude rays IS the spin rotation - no explicit axis), `Slerp` it across the leg by recorded-time fraction, applied in scaled space to the already-captured (jitter-free) points. Self-calibrating: a launch ascent (no preceding conic) / descent-to-surface (no following conic) is left body-fixed, and where body-fixed already matches the conic the rotation is ~identity (no-op) - so it does NOT regress what the reverted lift broke. `Anchor leg: ... residualStart/End` confirmed **0km** on every leg in-game. **Marker (icon + label, `TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` + `ParsekUI`):** during the polyline phase the labeled marker samples the leg's exact per-frame DRAWN (anchored) points at the head's recorded-time fraction (scaled->world), so it rides the corrected line by construction (no separate rotation to drift); `Marker DRAWN ... ridesPolyline=True` confirms. NOT the full Phase-8b/8c cutover (the autonomous renderer still owns the polyline + the marker still draws via the ParsekUI path), but the visible bug is fixed and the heliocentric transfer segment also reads correct. **Still to validate:** Duna SOI entry / arrival (capture burn should conic-anchor like the escape; descent should stay body-fixed).
- **Playtest 6 (2026-06-03): conic-anchor OVER-REACHED on the Duna/Ike arrival; guarded (multi-agent workflow investigation).** The escape-burn anchor regressed the Duna arrival: `TryAnchorLegToConicSeam` had NO guard and anchored every leg bracketed by two conics, but the Duna/Ike arrival legs are bracketed by ARRIVAL HYPERBOLAS (ecc 1.70 / 18.60); `getPositionAtUT` on an inbound arm far from periapsis lands the seam tens of Mm from the leg, so `FromToRotation` swung the leg (and the marker riding it) to the wrong arm. Confirmed in-game: `Anchor leg` residuals 46543km (Duna leg 11), 599km (Ike leg 12), 551km, 430->3041km (vs 0km at Kerbin), all drawn active. CRITICAL: an "elliptical-only / ecc<1" guard is INSUFFICIENT (the alt-60km leg is elliptical-bracketed yet 430-3041km off); the RADIAL RESIDUAL is the necessary-and-sufficient discriminator. **Fix:** pure `IsSeamResidualTooLarge` (reject when the seam-vs-leg radial residual > 50km absolute or > 5% of the leg radius); the residual is now computed BEFORE mutating `scratchScaledSpace`, so a rejected leg stays body-fixed and `TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` falls back to the body-fixed head. Kerbin escape still anchors (0km). `Anchor leg:` line enriched (anchored=true/false, bracketing sma/ecc, radii, rotation angles); new `Polyline draw-set CHANGED ... drawn=N warp=Mx recs=[...]` change-emit for the Bug-3 double-line. 6 `IsSeamResidualTooLarge` unit tests. **SEPARATE pre-existing bugs from the same Duna run (NOT the anchor; Root B = inertial orbit/icon under loop shift):** (Bug 2) the low circular Duna orbit overshoots the body-fixed landing site by ~131 deg, then the marker teleports onto the descent polyline. NOT inherent and NOT the anchor: this is the deferred cross-parent destination-SOI arrival-UT alignment phase, now tracked as its own OPEN entry below (see "Looped re-aimed interplanetary LANDING: destination not rotation-aligned across the loop shift"). (Bug 3) a double landing polyline at 1x: NOT the anchor (descent legs are unanchored); the one captured `drawn=2` frame is two distinct surface vessels (lander + EVA kerbal) co-drawing at the relaunch seam, candidate mechanism the inclusive-both-ends head-UT gate at a contiguous A.end==B.start boundary (visible at 1x where playback dwells, gone under warp) - needs the new drawn>=2 emit to confirm.

### Approaches tried / rejected (do NOT repeat)
- **(REVERTED) Rotate the orbit node by `kerbinRot(shift)`** (`ApplyLoopShiftLanRotation` in `ApplyOrbitToVessel`, non-star bodies). Math sound, Opus-confirmed sign, BUT it rotates only the map OrbitDriver orbit (line + map icon), not the flight-scene ghost MESH, the recorded trajectory POINTS, or the OTHER stages. In playtest: rotated loiter line inconsistent with the un-rotated mesh; hyperbolic escape line rotated off its own ghost; a sibling-stage trajectory rendered in the wrong place. Reverted. Lesson: a per-element transform is invalid; any transform must apply to the ENTIRE ghost rendering consistently.
- **(REJECTED) Phase offset on the loiter icon/mesh** (drive at `effUT - dt` so the loiter starts at the body-fixed raise end). No speed change, but it only MOVES the teleport to the loiter->escape boundary: the offset loiter ends 96.6 deg short of the inertial escape, so the jump reappears there. Whack-a-mole - the raise (body-fixed) and escape (inertial) bracket the loiter and are themselves 96.6 deg apart, so the loiter can match one side but not both.
- **(REJECTED) Catch-up sweep** (extend the gap-glide to sweep the icon across the 96.6 deg gap into the loiter). The icon would move FASTER than the raise before it and the loiter after it - a visible speed discontinuity. User explicitly rejected ("fast sweep is not acceptable").
- **(REJECTED) Polyline bridge only** (draw a connector arc across the seam without moving the icon). Cosmetic only - the icon still teleports to its true loiter point; the connector just sits behind it. Does not fix the jump.
- **(REVERTED 2026-06-03) Render orbital-vacuum polyline legs inertial** (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer` inertial leg reconstruction by `TrackSection.environment`, commit `1c6f1293`). Two failures in playtest: (1) it did NOT remove the visible pre-hyperbolic isolated polyline segment the user reported (the bug it targeted persisted), and (2) it REGRESSED the loiter-phase icon - the marker was no longer drawn where it should be right before the circular loiter orbit. Reverted whole to the body-fixed baseline. Lesson: the visible long isolated segment was NOT confirmed to be a body-fixed-vs-inertial rotation of the polyline; do not re-attempt an inertial polyline rewrite until the segment's identity is pinned from a log against a concrete frame. The icon placement is coupled to the polyline draw (the marker rides the polyline head), so any polyline draw change must be validated against the loiter-phase icon, not only the burn leg. **RESOLVED (Playtest 5, above):** the segment IS a loop-shift body rotation, but the longitude-LIFT this fix used is wrong everywhere (proven by the `Seam-gap PIN` diagnostic: 646-1150km off the recorded conic). The working fix anchors the leg to the recorded conic seam (`getPositionAtUT`) directly, NOT via the lift; the marker rides the anchored line by sampling the drawn points. So the lift reconstruction stays a dead end; the conic-anchor is the correct path.

### Candidate real fixes (A IMPLEMENTED but did NOT fix the symptom; B not pursued)
- **A (IMPLEMENTED in branch fix-inertial-gap-glide / PR #1012, but playtest shows it did NOT fix the symptom): render the ORBIT-RAISE gap-glide in the INERTIAL frame.** The orbit-raise is an orbital vacuum maneuver (parking -> loiter, ~131 km); replaying it from surface-locked body-fixed points was believed to be the bug. `UpdateGhostOrbitFromStateVectors` (GhostMapPresence.cs) now reconstructs each gap point's recorded INERTIAL position from its recorded UT + recorded body rotation (incl. `initialRotation`) via `OrbitReseed.TryFromHistoricalLatLonAltAndRecordedVelocityWithEpoch`, and seeds the orbit at the loop-shifted epoch (`point.ut + loopEpochShiftSeconds == liveUT`) so loop phase is preserved exactly as the prior body-fixed `FromWorldPosAndRecordedVelocity(ut + shift)` call did. So parking -> raise -> loiter -> escape is one inertial frame: no teleport, no new seam, no speed change, nothing else moves. GATED to orbital vacuum gaps via the `orbit-raise-gap-points` reason (the pure `ShouldSeedGapGlideInertial(reason, branch)` predicate, reason + Absolute branch); the from-GROUND launch ascent has NO preceding OrbitSegment so it never reaches `ShouldDriveGapFromPoints` and stays surface-locked (the rocket climbs from the rotating pad). On any decline (non-finite rotation period / helper declines) it Warns and falls back to the body-fixed seed (never strands the icon). Verified at the unit level: (1) the Absolute gap points carry the recorded UT (the update-state-vector log prints `ut=...` per gap point); (2) the parking->raise handoff stays continuous (the parking segment is inertial, the raise glide is now inertial too). **PLAYTEST RESULT (2026-06-01 ~21:34, DLL ca59a3a0): did NOT fix the symptom.** `seedFrame=inertial` confirmed firing on the gap points, but the ~90 deg / CCW icon rotation is UNCHANGED and `polyline-orbit-overlap` is still 58 (identical to pre-fix). The orbit-raise gap is only ~2 frames of the affected window, so it was the wrong target. The user clarifies the bug is the PROTO-VESSEL ICON sitting off its OWN orbit line (rotated CCW), NOT the polyline. Root cause still under investigation; a temporary `IconVsOrbit` diagnostic was added to `MapRenderProbe` (uncommitted) to measure `angleIconVsOrbitEff` (icon position vs the orbit's own predicted position) definitively.
- **B (NOT pursued): align the re-aim relaunch so the launch site is back under the recorded orbit** (`kerbinRot(shift)` ~ whole rotations), removing the frame mismatch at the source. Conflicts with the interplanetary transfer-window timing - generally cannot satisfy both, so this may only be partially achievable. Documented for completeness; superseded by Fix A.

### Constraints / notes for the next attempt
- Do NOT rotate orbit elements in isolation; do NOT introduce a speed discontinuity. Any fix must keep the icon, the orbit line, the ghost mesh, and the other stages in ONE consistent frame.
- `ReaimLoiterCompressor` and the effUT/`DecompressSpanUT` clock are validated INNOCENT (orbit.pos glides smoothly across the seam). Do not chase them.
- Diagnostics: `GhostIconTruth` (which logged `orbitLon`/`transformLon`/`lonDiv` + inc/LAN/argPe + body-relative pos) and the full-rate Warn detectors `GhostIconJump` / `GhostIconDiverge` have now all been removed - the MapRenderTrace MVP (PR #1005) removed the last of them (`GhostIconTruth`) as a redundant always-on diagnostic. The gated `MapRenderProbe` (enable the `mapRenderTracing` setting) covers body-orbit / line / world-pos truth + a Tier-C icon-jump anomaly. **The icon-vs-orbit divergence is now re-added (branch `maprender-icon-vs-orbit-diag`):** the gated `MapRenderProbe` emits a Tier-C `icon-off-orbit` anomaly (pure predicate `MapRenderTrace.IsIconOffOrbit`, threshold `IconOffOrbitMinAngleDeg = 1 deg`) measuring `angleIconVsOrbitEff` - the angle between the icon's body-relative position and the orbit's OWN predicted body-relative position at the drive clock `effUT = liveUT - loopShift` - plus `lonIcon`/`lonOrbitEff`/`lonOrbitLive` longitude proxies and `inc`/`LAN`/`argPe`/`sma`/`ecc`. This catches the static off-orbit offset that `icon-jump` (no per-frame delta) and `line-blink` (line stays active) are blind to. Gated to the actively-driven icon (`!GhostMapPresence.IsIconSuppressed(pid)`): a suppressed / clamped icon is parked at an endpoint UT rather than driven at `effUT`, so checking it would be a guaranteed false positive, and a degenerate near-zero orbit position is skipped (`Vector3d.Angle` of a zero vector is a phantom 90 deg). The full inc/LAN/argPe-vs-transform reconciliation layer (decision-side) remains the deferred second cut.
- Reference data: recording `61e9177193444e329247d0e8288cf91e` member 30 ("Kerbal X"). Logs: `logs/2026-06-01_1638_diverge-check` (the 96.84 deg measurement), `logs/2026-06-01_1701_lan-fix-validate` (LAN-fix validation), `logs/2026-06-01_1734_hyperbolic-escape-regression` (hyperbolic escape).
- **Status:** ROOT CAUSE CONFIRMED 2026-06-02 + FIX VALIDATED IN PLAYTEST 2026-06-05, NOW DEFAULT-ON (branch `maprender-cutover`: `mapRenderDirectorDrive` default flipped to true). The `angleIconVsOrbitEff` metric + the `Vessel.GetWorldPos3D`/`VesselPrecalculate` decompile proved the icon resolves at the LIVE clock (KSP rebuilds `CoMD = body.position + orbitDriver.pos` from a live re-propagation every FixedUpdate), so the legacy effUT drive never controls it - the icon sits at `orbit(live)`, the line at `orbit(effUT)`, gap = the orbital phase over the loop shift. Fix: `StockConicTreatment.SeedAndDriveLive` bakes the shift into the EPOCH and propagates at live (phase-only; LAN untouched), `GhostOrbitArcPatch` clips at live bounds when baked, the probe measures against the live-clock orbit. Validated 2026-06-05 (s15 "Duna One", `mapRenderDirectorDrive` + `mapRenderTracing` on): `angleIconVsOrbitEff` collapses to ~1-3 deg (min 1.02) on director-driven frames vs the ~96.5 deg baseline, icon visually on its line. KNOWN RESIDUAL / next step (cutover Step 2, see `docs/dev/plans/map-ts-render-rewrite-phases.md`): ~1/3 of sampled director decisions (83/242 in the validation log) still fall back to the legacy effUT drive (no fresh seed: the deliberately-skipped re-aim/overlap members + the hyperbolic-escape ecc>=1 segment), which is where the remaining >45 deg anomalies cluster. Default-on is safe because those frames are byte-identical to the prior legacy path; deleting the legacy path (Phase 8e) requires closing that coverage gap first. Fix A (PR #1012 inertial gap-glide) stands as an internal correctness change but was the wrong target (the gap is ~2 frames); the LAN-rotation attempt stays reverted; Fix B (re-aim relaunch alignment) not pursued. The earlier "body rotation projection" root-cause framing is superseded by the confirmed PHASE-clock diagnosis above.
- **RESOLVED (2026-06-06): the icon-off-orbit fix is now true for every member through the single modular pipeline.** Integration 1 (PR #1048 + pan-stability #1049/#1050) drives the re-aim interplanetary transfer / escape / arrival through the Director, so the heliocentric leg's icon rides its own line (`angleIconVsOrbitEff` -> ~0) instead of falling back to the legacy live-clock drive. Integration 2 (overlap rendering: 2a #1051, 2b per-instance #1053 / #1058 / #1060, logging hygiene #1063 / #1064) drives overlap members through the Director and renders one icon (orbital) or one polyline marker (suborbital) per live overlap instance in both the map and Tracking Station. Integration 3 folded in the minimal pid-0 atmospheric-only coverage surface, closing the last legacy-fallback gap. Phase 8e then deleted the 8a-8d legacy *ownership* fallbacks (the autonomous Driver DECIDE-walk + `activeLegRecordings`) and the S4 gate-drop dropped the `mapRenderDirectorDrive` gate, so every member now drives through the Director and the off-orbit anomaly is fixed for all members (the cutover is COMPLETE at S4). The icon floor + `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon` + `IsIconSuppressed` were KEPT as a permanent no-conic / suppressed-icon fallback (the 8f reassessment - they are the only marker signal for below-atmosphere / off-arc / no-bounds ghosts), not deleted. Per-PR breakdown: `docs/dev/plans/maprender-rewrite-status.md`.
