## ~~v0.10.0 Map/TS render rewrite: Phase 8e cutover + S4 gate-drop + 8f closeout + two advisory re-tests~~ (DONE)

- **DONE:** the modular map/TS Director pipeline (chain assemble -> sample -> decide -> treatment -> draw) is the single render path. Phases 8a-8d (per-surface cutover), Integration 1 (re-aim rendering), and Integration 2 (per-instance overlap rendering) merged; Integration 3 folded the minimal pid-0 atmospheric-only coverage surface into the pipeline (proving the Director's accounted set is a superset of the autonomous walk's drawn set). Phase 8e then deleted the 8a-8d legacy *ownership* fallbacks (the autonomous Driver `CommittedRecordings` DECIDE-walk + `activeLegRecordings`), keeping the `onPreCull` draw as the sanctioned shared polyline host, with a grep-audit confirming `activeLegRecordings` has no readers; the S4 gate-drop dropped the `mapRenderDirectorDrive` gate, leaving a single modular system. **CUTOVER COMPLETE at S4.** The original 8f deletion of the icon floor / the legacy effUT icon drive / `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon` / `IsIconSuppressed` / the orbit-line grace fields was REASSESSED (data-backed) and NOT done: those are the ONLY marker signal for below-atmosphere descent, off-arc / window-clamp, and no-bounds (loiter / terminal / atmospheric) ghosts (the Director's TracedPath / polyline path does NOT own those), and the icon floor is the legitimate no-conic fallback for no-bounds ghosts; deleting them would regress those to a blank icon. So the no-conic suppress+marker is a KEPT permanent Director fallback. The 8f closeout RETIRED the `IconFloorGapCounter` S0 instrument (its "floor must reach 0 before deletion" premise no longer holds); the `unaccounted-drawn-recording` polyline-coverage instrument STAYS. Full per-PR breakdown: `docs/dev/plans/maprender-rewrite-status.md`; phase plan: `docs/dev/plans/map-ts-render-rewrite-phases.md`.
- **Advisory re-tests (closed):** the two non-blocking re-tests carried from the overlap validation - a Tracking-Station visual confirm of per-instance overlap markers, and an orbital-overlap ProtoVessel-churn check at high time warp - are closed.

## Post-cutover map/TS render backlog (next version)

The map/TS render cutover is COMPLETE (see the DONE entry above): the modular Director pipeline is the single render path; this file has no open map/TS render bugs (the render entries above are all RESOLVED/CLOSED). This is the consolidated list of what remains in this area for a future version. NOTHING here blocks the current release.

**1. Re-aim destination phase-lock for looped INTERPLANETARY missions (the one substantial piece).** Re-aim aligns the launch body but not the destination body's rotation/phase across the loop shift, so a looped interplanetary arrival drifts. "Duna One" is closed; the generalization (non-synchronous moons, destination loiter, 2+ moons, atmo-direct entry) is the deferred Phase 4 - see the "DUNA ONE CLOSED ... Phase-4 GENERALIZATION still deferred" entry immediately below. WARNING: this sits on the re-aim seam, a known high-cost area - build the failing multi-moon test and measure before any knob math, and treat "the faithful render is good enough" as a valid outcome (do not stack speculative fixes on a working baseline).

**2. Robustness / needs-in-game confirms (deferred during the cutover, non-blocking).**

**3. Minor polish (low value, all currently suppressed or sub-visual).**

## ~~OPEN~~ DUNA ONE CLOSED (per-loop arrival hold SHIPPED in PR #1030, validated 2026-06-05); Phase-4 GENERALIZATION still deferred - v0.10.0 Looped re-aimed interplanetary LANDING: destination rotation-alignment across the loop shift (Bug 2, s15 "Duna One")

- **Tracked as M-MIS-2 (P4/P5/P6 + S4 for the supported shape), M-MIS-3 (high-inclination / high-eccentricity targets), M-MIS-6 (multi-moon / Jool window alignment), and M-MIS-7 (intra-SOI re-aim)** in the Missions feature completion milestones at the top of this file.
- **STATUS (2026-06-06): Duna One CLOSED.** PR #1030 shipped the destination-SOI arrival HOLD (base: `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeArrivalAlignHoldSeconds` / `ApplyArrivalHoldToPhase` threaded through `TryComputeSpanLoopUT`, built by `ArrivalHoldPlanner.ComputeArrivalHold` from `MissionLoopUnitBuilder`) AND the dynamic PER-LOOP hold `W_N` (`ComputePerLoopArrivalHoldSeconds`) that cancels the per-loop rotation drift, plus the descent-icon polyline-ride fix; validated end-to-end on s15 "Duna One." The "design, no code yet" and "FIX DESIGNED, NOT IMPLEMENTED" notes below are SUPERSEDED (kept for design history). STILL DEFERRED (the Phase-4 generalization beyond Duna One, parked pending a real multi-moon playtest): destination parking loiter, 2+ moon destinations, atmo-direct entry, and a non-tidally-locked inner moon's orbital-phase lever.
- Reported in playtest 6 (2026-06-03, s15 "Duna One", Kerbin -> Duna landing): the low circular Duna arrival orbit (director StockConic, inertial epoch+shift) is drawn ~131 deg off the body-fixed landing site, the icon overshoots the landing, then teleports onto the body-fixed descent polyline (a ~180,554 km seam, logged `ReaimSeam`). The descent itself is correctly body-fixed and lands at the true geographic site; the mismatch is between the inertial capture orbit and the rotating-surface landing.
- **Root cause (NOT a render bug, NOT the conic-anchor, NOT inherent):** re-aim pad-aligns the LAUNCH body only (`ReaimWindowPlanner.PadAlignLaunch` snaps the relaunch to whole sidereal days of KERBIN's rotation). Nothing aligns the DESTINATION body's rotation phase across the loop shift (~1.572e9 s for s15), so Duna rotates an arbitrary fraction of a turn under the recorded inertial orbit and the two diverge. The in-SOI arrival/loiter/landing arcs are all recorded RELATIVE to entry, so they replay faithfully relative to their own recorded clock the moment we fix WHEN that clock starts; only the destination rotation phase (and any single inner-moon orbital phase) are misaligned, and both are pure periodic functions of absolute UT.
- **This is the deferred cross-parent twin of an alignment that ALREADY SHIPS for same-parent missions** (Mun/Minmus): the "Landing-body alignment" Off/Loose/Precise control (`MissionPeriodicity` + `SettingsWindowUI`, the `TransitedBodyRotationMode` {Drop/Loose/Tight}). For a cross-parent target `MissionPeriodicity.ExtractConstraints` returns `Support.UnsupportedCrossParent` and does not phase-lock; that is the explicitly-deferred Phase 4. Bug 2 is that unbuilt phase, not a wall.
- **Specified fix (SHIPPED in PR #1030 - see STATUS above; "no code yet" is design history):** a NEW temporal scheduling layer whose controlling variable is the destination-SOI ARRIVAL UT, chosen so the destination's rotation phase (and a single inner moon's orbital phase) recur to their recorded values within a physics-derived tolerance band (reuse the existing `TransitedBodyRotationMode` = Off/Loose/Precise). It is decoupled from the already-correct Kerbin launch by re-aim's per-window transfer regeneration (the flexible SOI-boundary seams absorb the slack), so the Kerbin side is NOT touched. It sits strictly ON TOP of the shipped geometric seam machinery (`ReaimSegmentAssembler.ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` + the per-window Lambert synthesis in `ReaimPlaybackResolver.BuildWindowSegments`) and does not modify it; an infeasible window degrades to faithful via the synthesis-convergence null (`BuildWindowSegments` returns null), not a geometric-residual reject. (`IsSeamResidualTooLarge` is a SEPARATE guard on the body-fixed escape/arrival BURN polyline conic-anchor, NOT the heliocentric capture.) The synodic launch cadence is PRESERVED (every window stays a launch opportunity, ~2 Kerbin years for Duna): alignment is achieved WITHIN each window by the flexible knobs (the continuous loop-clock arrival HOLD that inserts dead time at the heliocentric->capture boundary, the PRE-LANDING TRIM that removes time before the descent, and the destination loiter trim when one was recorded), NEVER by skipping to a rare naturally-aligned window; a window that cannot be aligned FAILS CLOSED to faithful, still on cadence. Nothing new is persisted. The mechanism aligns the DEORBIT (orbit->descent handoff) to the destination's recorded rotation phase. CRITICAL FINDING (s15 "Duna One", verified from the recording + ReaimDiag log): the recording has NO destination parking loiter (in-SOI ~1 Duna rotation: capture hyperbola + sub-1-rev low orbits + descent; the only loiter is the Kerbin-side parking) and only a brief Ike transit that adds no independent constraint (Ike tidally locked). REFUTED (validated against code): the tof-as-phase-lever does NOT align the landing - it only reshapes the heliocentric transfer arc; the recorded in-SOI arcs + the body-fixed descent replay at the loop-clock `spanLoopUT` (`TryComputeSpanLoopUT`), INDEPENDENT of the synthesized tof. The validated mechanism is the loop-clock arrival HOLD (insert dead time at the heliocentric->capture boundary; the INVERSE of a loiter cut) plus the PRE-LANDING TRIM (remove time before the descent), both applied in the shared loop clock so BOTH render paths inherit them. Phase 3a (the pure helpers `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeArrivalAlignHoldSeconds` / `ApplyArrivalHoldToPhase`, 19 tests) is DONE; Phase 3b wires both into `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` + a `LoopUnit` hold field + `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` (gated, off => byte-identical); Phase 3c is the live playtest. Full design + plan: `docs/dev/design-mission-periodicity.md` (Phase 4) and `docs/dev/plans/reaim-destination-arrival-alignment.md`.
- **Discovered defect - the arrival hold is loop-independent (ROOT CAUSE CONFIRMED, FIX SHIPPED in PR #1030 as the dynamic per-loop hold `W_N` = `ComputePerLoopArrivalHoldSeconds`; text below is design history):** the Phase 3b hold aligns ONE reference loop but is CONSTANT across every replayed loop, so a per-loop rotation offset accumulates. Three independent confirmations. CODE: `ArrivalHoldPlanner.ComputeArrivalHold` computes `liveEntryUT = phaseAnchorUT + (CompressSpanUT(recordedArrivalUT, loiterCuts) - spanStartUT)` then `w = GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeArrivalAlignHoldSeconds(recordedArrivalUT, liveEntryUT, T_rot)`, using the FIXED `phaseAnchorUT` with no playback-loop-index (`cycleIndex`) term, so W is constant every loop (measured 46450.59 s, s15). `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` does compute `cycleIndex` internally, but the hold scalar it applies is the same every cycle. MATH: the synodic cadence is 19,653,075.77 s = 299.9652 Duna rotations (`T_rot` = 65,517.86 s), not whole; the 0.0348-rotation shortfall lands the deorbit ~12.5 deg further around the spin each loop, which a loop-independent hold cannot cancel. LOG: `EmitOneSidedBracketDiagnostic` (`Display/GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs`, fields `overshootGap` / `lonBodyFixed` / `lonOrbitSeam` on the one-sided descent leg) read `overshootGap`=17 km (`lonBodyFixed`=84.5) one viewing and 224 km (`lonBodyFixed`=45.8) ~3 loops later; the 38.7 deg `lonBodyFixed` shift = 3.09 loops * 12.5 deg/loop exactly, while `lonOrbitSeam` (the inertial conic) stayed put. CONSEQUENCE: the inertial proto orbit conic and the body-fixed deorbit/descent polyline coincide only on the reference loop and separate progressively on later loops (0 km toward half the circumference) - the "two straight-ish lines instead of an arc" the user sees joining the proto orbit to the landing IS this Bug 2 proto-to-descent disconnect; the geographic landing site stays correct every loop, only the inertial-to-body-fixed JOIN drifts. Rules out sparse-sample chording (sub-pixel) and `TryAnchorLegToConicSeam` (the descent leg is correctly one-sided / body-fixed). DESIGNED FIX (the dynamic per-loop hold): make the hold a function of the loop index N, `W_N = (W_0 - N * (cadence mod T_rot)) mod T_rot` (`cadence` = synodic window period, `T_rot` = destination rotation, `W_0` = current reference hold), so the destination rotation re-aligns at the deorbit on EVERY loop and the conic flows into the body-fixed descent as one connected arc each loop. Free + cadence-preserving (the hold is dead time at the heliocentric->capture boundary that elapses under warp, so 0 to one rotation per loop costs no visible time and does not move the launch schedule); `W_N` stays in `[0, T_rot)` and `compressedSpan + W_N` maxes at `compressedSpan + T_rot`, far below one cadence (the same bound `TryComputeSpanLoopUT`'s clamp already enforces). SEAM: apply in `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` / `ApplyArrivalHoldToPhase` (which already compute `cycleIndex`); carry `W_0`, `cadence`, `T_rot` into the loop unit and compute `W_N` for the current `cycleIndex`; both render paths read the one shared clock and inherit it. REGRESSION FENCE: alignment Off (Drop) => `W_0`=0 => every `W_N`=0, byte-identical; the launch->SOI-entry pipeline is untouched (the hold acts only after SOI entry). RESIDUAL CAVEAT (RESOLVED 2026-06-05 - diagnostic artifact, not a real seam): the ~17 km / 3 deg "residual" seen on the aligned reference loop was a measurement artifact of `EmitOneSidedBracketDiagnostic` itself, NOT a geometric orbit-to-descent gap. The diagnostic evaluated the body-fixed deorbit point at the LIVE planet rotation (`Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()`) while the bracketing conic seam is fixed at `leg.startUT`, so the logged gap inflated purely as Duna spun while the leg stayed the active drawn leg (0 km at the aligned instant, ~8 km a few seconds later). The diagnostic now counter-rotates the body-fixed longitude to `leg.startUT` via the pure `BodyFixedLongitudeAtUT` helper (field renamed `overshootGap` -> `seamGap`, suffixed `@startUT`), so it reads the true ~0 km seam on the aligned loop; the real per-loop drift it still measures is the genuine inter-loop signal the dynamic hold targets. The true geometric seam is ~0 km, so there is no separate boundary-conic-fit / hold-quantization residual to chase. STILL SEPARATE: retiring the transfer proto that orbits past the deorbit (proto-overshoot) and the Ike orbital-phase lever stay deferred. Full writeup: `docs/dev/plans/reaim-destination-arrival-alignment.md` section 13b.
- **Distinct from the prior re-aim "arrival fix":** that work solved the GEOMETRIC seam (connecting the heliocentric transfer to the recorded in-SOI arcs in POSITION space via a boundary-value Lambert capture). Bug 2 is the complementary TEMPORAL / rotation-phase layer (the ~131 deg offset from the destination's un-aligned rotation across the loop shift). Do not conflate them.

### Locked scope (this phase)
- A SINGLE cross-parent destination (direct child of the Sun) with AT MOST ONE moon and a CAPTURED-then-deorbit landing. A 2+ moon destination reports not-supported.
- Atmo-direct (aerocapture / straight into the atmosphere, no captured destination orbit) is OUT of scope this phase: it records no captured destination OrbitSegment and lacks the destination loiter the residual re-timer needs.
- Default tolerance is Loose.
- Validate ORBIT-ONLY arrival alignment FIRST (descent coincidence with the separately deferred S4 descent re-stitch); the on-camera surface descent is validated only after the orbit-only seam is correct.

### Approaches tried / rejected (do NOT repeat - shared with the icon-off-orbit entry above)
- **(REVERTED) Rotate the orbit node by the body rotation over the shift** (per-element LAN rotation, `ApplyLoopShiftLanRotation`): math sound, but rotates only the map OrbitDriver orbit, not the flight-scene ghost MESH, the recorded trajectory POINTS, or the other stages, so the line desyncs from its own ghost and sibling stages render in the wrong place. Any transform must apply to the ENTIRE ghost consistently.
- **(REJECTED) Make the descent inertial:** the descent MUST stay body-fixed to land at the true geographic site. The fix aligns the inertial orbit projection TO the body-fixed descent by choosing when to arrive, never the reverse.
- **(REJECTED, proven dead) Reconstruct positions via the body-fixed -> inertial longitude LIFT** (`GetRelSurfacePosition(lat, lon+initialRotation+recordedUT*360/period, alt)`): 600-1200 km off the recorded conic (pinned by the `Seam-gap PIN` diagnostic). The faithful target is the recorded conic's inertial Kepler elements directly.
- **(REVERTED) Extend the heliocentric transfer's draw window into the SOI:** puts the ghost behind the planet. Handoff must stay at the recorded SOI boundary.
- **(NOT ATTEMPTED, dead-end) Satisfy a single joint resonance of ALL bodies in one launch instant:** for Kerbin -> Duna the exact coincidence is ~1142 Kerbin years away. The tractable model is decoupling-via-flexible-SOI-seams + per-window re-aim regeneration: keep launching every synodic window (cadence preserved) and align EACH on-cadence window's arrival WITHIN the window via the flexible knobs (loiter trim / tof-lever / SOI-entry timing); a window that cannot be aligned fails closed to faithful (the un-aligned render), never skipped. We never wait for a universal all-bodies coincidence.

### Open questions to resolve in design review (carried into the plan)
- **Window frequency vs tolerance:** Mun-tuned thresholds do not transfer to interplanetary cadence. These figures are NAKED (no-knob) recurrence bounds, NOT the launch cadence (which stays synodic): Loose (~910 s for Duna) recurs roughly 1 in 72 synodic windows naked; Precise (~45 s) roughly 1 in 1,440. Within-window alignment is what makes every on-cadence window usable: the CONTINUOUS loop-clock arrival hold reaches any destination rotation phase per window, even with no loiter (with the pre-landing trim as the earlier-direction complement). A window neither knob can align fails closed to faithful (still on cadence), so the no-aligned-window state MUST be a distinct, user-visible message, never a silent fall-through.
- **Geometric-vs-rotation interaction:** the geometric SOI-entry instant from `CalculatePatch` is not identical to the rotation-aligned arrival; whether one chosen window yields BOTH a convergent, sane synthesized capture geometry (the per-window Lambert solve in `BuildWindowSegments`) AND the rotation-phase match, or whether they trade off, must be validated on the real s15 case before declaring Bug 2 fixed.
- **Surface-polyline thread-through:** `ReaimedTrajectory` renders only from OrbitSegments (empty Points/TrackSections); the body-fixed descent polyline is drawn by the separate autonomous `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.Driver` at the live clock. The chosen window's loop shift must reach BOTH paths or they desync exactly as the playtest showed. Validate orbit-only / orbital arrival FIRST; the on-camera descent coincidence depends on the separately deferred S4 descent re-stitch.

- **Status:** OPEN, IN PROGRESS (re-aim Phase 4). Cross-parent destination alignment is still gated behind `MissionPeriodicity` `Support.UnsupportedCrossParent` (no phase-lock in the live path yet). Design seeds `docs/dev/design-mission-periodicity.md` Phase 4 + `docs/dev/plans/reaim-destination-arrival-alignment.md`. The shipped geometric seam machinery (heliocentric leg substitution + per-window Lambert synthesis) is the layer this sits on top of.
  - Implementation Phase 1 DONE: the pure arrival-window solver `Reaim/DestinationArrivalSolver.cs` (`SolveArrivalWindow` / `CountEffectiveConstraints`). It reuses the launch-side zero-drift primitive with the SYNODIC window spacing as the anchor period and the destination constraints (DestRotation + 0/1 MoonConfig) as the others sampled at k*synodic; it is window-index-pure (no resolver/loiter/render/Unity) and unwired. Covered by `DestinationArrivalSolverTests` (9 cases).
  - Implementation Phase 2 DONE: the pure additive selector `Reaim/DestinationConstraintExtractor.cs` (`ExtractDestinationConstraints`) picks the arrival constraint set (DestRotation = target rotation; MoonConfig = SOI-entered moons of the target; the target's own heliocentric orbital excluded; 2+ moons fail closed) out of the EXISTING extraction output. CRITICAL: it does NOT flip `Support` (a cross-parent mission must stay `UnsupportedCrossParent` or `Solve` phase-locks it via the periodicity path and the re-aim render path is skipped); additive + unwired. Covered by `DestinationConstraintExtractorTests` (9 cases). Remaining: P3 injection seam, P4 loiter re-timer, P5 render-path validation (live KSP), P6 tolerance UI.
  - Per-loop drift defect (the arrival hold is loop-independent): the shipped hold aligns one reference loop but is constant across loops, so the inertial-conic-to-body-fixed join drifts about 12.5 deg per loop. The dynamic per-loop hold `W_N = ((W_0 - N*(cadence mod T_rot)) mod T_rot + T_rot) mod T_rot` (gated on `W_0 > 0`) re-aligns every loop. Status: IMPLEMENTED + clean-context Opus review (SHIP) + PLAYTEST-VALIDATED (s15 Duna One, 2026-06-05), folded into PR #1030. Pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputePerLoopArrivalHoldSeconds` + `LoopUnit.DestRotationPeriodSeconds` threaded through the span clock per plan sections 13b/13c, +13 xUnit cases. Playtest confirmed: `WN` stepped per loop (cycleIndex 89/90/91 -> 52999/55281/57563 s, formula-exact to 11 digits), `overshootGap` stayed 0-7 km across both loops (not the pre-fix 224 km after ~3 loops), and the in-SOI chain connected SOI-entry -> Ike -> parking -> deorbit -> descent -> 600 m with the Ike flyby aligned.
  - Done (2026-06-05, surfaced by the per-loop-hold playtest, in PR #1030): the descent ghost ICON was not drawn on its own descent polyline. The descent member (`0b91670...`) has no proto ghost vessel (no PID, no OrbitSegments), and `ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers` gated the marker polyline-ride on `ghostPidForPhase != 0`, so for a PID-less recording `polylinePhase` was forced false and the icon fell back to the body-fixed head, off the line. Fix: for a PID-less recording, resolve polyline ownership by RecordingId via `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.IsRenderingNonOrbitalLeg(recordingId)` (the Driver's per-frame publish) instead of the PID gate; PID recordings stay byte-identical. A small rate-limited `PID-less marker rides its own polyline` log confirms it. NOT a regression from the per-loop hold (which touched only the loop clock): it is the deferred descent-marker-can't-ride-its-own-line issue, only visible once the line rendered correctly.

---

## Done - Missions: looped inter-body launch-window phase-lock (shipped via periodicity + re-aim; residual S4 arrival seam + Moho-class inclined targets deferred, see below)

- **Known limitation shipped in #958 (playtest 2026-05-26, evidence `logs/2026-05-26_2329_mun-mission-map-desync`):** a looped mission that crosses bodies (the Mun-landing "Kerbal X" tree) does not phase-align its replay to the live sky. Member #15 replays its recorded Kerbin transfer ellipse (`sma=6,274,896 ecc=0.873 peri=799 km`) then a recorded Mun approach hyperbola (`sma=-720,778 ecc=1.380 peri=273 km`) with a Kerbin->Mun SOI handoff baked into the recording, but the loop runs at an arbitrary `phaseAnchor` (54042.92 / 5861.38) unrelated to the recorded launch UT (`span start = 3991.76`), and there is ZERO launch-window / re-aim / phase-align logic (grep count 0). The recorded elements are in Kerbin's inertial frame at a fixed orientation and the Mun arc is Mun-relative, so at an arbitrary live UT: (1) Kerbin has rotated, so the orbit periapsis (recorded inertial orientation, once over KSC) no longer sits over the live launch site; (2) the Mun is at a different orbital phase, so the transfer apoapsis points at empty space and the Mun-relative landing arc renders at the Mun's CURRENT location, disconnected from the Kerbin transfer arc. INHERENT to replaying a celestial-phase-dependent trajectory at the wrong time - NOT a regression and NOT caused by the map-presence epoch-shift fix (that only places the ghost at the right phase ALONG its recorded ellipse; it cannot move the live Mun or re-orient the recorded inertial ellipse).
- **Goal:** determine the correct launch UT(s) so the looped replay's map / Tracking Station trajectories line up with the recorded geometry. Faithful launches happen at `UT0 + k*P` (UT0 = recorded launch = span start), where P is the period at which the bodies the mission depends on return to their recorded-launch configuration.
- **Decomposition of P:** (a) launch-body rotation phase (`body.rotationPeriod`, Kerbin sidereal day ~21,549 s) realigns the orbit over the launch site; (b) each transited body's orbital phase (`transitBody.orbit.period`, Mun ~138,984 s) realigns the intercept. Single-body missions: `P = rotation period` (clean, frequent, fully faithful). Inter-body: joint best-fit of (a)+(b) - the periods are incommensurate so it repeats only approximately, at a multiple of the dominant (intercept) period; this is also the physically-real launch-window cadence, which naturally bounds the instance count.
- **Proposed two tiers:** Tier 1 - phase-lock the loop to the dominant intercept period (target body's orbital period), aligned to `UT0`, so the transfer actually reaches the target (fixes the big visual break); quantize the loop cadence to multiples of P and align the phase anchor to `UT0 mod P`. Tier 2 - joint rotation+orbital best-fit so the orbit also sits over the launch site, plus multi-transfer chains (Kerbin->Mun->Minmus, interplanetary).
- **Open decisions (pick before building):** faithful-only mode (cadence always snapped to the launch-window period) vs a per-mission "faithful / free (decorative)" toggle; and for inter-body, accept approximately-faithful (small residual phase error, usable) vs exact-only (rare, very long period). Needs a short design note for the multi-body best-fit math + how to surface a quantized/long cadence in the Missions UI.
- **Relationship to the instance-count question:** the earlier "20 ghosts per render distance instead of per whole mission span" idea is PARKED behind this - faithful inter-body cadence is naturally long (one launch per window), so the instance count stays small without changing the cap. Revisit the render-distance cap (max self-proximity dwell within ~50 km / `LoopSimplifiedMeters`, vs `span/20` in `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeEffectiveLaunchCadence`) only after the phase-lock lands, and only if frequent same-body looping still needs it.
- **Phase 0 (done):** pure constraint extraction. New `Source/Parsek/MissionPeriodicity.cs` (`IBodyInfo` seam + `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo` impl, `ConstraintKind` / `PhaseConstraint` / `Support` / `ConstraintExtraction` types, and `internal static ExtractConstraints`). It reads the trimmed member set (`MissionLoopUnitBuilder.ComputeTrimmedMemberWindows`), classifies each included segment (surface/atmospheric `TrackSection` -> `Rotation(B)`; `bodyName` change across `OrbitSegments` / OrbitalCheckpoint checkpoints -> `Orbital(C)`; bare inertial orbit -> nothing), and flags `UnsupportedCrossParent` (sibling target like Duna) / `UnsupportedRendezvous` (Relative-to-vessel section). No wiring yet (nothing calls it), so zero behavior change. 15 pure tests in `MissionPeriodicityTests.cs` cover every Test-Plan case (single-body orbit -> empty; launch+orbit -> one Rotation; Mun mission -> Rotation+Orbital direct-child; cross-parent Duna -> UnsupportedCrossParent; transient flyby -> Orbital present; checkpoint-bridged backgrounded SOI still surfaces the body change; predicted tail / zero-rotation / retrograde guards; tidal-lock collapse).
- **Q3 over-constraint fix (done):** `ExtractConstraints` previously emitted `Rotation(B)` for ANY included surface/atmospheric segment of B. That over-constrained a config with no inertial orbit of B to hand off to: a pure surface/atmospheric arc is recorded surface-relative and renders at its correct ground location at ANY universe time (it rotates with B), so it imposes NO phase constraint (the design's "no-inertial-arc -> MinCycleDuration" edge case). Fix: `Rotation(B)` is now emitted ONLY when the included set has BOTH a surface/atmospheric segment of B AND an inertial-orbit segment of B (the ascent->orbit / orbit->descent hand-off) - the rotation phase only matters to line a surface segment's hand-off up to an inertial orbit of the same body. The launch body's own orbit segments stay in `earliestOrbitStartByBody` (rule 4 only skips them as SOI ENTRIES), so the hand-off check sees them. Preserved: "launch + Kerbin orbit" still yields `Rotation(Kerbin)`; "atmospheric ascent only" -> empty set -> `P = MinCycleDuration` (free loop); the Mun mission unchanged. Updated design-doc "What determines P" rules 1/2 + the phases-plan vocabulary to say the constraint requires the hand-off (not a bare surface arc). 2 new tests (`Extract_AtmosphericOnly_NoOrbit_NoRotationConstraint` end-to-end through Solve -> MinCycleDuration; `Extract_LaunchPlusOrbit_StillLocksRotation_HandoffRegressionGuard`); updated the retrograde + zero-rotation tests to include the hand-off so they exercise their intended guard.
- **Phase 3 UI (done, built on the Phase-1 Tier-1 solution; NOT Phase 2):** the Missions tab now surfaces the periodicity per looping mission (`MissionsWindowUI`). It computes the solution once per mission per frame in `ComputeMissionPeriodicity` (`ExtractConstraints` + `Solve` over the per-frame cached `view`/`compRoots`, `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings`, the mission's `ExcludedIntervalKeys`, `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance`, and `referenceUT = Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` for the live countdown), suppressing the per-call Verbose lines and emitting one `VerboseRateLimited` summary instead. New "Time to launch" header column placed right after "Missions and vessels" (the name column), before "Start time" (`ColW_TMinus = 90`, folded into `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth`). The live countdown sits on the mission's launch (first) vessel row, under that column header, via `DrawTMinusVesselCell` (every other vessel row + the mission header bar leave a same-width blank cell so the data columns stay aligned); the draw loop computes the periodicity once per mission and passes it to both the header period cell and the launch-row cell. The cell shows the four states via the pure `BuildTMinusCellText`: blank (not looping) / "not aligned" (unsupported no-lock sentinel: cross-parent / rendezvous) / "continuous" (`P == MinCycleDuration`) / "T- <countdown>" (supported), tinted amber when the locked window misses tolerance, and is drawn un-dimmed even when the launch interval is excluded (mission-level data, not a property of that interval). The period cell shows the faithful P + basis label ("~6h (Kerbin rot)" / "~1.6d (Mun window)") as a read-only tinted cell when phase-locked + constrained (via `BuildPeriodCellDisplay` + the dominant constraint from `SelectDominantConstraintIndex`), widened to `ColW_PeriodLocked = ColW_Period + ColW_TMinus + 4` (reclaiming the width freed by moving the countdown off the bar) so "~P (basis)" fits on one line; otherwise the existing editable cadence cell. Pure helpers (`FormatCountdownCompact`, `FormatPeriodCompact`, `BuildPeriodBasisLabel`, `BuildPeriodCellDisplay`, `BuildTMinusCellText`, `ComputeNextRelaunchUT`) are unit-tested (28 tests in `MissionsWindowPeriodicityDisplayTests`, incl. zero/negative/NaN + the four states + Kerbin/Earth day length + the relaunch-schedule cases below); the IMGUI layout is playtest-verified. `MissionsWindowUI.cs` is already on the ERS/ELS allowlist. Phase 2 (joint best-fit) + Phase 4 (synodic) stay deferred; the UI only DISPLAYS the Phase-1 solution.
  - **Flight-map custom-icon loop-clock fix (done):** the flight-scene custom map marker (`ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers` -> `TryComputeGhostWorldPosition`) sampled the ghost trajectory at the LIVE `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()`. For a looped-mission member whose mesh is hidden by zone distance (the launch / atmospheric phase, which has no orbit -> no map ProtoVessel), the recorded points sit at the original (past) UTs, so the live UT is always `OutsideTimeRange` -> `positionFailure` -> the icon never draws (KSP.log showed `candidates>=1 drawn=0 positionFailure=1 missingBody=0` every frame in map view, while the proto-vessel orbit ghosts rendered fine). #958 threaded the span-clock into the proto-vessel path but missed this custom-marker path. Fix: before computing the position, map the live UT to the shared span-clock effUT via `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT(idx, rec.StartUT, rec.EndUT, liveUT, flight.Engine.CurrentLoopUnits, out loopHidden)` (the SAME scene-agnostic resolver the TS / proto-vessel paths use; identity for a non-loop ghost or an Empty unit set, so non-loop behavior is byte-identical) and skip the frame when `loopHidden` (the shared clock has the member outside its window, matching the engine's mesh-hide decision). Surface-relative lat/lon/alt at the live body rotation puts the icon at the correct rotating ground position. New `MapMarkerSummary.LoopHidden` counter distinguishes a loop-clock skip from a position failure; 2 tests (`MapMarkerSummary_IncludesPrioritySkipCounters` extended + `MapMarkerSummary_LoopHiddenAloneHasSignal`). The position mapping reuses the already-tested `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`; in-game-verified.
  - **T- relaunch-cadence fix (done):** the T- countdown originally targeted `solution.NextWindowUT` = the next faithful P-window from now (`UT0 + k*P >= now`). But the loop engine does NOT relaunch at every P-window: `TryBuildMissionUnit` quantizes the cadence to `effectiveOverlapCadence = QuantizeCadenceToMultipleOfP(overlapCadence, P) = m*P` (m can be >= 2 when the recording span or the user period exceeds P), so it relaunches only every m-th window and SKIPS the rest. The old countdown ticked to "T- 0s" on a window with no launch. Fix: `MissionsWindowUI` now rebuilds the REAL `LoopUnitSet` once per frame (cached by `Time.frameCount` in `GetLoopUnitSet`, mirroring `GetMissionView`/`GetCompositionRoots`) via `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build(MissionStore.Missions, CommittedTrees, CommittedRecordings, autoLoopIntervalSeconds, FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance)` (the SAME inputs the scene drivers pass, so the same unit; Verbose summary suppressed), resolves the mission's unit (`TryResolveMissionUnit` maps the mission's trimmed members to committed indices and looks one up via `LoopUnitSet.TryGetUnitForMember`), and the new pure `internal static ComputeNextRelaunchUT(unit, now)` derives the next ACTUAL relaunch = `phaseAnchorUT + n * relaunchCadence` (relaunchCadence = `OverlapCadenceSeconds` when it overlaps the span, else `CadenceSeconds`; `n = max(0, ceil((now - phaseAnchorUT) / relaunchCadence))`). `MissionPeriodicityDisplay` surfaces `NextRelaunchUT` + `UnitBuilt`; `BuildTMinusCellText` takes the relaunch UT + a `unitBuilt` flag (a mission with no engine unit reads "not aligned") instead of `NextWindowUT`. Display-only: the UI's `LoopUnitSet` is never pushed to the engine, so `TryBuildMissionUnit`'s behavior is unchanged. 7 new tests (the `m=2` regression guard proving the countdown targets the 2P relaunch not the skipped P-window, overlap-vs-span cadence selection, parked-before-anchor clamp, exact-boundary no-skip, degenerate-cadence fallback, no-unit-built "not aligned").
- **Phase 1 (done):** single-constraint (Tier-1) phase-lock, wired into the loop builder (gated). New `MissionPeriodicity.Solve(constraints, support, ut0, nowUT, IBodyInfo)` -> `PeriodicitySolution` (P, NextWindowUT, ResidualSeconds, WithinTolerance, Support, ShouldPhaseLock, Method): unsupported -> no-lock sentinel; 0 constraints -> `P = MinCycleDuration`; one Rotation -> rotationPeriod; one direct-child Orbital -> `C.orbit.period`; tidally-locked Rotation+Orbital (equal periods) -> that period; the Mun case (Rotation(Kerbin)+Orbital(Mun), differing periods) -> lock the dominant `Orbital(Mun)` and KNOWINGLY drop+log the Kerbin-rotation residual; any other multi-independent set still locks the dominant intercept and logs the residual (the full joint best-fit is Phase 2). `NextWindowUT` = smallest `UT0 + k*P >= nowUT` (k may be negative for a future-dated UT0); guards `P <= 0` / NaN -> MinCycleDuration. Wired into `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` (new optional `IBodyInfo` arg, default null = no lock = today's behavior): a supported config snaps `phaseAnchorUT = NextWindowUT` (referenced to `LoopAnchorUT`, stable across frames) and quantizes the span + overlap cadence to a multiple of P (above the existing `MinCycleDuration` / overlap-cap floors via `QuantizeCadenceToMultipleOfP`); an unsupported / no-body-info config is byte-identical to the merged #958 looping. `BuildSignature` folds in the looping tree's transited-body set + their live periods (only when `IBodyInfo` is supplied) so a body-geometry change rebuilds. The three scene drivers (`ParsekFlight` / `ParsekTrackingStation` / `ParsekKSC`) pass `FlightGlobalsBodyInfo.Instance`. `Info`-on-build logs `PhaseLock APPLIED` (old->new anchor + window) / `PhaseLock SKIPPED` (unsupported reason); `Warn` when the Tier-1 residual exceeds tolerance. 21 new tests (solver Tier-1 cases + next-window k incl. future-dated UT0 + tidal collapse + over-constrained + tolerance boundary; builder snaps a supported single-body / same-parent config + leaves an unsupported one at the raw anchor + byte-identical no-body-info path; signature rebuild on body-geometry change; phase-lock applied/skipped/over-constrained log assertions). Affects ONLY looping Missions; cross-parent stays `UnsupportedCrossParent` (gated to today's behavior until Phase 4).
- **Phase 2 (done): joint best-fit over whole multiples of the dominant period.** Playtest showed the Tier-1 Mun loop locked the Mun intercept but dropped the Kerbin-rotation residual WHOLESALE (~9688s / ~161deg of launch-pad misalignment), so the launch did not line up with the pad. `MissionPeriodicity.Solve` now, for an incommensurate multi-constraint config, searches whole multiples `m` in `[1, MaxJointMultiples=16]` of the dominant constraint's period (so the dominant body stays locked at every relaunch) and picks the `m` that MINIMIZES the worst dropped-constraint circular phase error over one cadence step (`m*P`), preferring the smallest `m` on a tie (`JointResidualTieEpsilonSeconds`) so the relaunch period stays as short as the alignment allows. New pure helpers `FindBestJointMultiple` + `JointStepResidual` (both `internal static`, unit-tested). `P = m*dominantPeriod`; `ResidualSeconds` = the per-cycle drift at `m` (the fixed cadence still drifts on incommensurate periods - see the zero-drift task below); `WithinTolerance` compares it to the physics tolerance; `Method = "joint-best-fit"` when `m>1`, else `"dominant-intercept"`. For the stock Kerbin-rotation (21549.425s) + Mun-orbit (138984.38s) case the best multiple is `m=9` (~14.5 days): pad residual `9688s/161deg -> ~993s/16deg` (~10x better; still amber, a fixed cadence can't hit the quarter-degree tolerance). Single-constraint + tidal-lock configs are unchanged (`m=1`, residual 0). 3 broken Tier-1 tests updated (Mun case, over-constrained two-rotations, builder same-parent snap) + 3 new (`FindBestJointMultiple` exact-resonance / stays-at-one, `JointStepResidual` worst-dropped). `MaxJointMultiples` is a documented, easy-to-tune constant.
- **Phase 2.5: zero-drift per-window reschedule (DONE; the accurate-for-supply-routes follow-up).** The current best-fit uses a FIXED cadence (`m*dominantPeriod`), which cannot hold incommensurate periods aligned forever: each successive relaunch's dropped-constraint (launch-pad) error grows by the per-cycle residual (e.g. ~993s/cycle for the Mun case). For supply-route-grade accuracy the loop instead re-solves each relaunch INDEPENDENTLY to the true next joint near-coincidence after the previous launch, so the pad error stays BOUNDED (~one residual) instead of accumulating. Plan: `docs/dev/done/plans/zero-drift-reschedule.md` (math, schedule representation, gating, phasing). Key insight (plan §2.1): the per-constraint phase offsets cancel, so a launch `L = UT0 + k*dominantPeriod` satisfies constraint i iff `CircularPhaseError(k*dominantPeriod, period_i) <= tol_i` - an ABSOLUTE function of k, so picking good k never accumulates. Only multi-constraint incommensurate ("drifting") configs get a schedule; single/tidal/unconstrained/unsupported keep the existing fixed cadence (byte-identical). Scheduled units are gated non-overlapping so the overlap engine path is untouched.
  - **Phase A (done): pure solver.** New in `MissionPeriodicity.cs`: `NextJointNearCoincidenceUT` / `TryFindNextScheduleK` (lock the dominant exactly; smallest within-tolerance k in `ScheduleLookaheadMultiples=4096`, else bounded-best min-residual k - never accumulating), `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` (gates on >=2 distinct-period constraints; filters degenerate dropped periods with a Warn; returns null for single/tidal/unsupported), and the immutable `MissionRelaunchSchedule` class (snapshotted inputs + lazily-extended launch-UT cache + `TryResolveActiveLaunch` / `NextLaunchAfter` + `MinIntervalSeconds` for the overlap gate + `MaxScheduleSteps=8192` CPU safety cap). `GhostPlaybackLogic.LoopUnit` gains a nullable `RelaunchSchedule` field + a null-chaining constructor overload (no consumers yet, byte-identical for every existing config). 22 pure tests in `MissionZeroDriftScheduleTests.cs` (the hand-checkable synthetic 100/31 case incl. the non-uniform within-tol sequence 9/13/18/22 and intervals 400/500/400; the stock Mun case proving non-accumulation vs fixed cadence; tolerance boundary; multi-dropped worst=max; bounded-best fallback; degenerate/NaN/floor/future-dated guards; the safety cap parks + Warns + `NextLaunchAfter` NaN; monotonic resolution). No behavior change in game (nothing attaches a schedule until Phase B wires the builder). Math core reviewed clean-context.
  - **Phase B (done): builder wiring + span-clock consumption.** `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` now, for a phase-locked DRIFTING config (>=2 distinct-period constraints, the Mun/Minmus case), calls `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` and, when the schedule is non-overlapping (`MinIntervalSeconds >= span`, the INVARIANT keeping the overlap engine path off scheduled units), attaches it to the `LoopUnit`: `phaseAnchorUT = schedule.FirstLaunchUT` (a within-tolerance window >= the first-play floor) and `CadenceSeconds = OverlapCadenceSeconds = max(span, MinIntervalSeconds)`. A would-overlap schedule is rejected (fixed cadence kept, logged `zeroDrift=rejected-would-overlap`). Single/tidal/unconstrained/unsupported configs get no schedule and are byte-identical to the prior fixed cadence. `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryComputeSpanLoopUT` + `DecideUnitMemberRender` take an optional `MissionRelaunchSchedule` (null = the existing uniform path, byte-identical): when present they resolve the active launch from the schedule (largest scheduled launch <= currentUT), measure the in-span phase from it, and park in the inter-cycle tail between launches (render nothing). Threaded through all consumers: the flight engine single-instance branch + the loop-synced-debris parent-span branch (passes `parentUnit.RelaunchSchedule` so debris rides its scheduled parent), `ParsekKSC`, and `ParsekTrackingStation` via `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` (+ the flight-map custom marker / `GhostMapPresence` through the same resolver). The Mun config is now scheduled (the prior fixed m=9 ~14.5d cadence is gone for it); the two Phase-2 builder tests that encoded that contract were updated. Review fixes folded in: (a) the loop-synced-debris parent-span branch now CONSUMES `isInInterCycleTail` (routes it through `parentPaused`) so ride-along debris whose end is at/after the parent span end is hidden in the inter-launch gap instead of rendering a frozen stale ghost at the clamped spanEnd (a latent bug for any unit with `CadenceSeconds > span`, now reachable on every scheduled gap); (b) `BuildSignature`/`AppendTransitedBodyDigest` now folds `SoiRadius` + `OrbitalVelocity` (which feed the orbital tolerance, hence the within-tolerance windows) so a planet-pack SOI change re-derives the schedule; (c) `MinIntervalProbeLaunches` bumped to 8 (the non-overlap invariant itself is unconditional: `OverlapCadenceSeconds = max(span, MinInterval) >= span` regardless). New tests: builder attaches a schedule for the Mun config + non-overlap invariant, no schedule for single-constraint, would-overlap rejection; scheduled span-clock parked/render/tail + null-schedule byte-identical (incl. the reordered span<=0 guard) + `DecideUnitMemberRender` decisions + the `UnitMemberOverlaps==false` invariant; plus an in-game test (`TrackingStationSpanClock_ZeroDriftSchedule_ResolvesScheduledLaunch`) exercising the scheduled span clock through the live TS/map seam. The loop-synced-debris-rides-scheduled-parent path (engine:1820) is covered by the pure tail-flag test (`SpanClock_Scheduled_...ParksInTailBetweenLaunches`) plus the existing, in-game-verified `parentPaused` hide machinery the fix routes through (no dedicated in-game debris scenario, which would need a contrived live recording + the private debris path; the wiring + the tail flag it depends on are both verified). Full suite green (12697). Integration reviewed clean-context.
  - **Phase C + D (done): UI + hardening.** `MissionsWindowUI.ComputeNextRelaunchUT` now branches on `unit.RelaunchSchedule`: a scheduled unit's TTL countdown + "Warp to..." target both resolve to `schedule.NextLaunchAfter(now)` (the next NON-UNIFORM scheduled launch), not `phaseAnchor + n*cadence`. The Missions period cell shows a "varies" label for a scheduled (non-uniform) unit via the new pure `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` (e.g. "~3d (Mun window, varies)" at the max cadence, longer when the player throttles) off the schedule's `MinIntervalSeconds`, instead of the stale fixed `Solution.P`. The three scene drivers (flight/KSC/TS) were already correct after Phase B (they share the schedule-aware `DecideUnitMemberRender` / `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`). Hardening: caching is signature-based for the scene drivers (the schedule object persists + lazily extends across frames; the signature folds the body geometry incl. SOI/velocity) and per-frame for the UI display mirror (acceptable: each search breaks early at the first within-tol k); persistence is structural (nothing new serialized, the schedule re-derives from the already-persisted inputs); overlap is invariant-gated. New tests: scheduled `ComputeNextRelaunchUT` targets the next scheduled launch, `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` "varies" strings, and a determinism guard (two independently-built schedules resolve identically, underpinning both "UI cannot diverge from playback" and "re-derives identically after reload"). Full suite green (12700).
  - **Model revision (anchor on the tightest constraint + player throttle; done):** the first cut anchored on the DOMINANT = longest-period constraint (the Mun) and required the rest within tolerance, which pinned the body with the GENEROUS (SOI-width) tolerance to zero error while demanding the TIGHT one (the pad) line up too: for the stock Mun the first faithful window was ~803 Mun periods (~3.5 years) - unusable. The s15 Mun-mission segment review (frame boundaries: the Mun-relative approach/landing block self-anchors to the live Mun, so the Mun only needs to be within its SOI-width tolerance at the SOI seam, NOT pixel-exact) showed the Mun should not be pinned. Reworked: `SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` now picks the constraint with the SMALLEST duty cycle (tolerance/period) - the launch-pad rotation, not the Mun - and `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` anchors on it (`SelectDominantConstraintIndex` stays only for the fixed-cadence `Solve` fallback). This MAXIMIZES window frequency (rate ~ anchorPeriod / product(other duty cycles), so you pin the tightest to keep it out of the product): the stock Mun max cadence drops from ~3.5 years to ~3.25 Earth days (first faithful pad-anchored window j=13), and the launch lands PIXEL-PERFECT over the pad with the Mun within ~0.5 SOI. Added a player THROTTLE (`minSpacing`, the builder passes the requested relaunch period; Auto = every faithful window = max cadence; an explicit period skips faithful windows to launch less often) so the player picks a lower cadence for supply routes. `MissionRelaunchSchedule` renamed `dominantPeriod`->`anchorPeriod` / `dropped*`->`other*`, added the `minSpacing` throttle in `ExtendOnce`. Updated the two Mun builder tests (pad anchored exactly, Mun within SOI tol, ~13-pad-rotation first window) + new tests (`SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` picks the pad; throttle skips windows; max-cadence no-throttle). Plan + CHANGELOG updated (windows now recur every few days, not rare). Full suite green (12703). Future option (not implemented): re-chain the Mun-relative block to the actual SOI crossing to erase the boundary seam and loosen the Mun tolerance further - a playback-engine change.
  - **External-review follow-ups (done):** (S1) the overlap-reject gate previously trusted `MinIntervalSeconds` (only an 8-launch probe) and could wrongly pass if the true min gap occurred later. Fixed by FLOORING the throttle at the span (`minSpacing = cadence`, already `>= span`): the schedule places consecutive launches `>= minSpacing >= span` apart, so every interval is `>= span` and the unit is non-overlapping BY CONSTRUCTION, independent of the probe. The realistic faithful gap (days) is `>> span` so the floor only bites a pathological short-gap config (merging it to one-at-a-time playback); the defensive `MinIntervalSeconds >= span` gate is kept but now always passes (the would-overlap reject path is unreachable). `Build_DriftingButSpanExceedsInterval` retargeted to assert the schedule is attached + non-overlapping. (S2) `MissionRelaunchSchedule.NextLaunchAfter` (called every UI frame) was an O(cacheSize) linear scan; switched to a binary search like `TryResolveActiveLaunch`. (N1) corrected the `ScheduleLookaheadMultiples` comment to the anchor-on-pad model (k counts pad rotations; ~13 for launch+orbit-to-Mun, ~700 when a tidally-locked landing adds a tight Rotation(body) constraint). (N2) clarifying comment on `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay` (the interval is pad-anchored; the basis label names the dominant celestial event the window targets). Full suite green (12703).
  - **Landing-body rotation A/B flag (done; was: stock s15 Mun period ~1.65 Kerbin years).** Cause confirmed from KSP.log: the s15 "Kerbal X" mission is a land-AND-return, so the extractor emits THREE constraints - `Rotation(Kerbin)` (pad, tol ~15s), `Orbital(Mun)` (intercept, SOI tol ~4480s), AND `Rotation(Mun)` (the Mun LANDING; tidally locked so period = Mun orbit, but carrying the tight 0.25deg launch-pad tolerance ~96s). Anchored on the pad, finding a window where the Mun ROTATION is also within 0.25deg is rare (`minInterval=15149245s`). The Mun landing is body-fixed (self-anchors to the Mun surface, like the KSC ascent), so it does not need the tight pad tolerance - its phase is already pinned within the SOI by `Orbital(Mun)`. Implemented BOTH options behind a player A/B flag (`ParsekSettings.transitedBodyRotationModeIndex` -> `TransitedBodyRotationMode` Drop/Loose/Tight; default **Loose**; Settings > Looping "Landing-body alignment" cycle button): **Drop** excludes a transited (non-launch) body's `Rotation(body)` constraint -> the SOI tolerance governs -> ~15 Kerbin days (largest handoff seam); **Loose** keeps it at `TransitedBodyLooseRotationDegrees=5deg` -> ~1-2 Kerbin months (small seam); **Tight** keeps the 0.25deg (~1.65 Kerbin years, pixel-perfect handoff). The launch-body (pad) rotation is NEVER dropped/loosened. `MissionPeriodicity.SelectAnchorConstraintIndex` / `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` take `launchBodyName` + the mode (Drop pre-filters, Loose loosens via new `ScheduleToleranceSecondsFor`; new `IsTransitedBodyRotation` helper); `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build`/`TryBuildMissionUnit`/`BuildSignature` thread the mode (folded into the signature so a flipped flag rebuilds); the four scene/UI drivers pass `ParsekSettings.Current.TransitedBodyRotationMode`. Setting persists via stock GameParameters (public int field). New tests: the 3-mode first-window ordering (Drop<Loose<Tight), `ScheduleToleranceSecondsFor`/`IsTransitedBodyRotation`, and the Settings label/cycle helpers. Full suite green (12707).
  - **Separate (not a zero-drift regression): tracking-station 1-2s render delay.** Confirmed from KSP.log (TS: `destroy reason=gap-between-orbit-segments` at 00:33:44.860 -> next `create-dispatch` at 00:33:46.865 = ~2.0 real seconds). When a looped-mission replay crosses a GAP between two recorded orbit segments (here a ~62 game-second coast between the parking orbit [4181-4779] and the next orbit [4841-5727]), `GhostMapPresence` destroys the TS proto-vessel and recreates it at the next segment; at low warp the game-second gap is ~2 real seconds of nothing. Flight-map hides this via the custom span-clock marker that bridges the gap; the TS relies solely on the proto-vessel. Orthogonal to zero-drift (it depends on the recorded segment structure, not the launch schedule). **Subsumed (fix shared with the SOI/segment-flicker item below):** the same-body intra-block carry now keeps the TS proto-vessel alive across the gap too, so this 1-2s gap should be gone in practice. Confirm in the next TS playtest.
  - **SOI/segment flicker in flight map + TS (playtest 2026-05-28, `logs/2026-05-28_1826_soi-trajectory-flicker`, fixed):** approaching/inside Mun SOI the looped Mun-mission ghost's orbit line + icon flashed on/off across consecutive Mun-frame OrbitSegments (capture-burn, descent, return-burn transitions). Confirmed from KSP.log: pid=2775631560 cycled `reason=visible-segment lineActive=True` -> `reason=past-segment-end lineActive=False` -> `visible-segment` with new bounds every 1-3 real seconds for the whole Mun phase. Two coupled causes: (1) `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` (rate-limited 2a path) called `TrajectoryMath.FindOrbitSegmentForMapDisplay` which only carries across a gap when the surrounding segments are ORBIT-EQUIVALENT (same sma/ecc/inc/etc.); a brief Mun-frame intra-block gap between two DIFFERENT Mun orbits (capture burn) returned null -> destroyed the ProtoVessel + re-queued to pending -> recreated next tick. (2) `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` toggled `line.active=false` the moment currentUT walked past the current segment's endUT, before the segment selector picked the next segment (~one frame, ~300-500ms wall-clock at low warp), making the line blink even when the ghost survived. **Fix:** introduced same-body carry that intentionally does NOT require orbit equivalence. New pure helpers `TrajectoryMath.FindOrbitSegmentOrSameBodyCarry` (the previous segment carries across any same-body gap) and `TryGetBodyFrameBoundsForMapDisplay` (the bounds of the run of consecutive same-body segments around the playback head). `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels` 2a + `GhostMapPresence.UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle` (`coveringSegment` resolver) + `GetTrackingStationGhostRemovalReason` switched to the new carry, so the ghost is no longer torn down in same-body intra-block gaps. `UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording` now also caches body-frame bounds (loop-shifted by the same offset applied to `ghostOrbitBounds`) in a new `ghostBodyFrameOrbitBounds` dict; `TryGetBodyFrameOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel` reads it and `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` uses these wider bounds for the `line.active` decision while `GhostOrbitArcPatch` + `GhostOrbitIconClampPatch` keep using the per-segment bounds for arc clipping + icon clamping. New reasons: `visible-body-frame`, `past-body-frame-end`, `before-body-frame-start`. Result per the user spec: inside a body frame the orbit line stays continuously on (the arc shape itself still redraws per segment as the orbit driver retargets at each transition); only the actual SOI / body change blanks the line, and the ghost icon jumps from the end of its transfer arc to its correct-at-currentUT point in the destination-body trajectory. 9 new tests (active/gap-carry/body-change/past-last for `FindOrbitSegmentOrSameBodyCarry`, run-expansion/same-body-gap/body-change-gap/past-last/before-first for `TryGetBodyFrameBoundsForMapDisplay`). Full suite green (12716).
  - **Follow-up (playtest 2026-05-28, `logs/2026-05-28_1923_ts-rendering-after-alignment`, fixed): orbit-line blackout at TS entry + at flight-create for any loop-shifted ghost.** Confirmed from KSP.log: in TS, pid=3876519787 (Kerbal X #15) entered TS at 19:20:02.067 with `Cached body-frame bounds ... loopShift=0.00` (raw recorded UTs 4181-20094), `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix` then fired `reason=past-body-frame-end lineActive=False bounds=[4181.1,20094.2] currentUT=35864231.1` (35M-second mismatch), and the cache refresh with the correct `loopShift=35858243.50` only landed at 19:20:04.071 — exactly the 2.0s `LifecycleCheckIntervalSec` later. Same shape in flight at 19:19:03 (~0.4s blackout, gated by the smaller `MapOrbitUpdateIntervalSec=0.5s`). Root cause: both `GhostMapPresence.CreateGhostVesselFromSource` callers (the TS lifecycle's CREATE pass and `ParsekPlaybackPolicy.CheckPendingMapVessels`'s deferred-create pass) computed the loop epoch shift and passed `effUT` for source-resolve / logging, but `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` -> `UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording` always ran with the default `loopEpochShiftSeconds = 0.0` — so the very first `ghostOrbitBounds` + `ghostBodyFrameOrbitBounds` entries held raw recorded UTs until the next rate-limited refresh re-applied them with the correct shift. **Fix:** threaded an optional `loopEpochShiftSeconds` parameter through both `CreateGhostVesselFromSource` overloads (default 0 for byte-identical non-loop behavior) into the Segment + EndpointTail dispatches, then updated the two loop-aware callers to pass it (`UpdateTrackingStationGhostLifecycle` passes `tsLoopEpochShift = currentUT - effUT`; `CheckPendingMapVessels` passes `pendingLoopEpochShift = currentUT - toCreate[i].effUT`). The startup path (`CreateGhostVesselsFromCommittedRecordings`) keeps shift=0 (it is not loop-aware) because its ghosts are removed and recreated by the next lifecycle tick anyway. Full suite green (12716); playtest pending.

  - **Prior-art note (cloned mods, `Code/Parsek/mods/`):** verified in-game 2026-05-27 (`PhaseLock APPLIED method=joint-best-fit P=1250859 (=9 Mun periods) residual=992.7s`, map icon `drawn>=1` in-window, zero `positionFailure` all run). Conclusion: no cloned mod implements the multi-period near-coincidence we need; the zero-drift follow-up is a self-contained numerical method (continued-fraction / Stern-Brocot best-rational-approximation of the constraint period ratios).
